![[Welcome.jpg]]
# Two minutes till midnight in Wisconsin...
The chill of the evening clings to the air outside. You sit alone in your dorm room, staring at the clock radio resting atop your nightstand. The green digits on your wristwatch agree with the red digits on the clock; 11:58 PM – two minutes ‘til midnight. You pull your headphones off, set your Walkman on the desk, head over to your small bed and tune into the campus radio station on the cheap alarm clock. Light classical music can be heard fading out as the DJ talks about the next piece she's putting on the turntable.
11:59 PM
A minute later the radio crackles with static and an electrical buzz. Your small room is filled with an eerie hum that seems to vibrate through your very bones. You've heard rumors of this happening before – a mysterious pirate radio station taking over the campus airwaves at precisely midnight. You've tried to catch the show before but without success. Seems tonight you got lucky.
"Let there be METAL!"
The sound of distorted guitars can be heard through the static. A disturbed metal tune, with a happy beat, begins to play.
What have you found?
After a few minutes the song ends and the host returns.
"[[Dave|Dave]] Is Back Babies! ‘Metal at Midnight’ is live and we’ve got all the music and news you need to survive this [[Watashuka|messed up little town]]. And speaking of news, we’ve got some real juicy nuggets for all you little pink faced freshmen joining our church of METAL for the first time. And believe me, its news that THEY do NOT want you to know."
He pauses only a moment to catch his breath.
"We’re going live tonight because I know some of you little metal headed sideshow freaks have got class in that torture chamber known as [[01-Campus Directory| Sister Sarah’s]]. And believe me, they are trying super hard to keep this quiet. So Dave’s going all School House Rock tonight. Knowledge is power! And power is what they don’t want you to have."
The static hangs in the air as Dave goes quiet. Is that ... screams in the static? You lean in closer, your heart pounding in your chest as the static is broken by [[Dave|Dave's]] whispered voice.
"Yeah, that hospital’s all clean and bleachy fresh outside but in the back rooms … Oh brother, it’s Mike Myers meets that freaky little alien chest baby. Us vets know it. We've heard the screams. We've seen shadows moving all weird. We've seen dumpsters getting collected late at night. Ain't no trashman working after midnight! Yeah, Sarah’s stinks alright so watch your back there. "
You glance out your window, out across the campus, towards the hospital – or rather, what you can see of it through the dense trees. The lights seem too bright tonight, casting long, dancing shadows that seem to twist and writhe unnaturally. You swear you can hear the sound of a large truck operating.
"Worst yet, THEY know it’s there! And Dave’s got the cancelled checks to prove it; right where you’d expect. In that nasty, creepy museum all the norms pass every day on their way to class. Prairie Hall is just a 24/7, 365, all you can eat charnel house with a receptionist. But they do keep records there…."
"Call Mr. King, I've got a pitch for his next book!"
The radio crackles again, and you swear you hear something else – a whispering beneath Dave's words, a dark alien presence pushing through the static. Music breaks through the small speaker again. For the next several hours metal music flows from the pirate station. Just before dawn the music stops and Dave cuts in again. You were dozing but the odd interference and the mad host's words stir you awake.
"Damn, they found me so it’s time to wrap. But before I bounce remember…"
"We’ll fight on the land,"
"We’ll fight in the fields and in the streets,"
"We’ll fight in the hills,"
"We’ll never surrender."
"Man, someone call in the metal MILITIA!"
The radio begins blaring the last song of the show. The pirate station has cranked up the volume to an almost unbearable level as heavy power chords and frantic riffs cut through the airwaves. You jump back, heart racing. As the song plays you can hear the sound of equipment being thrown into boxes. Over the din, you think you can hear Dave singing along. After a few moments, the radio station fades back into quiet static, leaving you alone with your thoughts – and the chilling echoes of Dave's words. You barely notice when the campus radio comes back on the air. Looking back out the window you can see the start of the morning's false dawn.
The night DJ has been replaced by the morning show. Soft Americana music soothes the ringing in your ears as you listen to a sorrowful woman sing over an old guitar.
_In shadows deep where whispers stir_
_A pact is forged_
_silence unheard_
_My heart I give to the darkened sky_
_To save the fields_
_to let hope fly_
_Oh hear my call_
_oh ancient dread_
![](https://youtu.be/enBlR2tbyg4?si=b0JgDD_kCrg7KTkc)
## Welcome to Wisconsin.
Welcome to a world where truth hides behind conspiracy theories and history. A world where darkness lurks in the unlikeliest of places. A world where friend and foe are difficult to distinguish from one another.
Class is in session and a new semester begins tonight. Are you ready to confront the truths hidden within the hallowed halls of [[Caroline College]]?
Disclaimers:
- *This game makes creative use of organizations that exist in real life. This game is set in an alternate history and the inclusion of these peoples, the Ho-Chunk, the Amish and the Lutherans, are here for verisimilitude. I have learned much about these peoples during the creation of this setting and have nothing but respect for their culture. I have taken efforts to avoid working in their unique mythologies into this game. I am not versed enough in these histories to do justice to such an endeavor. Any facsimile to real people, real events or histories is purely coincide.* 
- *This document makes use of large language models to accomplish initial drafts or art that I am not qualified, or able, to produce. Everything goes through a human multiple times but if this is a topic that you have strong opinions on, please consider avoiding this work.*

# Summary of Literary Conceits
- **The Small Town with Dark Secrets**
	- **Conceit:** Watashuka appears to be a quaint, struggling small town in rural America—a perfect representation of quiet country life with local institutions like a Lutheran church, a college, and family-owned businesses. Beneath this peaceful façade, however, lies a hidden history of occultism, supernatural occurrences, and government conspiracies.
	- **Effect:** This conceit lures players into a familiar and nostalgic setting, only to slowly reveal its dark underbelly. The contrast between the idyllic rural setting and the creeping horror creates suspense and tension.
	- **Summary:** The familiar Americana setting contrasts with hidden cosmic horror.
- **The Time Loop**
	- **Conceit:** The entire game world is trapped in a time loop spanning 1983 to 1987, caused by a government experiment gone wrong. The loop resets every few years, with only subtle changes each time, while eldritch beings seem to exist outside of or partially immune to its effects.
	- **Effect:** The time loop gives the setting a feeling of repetition and inevitability, as the same strange occurrences and tragedies happen over and over again. It mirrors themes of **cosmic futility** and **existential horror** in the works of authors like **H.P. Lovecraft**, where humans are trapped by forces far beyond their control. For players, it introduces a puzzle-like challenge of breaking the loop to escape the repeating cycles of horror.
	- **Summary:** The repetition of events mirrors themes of cosmic futility and existential dread.
- **The "Satanic Panic" Twist**
	- **Conceit:** The 1980s fear surrounding heavy metal music and role-playing games (the "Satanic Panic") is flipped on its head. In the world of Watashuka, the very groups accused of promoting devil worship (metalheads, conspiracy theorists, gamers) are actually trying to **fight the supernatural forces** and protect the town from eldritch horrors.
	- **Effect:** This subverts the expectations of both the characters and the players, who might expect these groups to be involved with the occult. Instead, these so-called "outcasts" serve as unlikely heroes. This twist also plays into themes of **paranoia** and **misdirection**, where societal fears are focused on the wrong targets.
	- **Summary:** Metalheads and gamers are actually fighting the real occult forces, subverting 1980s fears.
- **The Conspiracy Theorist Who is Sometimes Right**
	- **Conceit:** Dave, the pirate radio host of "Metal At Midnight," serves as a wild, paranoid conspiracy theorist whose broadcasts often sound absurd. However, he occasionally stumbles onto real truths about the town’s supernatural history and ongoing conspiracies.
	- **Effect:** Dave embodies the trope of the unreliable narrator, forcing players to sift through his ramblings to find kernels of truth. His role introduces a **meta-narrative** where players must decide how much of his information to believe, knowing that even a broken clock is right twice a day.
	- **Summary:** Dave’s unreliable narration adds humor and paranoia, with glimpses of truth.
- **The Hidden Power Struggle**
	- **Conceit:** Watashuka is home to multiple factions vying for control, including cults, the government’s secret **Project Caroline**, and the Amish guardians protecting the world from supernatural forces. Each group operates in secrecy, and their true intentions are often misunderstood by the townspeople.
	- **Effect:** This creates a **layered narrative** where players are gradually drawn into a complex web of alliances, rivalries, and betrayals. The power struggle adds intrigue to the setting, with each faction hiding behind different facades (religious institutions, academic programs, local law enforcement), feeding the game’s themes of deception and the hidden truth.
	- **Summary:** Multiple factions work in secret, creating a web of deception and alliances. 
- **The Mundane Masking the Supernatural**
	- **Conceit:** Ordinary settings and objects (a biology lab, a local museum, a small-town grocery store) are used as fronts for supernatural activity and occult rituals. The familiar becomes the unfamiliar as seemingly benign places turn into sites of cosmic horror.
	- **Effect:** This literary conceit plays with the **uncanny**, creating unease by blurring the line between the mundane and the supernatural. It heightens the sense of paranoia, as players must question every normal-seeming place or person, wondering if they are tied to the dark forces manipulating the town.
	- **Summary:** Ordinary places hide eldritch rituals, blurring the line between normal and uncanny.
- **The Tension Between Religion and the Occult**
	- **Conceit:** The town’s deeply Lutheran identity is contrasted with the dark undercurrents of occult activity. The Lutheran Church is unaware of the true supernatural threats, mistakenly believing external devil worshipers are the issue while the real danger comes from cultists embedded in their own institutions.
	- **Effect:** This religious dynamic deepens the theme of **blindness to hidden dangers**. The church's misunderstanding of the threat reflects how human institutions often fail to perceive or address the true nature of evil. It also taps into the **Lovecraftian theme** of cosmic forces beyond human understanding.
	- **Summary:** The Lutheran Church misidentifies the true threat, reflecting human blindness to cosmic horror.
- **Cosmic Horror in a Small Scale**
	- **Conceit:** While the stakes involve cosmic entities and eldritch horrors, the setting focuses on small, personal stories—disappearances, strange rituals in biology labs, and eerie occurrences at a local hospital. The vastness of the threat is made more terrifying by how it plays out in an intimate, insular community.
	- **Effect:** This brings cosmic horror down to a human scale, creating a sense of helplessness as ordinary people confront unfathomable powers. The tension lies in how the town's residents unknowingly live alongside these horrors, oblivious to the full scope of what’s happening around them.
	- **Summary:** Vast cosmic threats play out in an intimate, personal setting, increasing the sense of helplessness.
- **Misinformation and Red Herrings**
	- **Conceit:** The story deliberately uses misinformation, false leads, and red herrings to mislead players and characters alike. **Amy Mann’s disappearance**, for example, serves as a red herring, diverting attention from the larger ritualistic threat posed by the cults.
	- **Effect:** This conceit adds a **puzzle-like quality** to the narrative, where players must navigate false clues and layered mysteries. The use of misinformation creates an atmosphere of distrust and confusion, contributing to the theme of **hidden truths and conspiracies**.
	- **Summary:** Red herrings and false leads create an atmosphere of paranoia and mystery.
- **The Inescapable Past**
	- **Conceit:** The region’s dark history, going back to the destruction of **Prairieville Academy**, continues to shape the present. The original rituals and occult influence haunt Watashuka, affecting every generation since.
	- **Effect:** This taps into the idea that **the past is never truly gone**, and that the evil deeds of one generation can ripple through time, affecting those who come after. The repeated cycles of the time loop reinforce this idea, symbolizing the town’s inability to escape its cursed history.
	- **Summary:** The town’s dark history continues to affect the present, symbolized by the time loop and recurring horrors.

# An Early 1980's College Setting For Call of Cthulhu Campaign
---
## Disclaimer
**This is a game of horror. Some themes may be disturbing to some players. Players are required to engage with the Session Zero to ensure that the game is appropriate for themselves, all players, and the keeper at the table.**
*Please note: this game makes creative use of organizations that exist in real life. This game is set in an alternate history and the inclusion of these peoples, the Ho-Chunk, the Amish and the Lutherans, are here for verisimilitude. I have learned much about these peoples during the creation of this setting and have nothing but respect for their culture. I have taken efforts to avoid working in their unique mythologies into this game. I am not versed enough in these histories to do justice to such an endeavor. Any facsimile to real people, real events or histories is purely coincide.* 
---
[[02-Session Zero Guidelines|Session Zero Guidelines]] for details about session zero planning can be found here.
---
## Character Creation
### Determining Character Stats
#### Rolling and Distributing Characteristics
For **Caroline College**, we use a variant of for determining characteristics.
1. **Roll 9 sets of (3d4+2)** and assign one of the nine sets to each of the following:    
    - Strength (**STR**)
    - Constitution (**CON**)
    - Dexterity (**DEX**)
    - Appearance (**APP**)
    - Power (**POW**)
    - Luck (**LUCK**)   
    - Size (**SIZ**)
    - Intelligence (**INT**)
    - Education (**EDU**)
Following standard Call of Cthulhu procedure, each value will be multiplied by 5 to determine the characteristic's value. 1/2 and 1/5 values can be determined from this value (except for Luck).
The goal with this system of generating characteristics is to provide a reasonable floor for character stats and a realistic upper end (you are students after all) that allows for growth throughout the campaign. Within this setting, there are numerous ways to gain increases to characters or bonuses.
## House Rules
There are a number of house rules used in this campaign setting, including optional ones.
See:
- [[01-House Rule-Distress Points (DSP)|Optional House Rule: Distress Points]]
- [[02-House Rule-School Life|House Rule: School Life]] 
---
## Mechanics Adjustments
The following are a list of adjustments, clarifications, and exercised options available in the Call Of Cthulhu system that are made use of in Caroline College.
### Sanity Loss Adjustments
- **Reading Mythos Tomes**:
    - Costs sanity but **will not trigger bouts of madness or insanity** if done in a safe environment.
### Recovery from Indefinite Insanity
Students at Caroline College have access to **counseling sessions** provided by the local Lutheran church. These sessions are non-religious and aim to aid students in recovering from indefinite insanity and trauma.
- **Weekly Counseling Sessions**:
    - **Availability**: Once per week, when not participating in a game session. This is the same as Call of Cthulhu recovery method in all ways except the frequency (weekly as opposed to monthly).
    - **Sanity Recovery Mechanics**:
        - **Recovery Attempt**:
            - Roll percentile dice (1d100).
            - On a result of **01–95**:
                - **Success**: Recover **1d10 Sanity Points**.
            - On a result of **96–100**:
                - **Setback**:
                    - Lose **1d6 Sanity Points**.
                    - Gain a **new phobia** related to the stress or topics discussed during counseling.
        - **Resolving Indefinite Insanity**:
            - If Sanity Points are gained during a counseling session, you may immediately make a Sanity check (using your updated Sanity score).
            - On a **Hard Success**, your indefinite insanity is resolved.
    - **Time Commitment**:
        - Attending a counseling session requires an in-game time slot, potentially conflicting with classes or investigations.
    - **Keeper's Note**:
        - Frequent therapy sessions may draw attention or have narrative implications, adding to the tension of balancing time.
        - **Failed Therapy Sessions**:
            - May induce phobias related to the therapy content, providing additional story hooks.
### Luck Recovery and Advancement
**Luck advancements** are made at the **start of every game session**.
- **Luck Recovery Mechanics**:
    - **Improvement Check**:
        - Roll 1d100.
        - If the roll is **above** your current Luck, add **1d10 points**.
        - If the roll is equal to or less than your current Luck, no points are recovered.
- **Note**:
    - Luck may not exceed 99.
    - The starting Luck value is not used again in the game.
### Skill Advancements
**Skill advancements** are made after thematically appropriate breaks, as determined by the keeper (expect **3–5 per semester, including exams**).
### PvP Interactions and Loss of Control
- **Player vs. Player (PvP) 'Attacks'**:
    - Must be made with **consent** of all involved players.
- **Loss of Control Situations**:
    - Occur when a character is under the effects of insanity, a Breakdown due to Distress, or certain supernatural influences.
    - Actions are at the keeper's discretion.
    - The keeper should consider player enjoyment and strive for consensual storytelling.
### Backstory Connections
- **Robust and Thematically Appropriate Backstories**:
    - Include one or more entries with a **dark element**.
    - Develop meaningful locations, significant people, and pivotal events that add depth.
- **Character Connections**:
    - Every character must have a connection to **at least two other characters** in the party in their backstory.
    - No character can have more than two connections to them.
### Group Skill Checks
- **Assisting with Skill Rolls**:
    - If more than one character attempts a skill roll for the same task, under pressure:
        - If at least **two characters have skill above baseline**, one person can make the roll with a **Bonus Die**.
### Spending Luck
- **Luck Points** can be spent to alter the result of a skill or characteristic roll on a **1-for-1 basis**.
- **Restrictions**:
    - Cannot spend Luck on:
        - Luck rolls
        - Damage rolls
        - Sanity rolls
        - Rolls to determine the amount of Sanity points lost
    - Cannot spend Luck on **Pushed Rolls**.
    - **Critical, Fumbles, and Firearm Malfunctions** cannot be altered with Luck.
    - **No skill improvement check** is earned if Luck was used to alter the roll.
---
## Character Creation Advice
This section is not about rule modifications or clarifications. Instead, it is advice for how to get the most out of your character's time at Caroline College. Every setting has tropes and archetypes and a game set in the early 80's in the Midwest of the United States is no different. So here is some advise for making characters that fit the feel of Caroline College.
### Hopefuls, Not Heroes. 
This is a story of people who got in over their heads and either rose to the occasion or failed in the most memorable way possible. Is it possible to make a character that has millions of dollars in assets available to them, the ears of kings and presidents, and was a former super solider work in the setting? Maybe. Would it [[!How I Play#Respecting the Mood|respect the mood]] of the setting. Absolutely not.
#### Character Ideas and Suggestions For Players Who Don't Know Where To Start
- **Get Dirty:** Remember that this is a horror game with a setting that assumes **no one** is pure and innocent. Everyone in Watashuka has a skeleton in their closet; even you. The size of this skeleton, and how far back in the closet it is, is up to you; but its there. For some it might be minor and public; youthful drug use that left a mark on you that you don't deny, a problem with juvie as a child that you'd rather not talk about, something. 
	- **Why?** Because just like a fantasy game where your character is expected to take wounds and recover, a horror game inflicts wounds too. But when those wound happen, it is more interesting, and hopefully fun, to have a way to show those wounds by more than a number in a box. Call of Cthulhu works best when the backstory is the most important page on the character sheet. As horrors rend your mind, your backstory changes. New facts become 'discovered' about your past. It is much more meaningful to have a fertile bed ready for this than just a blank sheet and rolled phobia.
	- **DO NOT USE THE GAME AS THERAPY.** It is tempting for some people to use real life, lived pain, as a basis for a character's backstory. Don't do this. We are gamers, not therapists. While it may be cathartic for you, it is not for your fellow table-mates.
- **Ask before touching:** The NPCs in the setting can be a great way of tying your character into the setting early on. While we have tried to add dozens and dozens of NPCs that you might know, some of these NPCs have backstories of their own. Work with the Keeper BEFORE fleshing out an elaborate back story involving you being the long lost child of an NPCs who never had children. By asking first, the Keeper can help find an appropriate way to tie you into the game. They may even be able to help you weave new lore of the world!
- **Don't Be Afraid To Be New:** The College actively recruits people from outside the region. Maybe you have no ties to the region. Maybe you are here as a last resort - the failing student who got a surprise full-ride scholarship to a little school in the middle of nowhere. Or perhaps you are running from something back home, something you would like to stay far away. Work with your Keeper as needed.
- **Don't 'Cheat':** "*Well, my character has connection to X so I should already know all about Y and Z.*". Or "*I'm the Q's daughter so I should be able to just walk into the secret meeting.*" This is a game of horror and horror means the unknown. Don't try to engineer a character that takes the fun out of the horror but circumventing it. We aren't here to 'win', we are here to play.
- **Embrace The Unknown:** If you are at Caroline College, you deserve to be at Caroline College. Rise above the madness by investigating it.
##### Example Starting Points For Characters
If you need them, take inspiration from the following. Mix, match, ignore, add to, etc. 
- **Small-Town Legacy** – A freshman who grew up hearing stories of their uncle's disappearance while working the night shift at _[[WCTU]]_ (notice all the hosts that are 'replacements'). They’re studying journalism, determined to find out what happened, but their family warns them against digging too deep.
- **New School, New Dreams, right?**: Maybe if I leave the state the dreams will stop. Maybe I won't drop out my first semester, again. Maybe a psychology major will help me remember the dreams I can't recall. Maybe it will help me forget them altogether.
- **Amateur Cryptid Hunter** – A kid who grew up on Ripley's and "In Search Of...".  Fascinated by rumors of cryptid sightings around Lake Geneva and Watashuka decides to major in biology to see if its even possible.
- **The Journalist’s Protégé** – A journalism major with a passion for uncovering the truth. They landed an early internship at _The Prairie Press_ under [[Norm Habersham]], but they've started to receive strange anonymous tips and can't shake the feeling they’re being watched.
- **The Former Delinquent** – Fresh out of high school, you barely scraped into college after a troubled past at North High (how did that happen). You’re trying to start fresh, but a broken home is hard to over come. Especially with spending all your life hearing hints that mom and dad knew more about what went down at South High that night. 
- **The Reluctant Believer** – A history major, raised by a strict religious family, who grew up hearing warnings about occult forces infiltrating Caroline College. Not a founding member, but a passionate one, your grandfather made sure you heard all of [[Mothers Opposing Metal|Mothers Opposing Metal's]] warnings. But now that you are on campus, you can’t help but notice strange things, particularly in St. John’s Chapel, that remind you of his warnings.
- **The Absent Minded Pre-Med Student?** – You've always been drawn to medicine, and was a promising student. But now that you are on campus it seems you can't remember where you put your stuff. And there must be allergies in your dorm because you wake up with nose bleeds... a lot.
- **The Photographer with a Problem** – A freshman art major with a passion for photography. Maybe the school will help you go to the next level... and finally learn how to stop getting that odd light smudge that sometimes show up in your pictures when you take photos of certain places.
- **Maybe Dad Was Right** – The child of a longtime Watashuka resident, you grew up hearing stories about strange happenings around Lake Mary, particularly from your eccentric family members. Now that you’re attending Caroline College, you’re starting to wonder if those stories might be more than just local myths.
- **Absentee Grandfather** - You are here. Therefore, you had a father. That's just science right? And that means he had a father; it follows. Then why is the last mention of my grandfather, anywhere in town, a baptism record from before WW2?
- **The Hesitant Explorer** – An outdoor enthusiast who joined Caroline College’s Adventure Club, eager to explore the forests around the town. Maybe you'll get a chance to see the creature that licked your palm clean of blood when you feel down that ravine when you were a kid. Too bad the scout guides scared it away before you could see more than its tongue.
- **The Quiet Music Major** – Drawn to the _Don Peachy Center for the Performing Arts_, you quickly discover that perfect pitch doesn't mean that someone in in your head telling you what to play when under stress.
### Backstory Elements
Developing a rich backstory adds depth to your character and enhances the gaming experience. Each character should create entries for the following areas, aiming for meaningful and engaging content. This is a horror game, so dark elements within a backstory is acceptable, thematically appropriate, and strongly encouraged (within the limits defined by Session Zero). Try to remember that your characters don't know what's happening in the setting yet; hints and suggestions go a long way!
#### Ideology/Beliefs
- **Bad Example**: "I believe in justice."
    - _Why it's bad_: Too vague and generic; lacks depth.
- **Acceptable Example**: "I believe that the legal system is flawed, and true justice can only be achieved outside of it."
    - _Why it's acceptable_: Adds complexity and hints at potential conflicts.
- **Good Example**: "Ethan prowls the city's backstreets at night, where justice rarely reaches. When the courts failed him and the guilty walked free, he wasn't above bending the rules to set things right. To him, the law is just a guideline, and true justice sometimes requires a darker path that others might deem questionable."
    - _Why it's good_: Provides depth, aligns with game themes, and introduces moral ambiguity.
#### Significant People
- **Bad Example**: "My mother."
    - _Why it's bad_: Too general; doesn't explain significance.
- **Acceptable Example**: "My mother, who supported my academic pursuits."
    - _Why it's acceptable_: Offers context but lacks depth.
- **Good Example**: "Amelia carries a tattered letter from her estranged mother, filled with unsent words of apology. She reads it under dim lamplight, wondering about the life her mother chose over her family. Each word fuels Amelia's resolve to find her, not just to reconnect, but to understand the choices that led them apart."
    - _Why it's good_: Adds personal stakes, urgency, and ties to potential plot lines.
#### Meaningful Locations
- **Bad Example**: "The park."
    - _Why it's bad_: Too vague; lacks meaningful context.
- **Acceptable Example**: "The old park near my childhood home where I used to play."
    - _Why it's acceptable_: Provides some context but lacks depth.
- **Good Example**: "The rusted remains of the old Ferris wheel loom over the deserted fairground, a place where Lucas once shared a fleeting moment of joy with his first love before she moved away without a word. He returns there, the silence heavy with memories and unanswered questions, hoping one day to recapture that lost connection or at least find closure."
    - _Why it's good_: Rich atmosphere, ties into supernatural elements, and profoundly impacts the character.
#### Treasured Possessions
- **Bad Example**: "A book."
    - _Why it's bad_: Generic; doesn't reveal anything about the character.
- **Acceptable Example**: "An old diary from my grandmother."
    - _Why it's acceptable_: Provides a familial connection but could be more detailed.
- **Good Example**: "Lily discovered an old, leather-bound book hidden behind a loose brick in her grandmother's fireplace. The pages are filled with faded handwriting and strange symbols she doesn't understand. As she reads, unsettling family secrets begin to surface—stories of forgotten ancestors and choices that cast long shadows over her family's history, secrets they had tried desperately to keep buried. At least she knows she isn't alone in her bad choices."
    - _Why it's good_: Deeply personal, tied to game lore, and serves as a catalyst for adventures.
---
With these house rules and guidelines, we aim to create an engaging, immersive, and enjoyable gaming experience for everyone involved and one that is tailored to the stories told at Caroline College. Every table is different. And during session zero these rules adjustments can be discussed, modified or removed as the table decides. 

---

title: "Session Zero Guidelines"
draft: false
publish: true
tags:

---
# Session Zero Guidelines
### Starting Campaigns
We begin new campaigns with a **Session Zero** to:
- Align expectations.
- Discuss boundaries.
- Establish the tone.
- Integrate characters into the world.
### Backstories
- **Characters Should Not Start as Heroes**:
    - Focus on backstories that plant seeds for future adventures.
    - Avoid having characters who have already achieved greatness.
### Fitting the Tone
- Ensure your character fits the **theme of the campaign** (early 1980's horror sit in small town America).
### Party Dynamics
- **Create Characters That Fit the Party**:
    - Develop strong connections with at least two other characters.
    - Collaborate during character creation to ensure cohesion.
    - Come to session zero with ideas, not characters.
### Respecting the Mood
- **Maintain Immersion**:
    - Avoid breaking tension with out-of-place jokes, side talk, etc..
    - Engage with the core themes agreed upon.
### Rule of Cool
- **Story Over Rules**: We'll follow the Rule of Cool to prioritize narrative over strict rule adherence.
### Improvisation and Player Agency
- **Your Actions Shape the Story**:
    - Major events occur based on your decisions.
    - Creativity is rewarded, even if payoffs aren't immediate.
    - Not every encounter is balanced; sometimes avoiding conflict is wise.
### Player Preparation
- **Stay Engaged**:
    - Be attentive during sessions.
    - Review notes between sessions.
    - Keep your character curious and involved.
- **Session Recaps**:
    - Before each session, a player provides a recap of the previous session (group's choosing).
    - **Incentive**:
        - The player who provides the recap gains a **one-time Bonus Die** for the session (unused bonus dice do not roll over).
### Safety Tools
- **Player Comfort Is a Priority**:
    - **Session Zero**: Establish comfort levels and boundaries.
    - **Lines & Veils**:
        - **Lines**: Hard limits not to be crossed.
        - **Veils**: Topics that can occur but not be spotlighted.
    - **X Card**:
        - Tap the X card to immediately stop and change uncomfortable content.
    - **Consent Flowers**:
        - **Green**: Keep going.
        - **Yellow**: Proceed with caution.
        - **Red**: Change the subject.
- **Examples**:
    - A player indicating a yellow consent flower might prompt the keeper to adjust the scene's intensity without disrupting gameplay.
### Themes and Boundaries
- **Discuss Sensitive Topics**:
    - Be proactive in expressing preferences.
    - Common topics include violence, discrimination, sexuality, and personal phobias.
### Conflict Resolution
- **In-Character Conflict**:
    - Should serve the narrative.
    - Avoid actions that disrupt group dynamics.
- **Out-of-Character Conflict**:
    - Address issues respectfully among yourselves.
    - The keeper is a storyteller, not a mediator.
### Role-Playing
- **Immerse Yourself**:
    - Act and speak as your character.
    - Avoid phrases like "My character does X."
### Player Respect
- **Treat Each Other with Respect**:
    - Respect beliefs and views without imposing them.
    - Create a welcoming environment.
    - Address discomfort promptly and respectfully.
---
## Common Topics to Discuss
During Session Zero, we'll address the following possible story elements to ensure everyone's comfort:
- **Frequently Lined Topics**:
    - Sexualized violence
    - Child abuse
    - Animal cruelty
- **Frequently Veiled Topics**:
    - Racism
    - Discrimination against minorities
    - Sexuality
    - Torture
    - Phobias (spiders, snakes, clowns, dentists)
    - Serious illnesses
    - Sexism
    - Suicide

# Optional Expanded Sanity Rules for Call of Cthulhu
_Note: These rules are optional and will be discussed during Session Zero. They are designed to enhance the horror experience in long-term campaigns without incapacitating characters through excessive Sanity loss._
*These rules were heavily inspired by the work Apostol Apostolov at [## Chaosium Call of Cthulhu 7th Edition House Rules](https://www.gmbinder.com/share/-Mjep4ji0GZdmV57OMGg)*
For details on making characters see [[01-Characters-Caroline|Character Creation]]
## Introduction
The Expanded Sanity Rules introduce a new mechanic called **Distress Points (DSP)** to add psychological depth and realism to our game. Like standard Sanity Points (SAN), which decrease as characters encounter supernatural horrors, Distress Points start at a maximum value and decrease as characters face stress from realistic, non-supernatural threats. This allows characters to handle man-made horrors and stressful situations without immediate risk of madness.
## Distress Points (DSP)
### What Are Distress Points?
- **Distress Points** represent your character's mental resilience to stress from non-supernatural situations, such as tough decisions, resource scarcity, or dangerous environments.
- Every character starts with DSP equal to their **POW** (similar to how SAN is calculated).
### Losing Distress Points
- **Non-Supernatural Encounters**: Non-supernatural horrors cause DSP loss instead of SAN loss. This would replace the traditional sanity roll for these mundane encounters.
- **Stressful Situations**: When facing non-horrific, but still stress situations, DSP checks may need to be made.
- **SAN Rolls**: Making a sanity roll, by definition, is caused by a situation that is stressful. You lose a a DSP every time a sanity roll is made; pass or fail.
- **Voluntary SAN Damage**: You can always choose to take SAN damage instead of losing DSP, but not the reverse.
### Effects of Distress Points
- **Above Half DSP** (more than half of your maximum DSP): You remain composed; your hidden traits are under control.
- **Equal to or Below Half DSP** (half or less of your maximum DSP):
    - Begin to show minor signs of stress linked to your **Dark Trait**.
    - Each time you lose 5 or more DSP at once, roll against your current DSP. If you roll equal to or less than your DSP, you experience a **Breakdown** for 1d4 rounds.
- **Equal to or Below One-Fifth DSP** (one-fifth or less of your maximum DSP):
    - Your behavior is noticeably affected by your Dark Trait.
    - Breakdowns last longer (1d10 rounds), and the Keeper may suggest actions for your character.
- **At Zero DSP**:
    - You suffer a **Complete Breakdown**.
    - The Keeper may take control of your character until DSP is recovered.
### Maximum DSP
- **DSP cannot exceed your starting value** (POW). Rest and recovery can help you regain lost DSP up to this maximum.
## Example of a Breakdown
### **Scenario**:
Maria, an investigator with a starting POW of 60, starts with **DSP = 60**. Her **Dark Trait** is **Paranoia**, which she keeps hidden from the rest of the team.
### Events Leading to the Breakdown:
1. **Initial Stress**:    
    - Maria and her team are exploring an abandoned asylum.
    - She encounters realistic but disturbing graffiti and unsettling noises.
    - Over time, she loses **20 DSP**, reducing her DSP to **40**.
2. **DSP at Half Maximum**:
    - Since her DSP is now at **40** (which is two-thirds of 60), she remains composed.
3. **Further Stress**:
    - The team finds a room with detailed accounts of past tortures (non-supernatural).
    - Maria loses **15 DSP** due to the distressing content, bringing her DSP down to **25**.
4. **DSP Falls to Half or Less**:
    - With DSP at **25** (less than half of 60), she begins to show minor signs of her Dark Trait (Paranoia).
    - She starts questioning the intentions of her teammates subtly.
5. **Triggering a Breakdown**:
    - Suddenly, a realistic but horrific trap is sprung, causing Maria to lose **10 DSP** at once, dropping her DSP to **15**.
    - Because she lost **5 or more DSP at once** and her DSP is below half, she must roll against her current DSP (**15**).
        - She rolls a **22**, which is above her DSP.
        - **Breakdown Triggered**: The Breakdown will last **1d4 rounds** (let's say she rolls a 3).
### During the Breakdown:
- **Behavior**:    
    - For the next **3 rounds**, Maria's paranoia takes over.
    - She becomes convinced that one of her teammates is sabotaging the mission.
    - She might accuse them openly, refuse to share information, or even act defensively if approached.
- **Keeper's Role**:    
    - The Keeper reminds Maria's player of her Dark Trait and suggests actions that reflect her heightened paranoia.
    - The player can choose how to role-play these suggestions within the confines of the Breakdown.
### After the Breakdown:
- Maria's DSP remains at **15**.
- She regains some composure but still shows signs of stress.
- The team may notice her odd behavior, and she might need to find ways to recover DSP.
## Dark Traits
### What Are Dark Traits?
- **Dark Traits** are hidden aspects of your character's personality that emerge under stress.
- They add depth to your character and provide role-playing opportunities.
### Selecting a Dark Trait
- Choose a Dark Trait during character creation. It should remain secret from other players but not the keeper.
- Examples include traits like paranoia, obsession, aggression, or compulsiveness.
- Your Dark Trait influences how your character behaves as DSP decreases.
### Revealing Dark Traits
- As DSP decreases, subtle behaviors linked to your Dark Trait begin to surface.
- Under severe stress or during Breakdowns, these traits may dominate your actions.
## Managing Distress
- **Rest and Relaxation**:
    - **Short Rest**: Resting for at least an hour in a safe, comfortable environment restores **1d10 DSP**. This cannot be repeated until at least one point of DSP has been lost.
    - **Extended Rest**: A **full** day of rest restores **10 DSP** (may be repeated as needed).
- **Composure Attempts**:
    - **POW Roll**: Attempt a POW roll to compose yourself. If your current DSP is at or below half maximum, the roll is of Hard difficulty.
    - **Success**: Restores **1d4 DSP** during danger or **1d6+1 DSP** when safe.
- **Assistance from Allies**:
    - Another character can use a **Psychology** roll to help you recover.
    - Success has the same effects as a successful POW roll. These cannot be used in conjugation. But if one fails, the other may be attempted. 
- **Indulging in Manias**:
    - Engaging in a personal mania restores **1d6+1 DSP**.
    - Requires a Sanity roll; failure results in **1 SAN loss**.
### Pacing Stress Loss
- To keep gameplay smooth, DSP losses can be accumulated over a scene and applied at the end.
- This minimizes interruptions and maintains narrative flow.
- Immediate DSP losses may still occur during sudden shocks or critical moments.
### Increased Impact of Phobias
- If your character has a **Phobia**, encountering its trigger doubles any DSP losses.
## Purpose of These Rules
- **Enhanced Role-Playing**: Allows for deeper character development as hidden traits surface under stress.
- **Balanced Horror Experience**: Maintains the horror atmosphere without quickly incapacitating characters through massive Sanity loss.
- **Long-Term Campaign Suitability**: Ideal for extended play, where character arcs and psychological journeys are explored over time.
## Conclusion
Please consider how these rules might enhance your gaming experience. They aim to add psychological realism and depth to our campaign, offering new challenges and role-playing opportunities without overwhelming your character with Sanity loss. We'll discuss these rules in detail during Session Zero to ensure everyone is comfortable and understands how they will be integrated into our game.
---
# List of 50 Example Dark Traits
The following are example dark traits; others are possible. Please discuss your choice with the keeper before finalizing your selection.
## Dark Traits Table
- **1. AGGRESSIVE**: Physical action and violence are your solutions to every problem.
	- **Under Distress**: You display bouts of verbal aggression and may intimidate allies who challenge your decisions.
	- **Breakdown**: You are unlikely to restrain yourself from combat until any perceived enemy is neutralized.
- **2. MARTYR**: You feel overwhelmed by responsibility for others.
	- **Under Distress**: You become less concerned with your own well-being and focus entirely on your allies' needs.
	- **Breakdown**: You're willing to sacrifice yourself for a greater goal or the survival of others.
- **3. COWARD**: Fear dominates your actions.
	- **Under Distress**: You become pessimistic and sarcastic, openly expecting the worst outcomes.
	- **Breakdown**: You panic and flee, even if it means abandoning your friends in danger.
- **4. EGOTIST**: Your primary concern is your own well-being and survival.
	- **Under Distress**: Your decisions prioritize your needs over others.
	- **Breakdown**: You place your safety above everything, even denying help or betraying allies.
- **5. SADISTIC**: You derive pleasure from others' discomfort.
	- **Under Distress**: You may enjoy causing harm or misfortune to feel better.
	- **Breakdown**: You pursue actions that cause maximum harm to enemies, even if it jeopardizes plans or allies.
- **6. PARANOID**: You believe others are constantly scheming against you.
	- **Under Distress**: You see coincidences as evidence of conspiracies.
	- **Breakdown**: You're convinced immediate events are part of a grand plot and take drastic action to counter it.
- **7. PSYCHOPATHIC**: You disconnect from others' emotions and needs.
	- **Under Distress**: You focus solely on your goals, unable to communicate intentions or feelings.
	- **Breakdown**: You lose the ability to cooperate, resolving problems only on your own.
- **8. ANNOYING**: You have habits that irritate others, like excessive talking or fidgeting.
	- **Under Distress**: These habits intensify, helping you cope with uncertainty.
	- **Breakdown**: You struggle to concentrate, taking extra time and lacking focus.
- **9. DEPENDENT**: You seem independent but rely on others when stressed.
	- **Under Distress**: You cling to others for guidance and protection.
	- **Breakdown**: You're incapable of making decisions without someone telling you what to do.
- **10. MEGALOMANIAC**: You have an insatiable need for power and control.
	- **Under Distress**: Feeling weak causes you anxiety and frustration.
	- **Breakdown**: You'll stop at nothing to gain power, even embracing dangerous paths.
- **11. CURIOUS**: Your thirst for knowledge overrides caution.
	- **Under Distress**: You can't resist uncovering secrets, even risky ones.
	- **Breakdown**: You're compelled to experiment with newfound knowledge, often recklessly.
- **12. FIXATED**: You focus on repetitive activities to escape stress.
	- **Under Distress**: You feel compelled to continue these activities.
	- **Breakdown**: You fixate on one activity as a source of comfort, resisting attempts to stop.
- **13. LOUD**: You express emotions vocally.
	- **Under Distress**: You can't keep your voice down and openly share your thoughts.
	- **Breakdown**: You make a scene, yelling or ranting, potentially wasting valuable time.
- **14. ZEALOUS**: A strong belief or moral code anchors you.
	- **Under Distress**: You obsess over this belief and become anxious if it's challenged.
	- **Breakdown**: You feel your belief is under attack and will defend it fiercely.
- **15. CATATONIC**: You withdraw inward to cope.
	- **Under Distress**: You find it hard to speak and may shut down.
	- **Breakdown**: You halt actions, adopt a neutral posture, and become nearly mute, passively resisting interaction.
- **16. BURDENED**: You carry deeper troubles than most.
	- **Under Distress**: Your underlying issues surface, affecting your behavior.
	- **Breakdown**: Combine behaviors from two traits, intensifying your reactions.
- **17. COMPULSIVE LIAR**: You habitually lie, even without cause.
	- **Under Distress**: Your lies become elaborate and hard to maintain.
	- **Breakdown**: You create a false reality and insist others accept it.
- **18. MANIPULATIVE**: You influence others for personal gain.
	- **Under Distress**: You resort to deceit and exploitation.
	- **Breakdown**: You may manipulate allies into dangerous situations for your benefit.
- **19. OBSESSIVE**: You fixate on thoughts or ideas.
	- **Under Distress**: Obsessions dominate your actions.
	- **Breakdown**: You can't focus on anything else until satisfying your obsession.
- **20. PESSIMISTIC**: You expect the worst outcomes.
	- **Under Distress**: Your negativity affects group morale.
	- **Breakdown**: You're immobilized by hopelessness.
- **21. RECKLESS**: You take unnecessary risks.
	- **Under Distress**: You disregard safety measures.
	- **Breakdown**: You engage in dangerous actions without considering consequences.
- **22. JEALOUS**: You envy others' successes or possessions.
	- **Under Distress**: You undermine or sabotage others.
	- **Breakdown**: You attempt to take what others have by any means.
- **23. DECEITFUL**: Honesty isn't your policy.
	- **Under Distress**: You lie to protect yourself or gain an advantage.
	- **Breakdown**: You can't tell the truth, even when necessary.
- **24. ARROGANT**: You believe you're superior.
	- **Under Distress**: You belittle others and ignore advice.
	- **Breakdown**: Overconfidence leads you to make poor decisions.
- **25. CONTROLLING**: You need to be in charge.
	- **Under Distress**: You become domineering.
	- **Breakdown**: You attempt to control every aspect, causing conflict.
- **26. STUBBORN**: You refuse to change your mind.
	- **Under Distress**: You reject others' ideas.
	- **Breakdown**: You insist on your way, regardless of consequences.
- **27. IMPULSIVE**: You act without thinking.
	- **Under Distress**: You make hasty decisions.
	- **Breakdown**: You take immediate action without consideration.
- **28. ENVIOUS**: You desire what others have.
	- **Under Distress**: You fixate on others' possessions or status.
	- **Breakdown**: You might steal or sabotage to level the field.
- **29. APATHETIC**: You lack interest or concern.
	- **Under Distress**: You disengage from situations.
	- **Breakdown**: You become unresponsive to events around you.
- **30. NARCISSISTIC**: You have an inflated sense of self-importance.
	- **Under Distress**: You demand special treatment.
	- **Breakdown**: You believe only you can solve problems, dismissing others.
- **31. MASOCHISTIC**: You find satisfaction in your own discomfort.
	- **Under Distress**: You may self-sabotage or take unnecessary risks.
	- **Breakdown**: You engage in self-destructive behaviors.
- **32. UNTRUSTING**: You doubt others' intentions.
	- **Under Distress**: You suspect betrayal from those around you.
	- **Breakdown**: You isolate yourself, refusing help.
- **33. GLUTTONOUS**: You overindulge in pleasures.
	- **Under Distress**: You seek immediate gratification, neglecting duties.
	- **Breakdown**: You binge excessively, ignoring consequences.
- **34. IRRATIONAL**: You abandon logic and reason.
	- **Under Distress**: You make illogical decisions.
	- **Breakdown**: You cannot be reasoned with, acting unpredictably.
- **35. VINDICTIVE**: You hold grudges and seek revenge.
	- **Under Distress**: You dwell on past slights.
	- **Breakdown**: You focus solely on settling scores, regardless of cost.
- **36. FRACTIOUS**: You're irritable and prone to conflict.
	- **Under Distress**: You pick fights over minor issues.
	- **Breakdown**: You become uncooperative and disruptive.
- **37. OBSTINATE**: You're unyielding and inflexible.
	- **Under Distress**: You resist any change or compromise.
	- **Breakdown**: You become a barrier to progress and group harmony.
- **38. SUPERSTITIOUS**: You believe in omens and rituals.
	- **Under Distress**: You rely on superstitions to make decisions.
	- **Breakdown**: You refuse to act without a 'sign' or ritual.
- **39. WORKAHOLIC**: You're addicted to work.
	- **Under Distress**: You immerse yourself in tasks to avoid issues.
	- **Breakdown**: You neglect health and relationships, focusing only on work.
- **40. HYPOCHONDRIAC**: You fear illness excessively.
	- **Under Distress**: You misinterpret symptoms as serious ailments.
	- **Breakdown**: You believe you're critically ill, hindering your actions.
- **41. RESENTFUL**: You hold onto past wrongs.
	- **Under Distress**: You bring up old grievances.
	- **Breakdown**: You act out against perceived offenders, even if unwarranted.
- **42. INDECISIVE**: You struggle to make choices.
	- **Under Distress**: You're paralyzed by options.
	- **Breakdown**: You're incapable of deciding without external intervention.
- **43. GUILT-RIDDEN**: You're burdened by remorse.
	- **Under Distress**: You fixate on past mistakes.
	- **Breakdown**: You may confess to wrongs, real or imagined, distracting from current issues.
- **44. SCHADENFREUDE**: You take pleasure in others' misfortunes.
	- **Under Distress**: You may cause or amplify others' failures.
	- **Breakdown**: You actively create situations where others will fail.
- **45. COMPULSIVE CLEANER**: You need cleanliness and order.
	- **Under Distress**: You focus on tidiness over urgent matters.
	- **Breakdown**: You stop everything to clean compulsively, ignoring pressing issues.
- **46. ESCAPIST**: You avoid reality through distractions.
	- **Under Distress**: You retreat into fantasy or indulgent activities.
	- **Breakdown**: You detach completely from reality, becoming unresponsive.
- **47. CONTROL FREAK**: You micromanage every detail.
	- **Under Distress**: You can't delegate tasks, overwhelming yourself.
	- **Breakdown**: You try to handle everything alone, leading to burnout.
- **48. PROCRASTINATOR**: You delay tasks habitually.
	- **Under Distress**: You avoid responsibilities, causing delays.
	- **Breakdown**: You refuse to act, even when action is critical.
- **49. PERFECTIONIST**: Nothing meets your standards.
	- **Under Distress**: You obsess over minor flaws.
	- **Breakdown**: You're immobilized by the impossibility of perfection.
- **50. EMOTIONLESS**: You suppress your feelings.
	- **Under Distress**: You become detached and indifferent.
	- **Breakdown**: You can't empathize, making cold, calculated decisions without regard for others.

---
title: "House Rule: School Life"
draft: false
publish: true
tags:
  - TTRPG
  - Horror
---
**Recommendation**: Playing a character < = 39 years old is thematically appropriate. But nothing is stopping you from making a feisty middle-ager or spunky retiree. Just *work with the party*  to explain why these generationally disparate people are spending so much time together.
# House Rule: School Life
In this campaign, players must balance academic responsibilities with their mystery-solving adventures. Attending class not only helps avoid failing grades but also provides in-game bonuses through skill improvements.
See [[01-Characters-Caroline|Character Creation]] for more details about making a character in the world of Caroline College.
## Making The Grade
- **Class Selection**: Each player must choose 5 classes each semester.
	- Freshman Fall Semester: 
		- 3 **required classes**: One science, one history, and one language.
		- 2 **optional classes**: Chosen from the list of electives.
- **Passing a Class**:
	- Two exams will be held during the semester: a mid-term and a final
		- Making the mid-term advancement will grant a 'penalty' die on the final
			- As you want to 'fail' an advancement roll, the penalty die is a benefit 
	- Passing an exam involves making an advancement roll in the relative topic
		- *Luck may be used on this roll!* If you use luck to pass either of the two exams, you forfeit ALL advancements rolls from the course as well as attendance bonus.
			- Sometimes passing is more important.
	- Courses covering multiple skills
		- If a course covers multiple skills, then the player which ONE skill they will make the advancement for; not both
		- Different skills may be selected for the mid-term and final
- **Failing Classes**
	- Two consecutive semesters with five or fewer classes pass may result in academic probation. 
		- This can cause the student to lose access to campus facilities (including clubs and organizations), story line options, or other narrative consequences
- **Honor Roll**
	- Two consecutive semesters with 10 or more passed classes may result in honor role-playing
		- This may cause the character to gain access to new campus facilities, people, permissions and other bonuses.
- **Class Attendance**
	- Attending classes regularly will grant **+5%** to the relative skill at the end of the semester. 
		- This is in addition to the advancements made from the mid-term and final.
		- In courses that involve more than one skill, points will be distributed between the skills as the player wishes.
	- Meeting the attendance requirement, but failing a class, will still grant the bonus (you at least learned *something* by showing up).
	- All courses have a college required 70% attendance policy for all held classes.
		- Meeting this requirement is determined narratively.
- **Tension Mechanic**: Players must choose between attending classes or pursuing adventures, balancing academic success with their investigations.
## Limited Occupation: College Student
**All** characters at Caroline College use the occupation **College Student**.
- **Occupation Skill Points**: EDU × 3 (Reduced from the standard to reflect starting students but with more opportunities for advancement during the campaign).
- **Credit Rating**: 5–10
- **Suggested Contacts**: Other students.
- **Skills**:
    - Language (Own or Other)
    - Library Use
    - Listen
    - **Three Fields of Study** (choose three academic skills relevant to your character's studies)
    - **Any Two Other Skills** as personal or era specialties 
---
# Class Descriptions and Schedule
## Required Science Classes (Both lecture and lab must be attended)
- **Intro to Biology**
	- **Description**: Basic biological concepts with a focus on cellular structures, genetics, and ecology. The lab allows hands-on experience, where strange things might start to happen.
- **Chemistry 201**
	- **Prerequisite**: Chemistry 101, College Math or greater, or permission from the department chair
	- **Description**: Analyzing chemical bonding using atomic theory, stoichiometric methodologies, interpreting graphical chemical data and an introduction quantum mechanics. You never know when knowledge of chemical substances might help solve an occult mystery.
- **Technical Physics I**
	- **Prerequisite**: Calculus I, or permission from the department chair
	- **Description**: Calculus based introduction to physics. Topics include elementary forces, work and optics. 
## Required History Classes (Choose 1)
- **Western Civilization I**
	- **Description**: A comprehensive study of Western history, covering ancient civilizations through the Renaissance, with key insights into the origins of arcane practices.
- **History of the United States until 1855**
	- **Description**: An exploration of U.S. history from colonization to modern times. Local Wisconsin history becomes relevant to uncovering the hidden past of Watashuka.
## Required Language Classes (Choose 1)
- **English Composition I**
	- **Description**: Focuses on writing and analysis
- **Introductory Latin**
	- **Description**: Introduction to Latin
- **French I**
	- **Description**: Basics of French language
---
## Optional Classes (Choose 2)
- **Introduction to Public Speaking**
	- **Description**: This course teaches students the basics of effective verbal communication, focusing on persuasive speaking techniques, managing audience perception, and developing confidence in public speaking. Students will engage in debates, presentations, and impromptu speeches.
- **Foundations of Gymnastics**
	- **Description**: An introduction to physical conditioning, agility, and body mechanics. The course covers basic skills in climbing, jumping, running, and balance through physical training and exercises. Designed for students looking to enhance their physical prowess.
- **Intro to Parapsychology: An Introduction to the Weird**
	- **Description**: This course explores the fringes of scientific inquiry, delving into phenomena such as telepathy, clairvoyance, psychokinesis, and hauntings. Students will examine case studies, historical research, and conduct their own experiments to understand the possible connections between the mind and supernatural occurrences. Expect things to get weird.
- **Introduction to Computing**
	- **Description**: Students will learn the fundamentals of computing, including basic programming, data entry, and information processing. The course emphasizes practical computer applications in various fields.
- **Acting for Beginners**
	- **Description**: This course focuses on the foundations of acting, including role-playing, physicality, and emotional expression. Students will learn how to embody different characters, effectively altering their appearance and persona through performance techniques.
- **Basic Electronics**
	- **Description**: An introductory course covering basic principles of electricity, circuits, and electronic components. Students will engage in hands-on projects to understand the fundamentals of building and repairing electronic systems.
- **Marketing 101: Principles of Market Influence**
	- **Description**: This introductory course covers the fundamental concepts of marketing, including market research, consumer behavior, advertising strategies, and product positioning. Students will learn how to craft persuasive messages and develop marketing plans, with a focus on influencing consumer decision-making in various industries.
- **Basic First Aid and CPR**
	- **Description**: Students will learn essential first aid techniques, including CPR, wound treatment, and emergency response. The course is hands-on and prepares students for basic medical emergencies in everyday situations.
- **Introduction to Legal Studies**
	- **Description**: This course introduces the foundational concepts of law, including constitutional law, criminal justice, and civil procedures. Students will explore real-world case studies and participate in mock trials.
- **Information Research and Literacy**
	- **Description**: This course teaches students how to efficiently locate, evaluate, and use information from various sources, including libraries, archives, and digital databases. Emphasis is placed on research strategies and citation techniques.
- **Introduction to Mechanics**
	- **Description**: This hands-on course introduces students to the fundamentals of mechanical systems, focusing on repairing and maintaining machines, vehicles, and industrial equipment. Students will work in a lab setting, learning to use tools and heavy machinery.
- **Introduction to Medical Science**
	- **Description**: Designed for pre-med students, this course introduces the basics of human anatomy, pathology, and medical ethics. Students will explore medical case studies and observe hospital procedures.
- **Ecology and Environmental Studies 101**
	- **Description**: This course explores ecosystems, biodiversity, and environmental conservation. Students will learn about the interconnections between species and their environments through fieldwork and lab exercises.
- **Orienteering 101**
	- **Description**: A practical course in map reading, compass use, and wilderness navigation. Students will engage in field activities, learning how to navigate different terrains and track wildlife.
- **Introduction to Psychoanalytic Theory**
	- **Description**: This course introduces the basic principles of psychoanalytic theory, including concepts such as the unconscious, repression, and dream interpretation. Students will examine foundational case studies from Freud and Jung.
- **Forensic Science 101**
	- **Description**: Students will learn basic forensic techniques, focusing on crime scene investigation and evidence gathering. Emphasis is placed on attention to detail and spotting hidden clues during investigations.
- **Wilderness Survival Techniques**
	- **Description**: This course teaches the fundamentals of wilderness survival, including shelter building, fire-making, and finding food and water in the wild. Students will participate in hands-on field exercises.
- **Swimming for Lifelong Health**
	- **Description**: Students will learn swimming techniques, water safety, and endurance training. This course is ideal for beginners or those looking to improve their swimming skills.
- **Introduction to Anthropology**
	- **Description**: This course explores human cultures, ancient practices, and the development of civilizations. A particular focus is placed on the cultural practices of indigenous groups, such as the Ho-Chunk Nation, providing key insights into their sacred sites and traditions.
- **Introduction to Psychology**
	- **Description**: This course studies the human mind and behavior, including key psychological theories on cognition, perception, and social behavior. It is particularly useful for understanding the motivations of NPCs and evaluating mental health or sanity during investigations.
- **Public Speaking**
	- **Description**: This course provides instruction on developing persuasive speaking skills, helping students gain confidence in communication. It covers techniques for influencing and convincing others, skills that are useful during interactions with NPCs and negotiations.
- **Introduction to Philosophy**
	- **Description**: A deep dive into metaphysical questions and esoteric thought, this course examines classical and modern philosophical theories. Special attention is given to occult philosophies and ancient belief systems, making it ideal for players interested in occult knowledge.
- **Introduction to Theater**
	- **Description**: This course introduces students to improvisation, performance, and role-playing. Students will learn how to quickly adapt their personas and use verbal techniques to deceive or convince others, perfect for moments when quick thinking and fast talk are essential.
- **Drawing and Painting I**
	- **Description**: This studio-based course teaches the basics of drawing and painting techniques. Students will develop their skills in artistic expression, which can be used for sketching clues, analyzing artworks, or interpreting occult symbols found during investigations.
- **Introduction to Music Appreciation: From Cavemen to Chopin**
	- **Description**: A broad survey of music history, from ancient rhythmic traditions to classical compositions. This course hones students’ listening skills, making them more attuned to subtle auditory cues, which are often crucial during investigations where sound plays a role.
- **College Math**
	- **Description**: This course covers essential mathematical principles such as algebra, trigonometry, and basic calculus concepts. It serves as a foundation for students pursuing science, engineering, or economics, offering problem-solving techniques applicable to various fields.
- **Calculus I**
	- **Description**: An introduction to differential and integral calculus, focusing on limits, derivatives, and applications of the derivative in real-world contexts. This course is required for students pursuing technical fields such as physics, engineering, and economics.

**Caroline College**  
Office of the President  
Watashuka, Wisconsin 53586  
(608) 555-1234
_May 20, 1983_
Dear Student,
It is with great pride that I extend my warmest congratulations on your admission to **[[Caroline College]]** for the Fall 1983 semester. As an alumnus of the Class of 1937, I recall the excitement that comes with the opportunity to begin a new academic journey. You are about to join a close-knit community where students, faculty, and staff come together to explore ideas, develop talents, and forge lasting friendships.
Caroline College has been a beacon of learning since its early days as Prairieville Academy. Whether your passion lies in the sciences, the arts, technology, or the humanities, you will find a home here. For those pursuing scientific research, our cutting-edge **Qubit Tower** and **Brown Science Complex** provide state-of-the-art facilities that will push the boundaries of your understanding. Students drawn to music and the arts will find inspiration in the **Don Peachy Center for the Performing Arts**, where creativity thrives.
If your heart lies in the study of history, philosophy, or religious traditions, you will have the chance to engage deeply with our **Bowstein Center for Philosophy and Religious Research** and **Revival Study Center**, exploring questions that have shaped human thought for centuries. Whatever your interests—be it the humanities, liberal arts, agriculture, or even modern technology—Caroline College offers a broad academic experience that nurtures both intellectual curiosity and personal growth.
Though we are no longer a religious institution, our deep spiritual heritage remains an integral part of the Caroline College experience. Our campus fosters a thoughtful environment where students are encouraged to reflect not just on academic challenges, but on their place in the world and their potential to impact it.
In the coming weeks, you will receive further details about your orientation, class registration, and housing assignments. Should you have any questions, feel free to reach out to our Admissions Office at (608) 555-5678.
Once again, welcome to Caroline College. I look forward to meeting you this fall and witnessing the new chapter you will write in our shared history.
Warm regards,
[[Dr. Daniel J. Stanton]]
President, Caroline College  
Class of 1937
