# Caroline College: Campus Directory
![[Caroline_College_RasterAged.jpg]]
- **[[Prairie Hall]]**
	- **Built:** 1856
	- **Description:** The oldest structure on campus, Prairie Hall was the first building constructed for the original Prairieville School. Now a historic museum, it houses artifacts from early Wisconsin life and stands as a testament to the school’s origins in education. The building sits atop an elaborate basement which houses most of the artifacts.
- **Founder's Hall**
	- **Built**: 1862, relocated 1945
	- **Description**: **Founder's Hall**, originally constructed after the rebuilding of the Prairieville School in 1862, now serves as the college's alumni center. It was relocated in 1945 to make way for campus land expansion and construction.
- **Morgan Lafayette Liberal Arts Center**
	- **Built:** 1950
	- **Description:** A bustling center for liberal arts, the Lafayette Center encourages interdisciplinary collaboration and intellectual discourse. Its modernist architecture was funded through significant post-war grants, supporting the growth of liberal education.
- **Duff Business Center of Excellence**
	- **Built:** 1949
	- **Student Nickname**: DBC
	- **Description:** The Duff Business Center is home to the esteemed business program, offering real-world opportunities for students through partnerships with local industries. Its growth was fueled by post-WWII funding aimed at developing future leaders in business.
- **Rite Hall**
	- **Built:** 1875
	- **Student Nickname**: Admin
	- **Description:** Serving as the administrative core of Caroline College, Rite Hall houses student services, faculty offices, and administrative departments. This stately building has long been the backdrop for important college events and student support services.
- **Brown Science Complex**
	- **Built:** 1945-1954
	- **Student Nickname**: The Dungeon
	- **Description:** The Brown Science Complex consists of interconnected buildings dedicated to advancing scientific inquiry. The complex was developed with government support to enhance STEM education post-WWII.
	- **Buildings Include:**
    	- **Castelaz Building and Observatory** (physical sciences): the crown jewel of the Brown complex, the observatory houses a stunning 30-inch refractor telescope, the **Wright Telescope**; one of the largest student-operated telescopes in the Midwest.
    	- **Gardner Mathematics Hall** (mathematics and parapsychology):  Gardner Hall is a  striking example of modern architectural prowess that houses a thriving mathematics department. At the heart of Gardner Mathematics Hall lies the **Great Hall**, a breathtaking three-story atrium with soaring ceilings and intricate glasswork that bathe the space in natural light. Here, students gather to collaborate on complex problems, attend guest lectures, and engage in spirited debates – all within an atmosphere of intellectual rigor and camaraderie.
    	- **Luttermoser Science Hall** (biological and chemical sciences): The centerpiece of Luttermoser Science Hall is the **Atrium of Discovery**, a vast open-plan space that encourages interdisciplinary collaboration and exchange among faculty and students. Here, you'll find interactive exhibits, artwork inspired by scientific concepts, and even a living wall of plants.
    	- **The Obelisk of Nekhbet** (monument): On permanent loan from Cairo University. Installed in 1954, the Obelisk stands as a symbol of the college’s commitment to global cultural awareness and intellectual exchange.
- **Scarlet Center for Women’s Studies**
	- **Built:** 1970
	- **Description:** A focal point for research and study of gender studies, law, forensic science and social justice issues, the Scarlet Center is a progressive space dedicated to intellectual exploration. Its development was part of a post-war expansion to support diverse academic programs.
- **Adda F. Howie Center for Agricultural Theory**
	- **Built:** 1958
	- **Description:** Named after a trailblazing figure in agricultural science, the Howie Center connects theoretical agricultural studies with practical applications. The center’s programs have been instrumental in modernizing regional agricultural practices.
- **C.D. Levi Agriculture Science Complex**
	- **Built:** 1901
	- **Student Nickname**: The Farm
	- **Description:** Known for its extensive greenhouses and experimental farms, "The Farm" provides hands-on experience in agriculture. The complex’s expansion after WWII reflects the nation’s emphasis on sustainability and food security.
- **Lantern Memorial Park, Reflecting Pool, and Cemetery**
	- **Established:** 1939
	- **Student Nickname**: The Swinging Tree
	- **Description:** A serene spot for reflection, Lantern Memorial Park commemorates the life of visiting artist Elijah Kane. It offers a peaceful place for students to gather, surrounded by nature and tranquility.
- **Prairie Dog Stadium**
	- **Built:** 1914
	- **Description:** Home to the Prairie Dogs baseball team, this stadium fosters community spirit and competition. The facility is also used for various campus events, including intramural sports and large gatherings.
- **The Burrow**
	- **Built:** 1968
	- **Student Nickname**: Student Center
	- **Description:** As the social hub of campus, The Burrow provides spaces for student organizations, recreational activities, and events. This lively center encourages students to engage with their peers and build lasting friendships.
- **Ho-Chunk Cultural Heritage Museum**
	- **Built:** 1955
	- **Student Nickname**: HCC
	- **Description:** The HCC museum showcases the rich history and cultural contributions of Wisconsin's Ho-Chunk Nation. It serves as an educational space where students and visitors can learn about indigenous heritage.
- **S. Fields Building**
	- **Built:** 1885
	- **Student Nickname**: SFB
	- **Description:** This building houses the departments of anthropology and sociology. It offers students the opportunity to explore societal structures and human behavior through comprehensive research programs.
- **Philip Love Aquatic Center**
	- **Built:** 1975
	- **Student Nickname**: The Pool
	- **Description:** The newest facility on campus, the Philip Love Aquatic Center boasts both indoor and outdoor pools, offering opportunities for recreational swimming, water sports, and scuba certification.
- **Rutherford-Walsh Mann Track and Sport Field**
	- **Built:** 1901
	- **Description:** A key athletic facility, this complex supports track and field events, intramural sports, and physical education classes. Its construction reflected the post-war emphasis on physical fitness and community well-being.
- **McElhenney Journalism School and Communications Center**
	- **Built:** 1955
	- **Description:** A center for media and communications studies, McElhenney School trains students in modern journalism practices. The school’s graduates have gone on to work in national media outlets, reflecting its reputation for excellence.
- **Bowstein Center of Philosophy and Religious Research**
	- **Built:** 1869
	- **Description:** The Bowstein Center engages students with global philosophical and religious traditions. The center’s vast library and connections with international scholars make it a vibrant hub for intellectual exchange.
- **Gale Veterinary Hospital and Training School**
	- **Built:** 1957
	- **Description:** This hospital specializes in the treatment of large animals, providing students with hands-on veterinary training. It serves both the campus and the surrounding agricultural community.
- **Research Greenhouses (Plant Science Research)**
	- **Built:** 1953
	- **Description:** The Research Greenhouses offer state-of-the-art facilities for plant science and agriculture. Students here work on projects related to sustainability, conservation, and crop development.
- **West Maintenance Building**
	- **Built:** 1946
	- **Student Nickname**: The Dump
	- **Description:** Housing the campus facilities management team, this building ensures the maintenance and smooth operation of the entire campus, from heating systems to grounds keeping. A few industrial arts courses are even taught here. The students who choose to engage are given the opportunity to learn and help their school!
- **Campus Security Station**
	- **Built:** 1888
	- **Student Nickname**: The Jail
	- **Description:** The security station monitors the campus 24/7, offering students and staff a sense of safety and peace of mind. Its modern surveillance systems keep the campus secure.
- **Fonseca Power Systems Research Facilities**
	- **Built:** 1960
	- **Student Nickname**: The Nightlight
	- **Description:** This engineering research facility provides students with unparalleled opportunities in civil, electrical, and mechanical engineering. Its advanced labs and technology help foster the next generation of engineers.
- **Don Peachy Center for the Performing Arts**
	- **Built:** 1956
	- **Description:** A vibrant space for theater and music, the Don Peachy Center is home to numerous student performances and cultural events. Its folk and ethnic music programs are renowned in the region.
- **Fine Arts Building**
	- **Built:** 1899
	- **Student Nickname**: The Fab
	- **Description:** The **Fine Arts Building**, constructed in 1899, stands as one of the oldest structures on campus, housing studios, galleries, and classrooms for the college’s art programs. Originally named after a prominent local patron, its title was quietly changed in 1923 following a scandal that has since been buried, leaving it now known simply as the *Fine Arts Building*.
- **J. Sawyer Amphitheater**
	- **Built:** 1937
	- **Student Nickname**: The Pit
	- **Description:** This expansive outdoor venue hosts concerts, guest speakers, and campus-wide events. Its open-air design provides a picturesque setting for graduation ceremonies.
- **Prairie Academy Teacher Training Center**
	- **Built:** 1965
	- **Student Nickname**: The Academy
	- **Description:** The Academy is a center for teacher training, returning the college to its roots. The facility is also home to the **E. Rowe School for the Gifted**, providing specialized education for exceptional students.
- **Sterling Men’s Dormitory and E. Root Women’s Dormitory**
	- **Built:** 1950
	- **Description:** These dormitories provide comfortable housing for students from all corners of the country. Their location in the heart of campus ensures students are close to academic and social life.
- **Dennis W. Dark Ecology Research Center**
	- **Built:** 1961
	- **Description:** This research station offers students the opportunity to study the region’s native ecology, with advanced technology for weather tracking and ecological research. Advanced ecology and environmental laboratory work is performed here.
- **Annex Buildings**
	- **Built:** 1863
	- **Student Nickname**: The Attics
	- **Description:** Originally constructed to house soldiers during the Civil War, these buildings are now used for storage. They stand as a reminder of the college's long history and connection to national events.
- **Qubit Tower**
	- **Built:** 1968
	- **Student Nickname**:  The Brain
	- **Description:** Qubit Tower is home to **two** of the most powerful supercomputers in the Midwest, offering students unique opportunities in computational research and data science.
- **Revival Study Center (Classical Studies)**
	- **Built:** 1870
	- **Description:** A center for the study of classical languages, archology and ancient civilizations, this facility hosts a comprehensive collection of rare texts and artifacts, fostering academic excellence in classical studies.
- **J. W. Midnight Library**
	- **Built:** 1955
	- **Description:** The campus library offers extensive resources for students, including rare books, archives, and study spaces. Librarians are available to assist students in their academic pursuits. Library science courses are offered in basement levels 1 and 2.
- **Sister Sarah’s Teaching Hospital**
	- **Built:** 1927
	- **Description:** A teaching hospital providing top-notch medical services to the campus and community, as well as training opportunities for healthcare students in clinical settings. It offers coursework in pre-med as well as provide facilities for biological labs.
- **Applied Health and Nursing Center**
	- **Built:** 1966
	- **Description:** The **Applied Health and Nursing Center** is a modern, multi-story facility that serves as the hub for Caroline College’s nursing and health education programs. Equipped with state-of-the-art simulation labs, clinical classrooms, and research spaces, the center provides hands-on training for students pursuing careers in healthcare. Its proximity to Watashuka’s teaching hospital ensures a seamless integration of academic learning with real-world clinical experience, preparing students for immediate entry into the healthcare field.
- **St. John's Lutheran Chapel**
	- **Built:** 1890
	- **Description:** The oldest Lutheran chapel on a public college campus in the region, St. John’s offers classes in religious studies and serves the spiritual needs of the student body. Graduate work in comparative religion and philosophy is offered here.
- **[WCTU](WCTU Radio Station)**
	- **Overview:** The campus radio station at Caroline College. It is housed in the **McElhenney Journalism School**.  The station is run by a mix of students and fulltime staff. Fulltime staff includes:
		- **Michelina Plum**, who hosts the late-night show "Night Vibes." from 10:00pm to 5:00 am. The show focuses on classical musical to sleep and study to.
		- Albert Hawkins, who hosts the early morning news and Americana program "News and Roots" from 5:00 am to noon.
	- [WCTU AM Radio (Public Radio On The Campus Of Caroline College)](https://www.youtube.com/channel/UCEfcVULpxQaQyBZCcSVTwtQ)

20. **Our Earth Group**
    - **Skills**: Biology, Survival
    - **Story Hooks**: Protecting local environments leads to strange discoveries; nature behaving unpredictably.
**Keeper's Note**: Involvement in clubs can provide:
- **Skill Bonuses**: Gain a +5% bonus to associated skills while active in the club.
- **Story Opportunities**: Clubs can introduce unique quests, NPCs, and resources.
- **Potential Risks**: *Groups can grant mechanical benefits as well as possible contacts. But some clubs may be fronts for groups your character may not wish to draw attention from.*

---
title: About Caroline College
draft: false
publish: true
tags:
  - TTRPG
  - Horror
---
**Welcome to Caroline College: Rooted in Tradition, Driven by Innovation**
Founded in 1856 as Prairieville Academy, Caroline College has been at the heart of Wisconsin's frontier history for over a century. Located in the picturesque town of [[Watashuka]], nestled between rolling hills and just a short drive from Lake Geneva, our campus offers the perfect blend of historic charm and cutting-edge facilities. We honor our heritage while embracing the future—just as the founders of Prairieville Academy envisioned.
**Go Prairie Dogs!** At Caroline College, we take great pride in our mascot, the Prairie Dog. Just like our tenacious mascot, our students are known for their resilience, teamwork, and school spirit. Whether you're cheering on our teams at Prairie Dog Stadium or collaborating with classmates on a project, you'll feel the energy and camaraderie that define Caroline College.
**Academic Excellence Meets Technological Advancement** While we celebrate our rich frontier past, Caroline College is home to modern, world-class facilities. Our **Qubit Tower**, housing two of the most powerful supercomputers in the Midwest, stands as a testament to our commitment to cutting-edge research and technological innovation. In addition, our **Brown Science Complex**, including the **Castelaz Building and Observatory** and the **Luttermoser Science Hall**, equips students in the physical, biological, and chemical sciences with the tools they need to thrive in their fields. Whether you're stargazing at the Wright Telescope or conducting hands-on experiments, Caroline College is a hub for discovery.
**Spiritual Legacy** Though no longer a religious institution, Caroline College remains deeply tied to its spiritual roots. The school’s founding as a religious teaching academy continues to shape our values and traditions. Our campus reflects this legacy, fostering an atmosphere of intellectual curiosity and ethical reflection, grounded in our shared history.
**A Scenic and Connected Campus** Our idyllic campus combines serene, tree-lined walkways with modern conveniences, offering students the best of both worlds. Located just 100 miles from Chicago and 60 miles from Milwaukee, Caroline College provides access to vibrant city life while offering a peaceful, focused environment for learning and personal growth.
**Join Us at Caroline College** At Caroline College, tradition meets innovation. We invite you to become part of a proud legacy that began with Prairieville Academy and continues today with unmatched academic opportunities, a vibrant campus life, and a commitment to student success.
Explore Caroline College, where you’ll find your place in history and your path to the future. Go Prairie Dogs!

---
title: Prairie Hall-Secrets
draft: true
publish: false
tags:
  - TTRPG
  - Horror
---
# Keeper Version
**Truth Behind the Legend:** While many believe Prairie Hall may be a reconstruction, it is, in fact, the original building, saved through unexplained means during the destruction of Prairieville Academy in 1860. The truth behind the event is linked to an occult ritual that went awry, resulting in the deaths of most of the academy’s founders. Only Eleazar Root and John W. Sterling survived. They rebuilt the school but buried the darker parts of their history. The public story that the building was saved is a carefully crafted lie.
**Basements:** The first two basement levels are part of the museum, as players might expect. However, deeper below lies a third and fourth level, dug out in the 1930s under the guise of expanding storage. These lower levels house documents and artifacts that hint at the occult origins of the academy, including cryptic texts, old ritual tools, and records of the supernatural events surrounding the academy's early days.
The **fourth basement** is particularly well-guarded, constructed with reinforced steel walls thicker than most bomb shelters. This floor is sealed, locked behind layers of security systems. Inside are disturbing remnants of past experiments carried out by the college in the 1930s. These secret records confirm the existence of ancient cults that have influenced Caroline College since its inception. Evidence of the college’s involvement in dark rituals, including summoning practices, are hidden away, never meant to see the light of day.
**Dave’s Claim:** As mentioned in the broadcasts of _Metal at Midnight_, Dave believes that dark secrets are buried beneath Prairie Hall. While many dismiss his claims, he is unknowingly close to the truth. The fourth basement holds proof of occult rituals conducted by past members of the academy, along with records of darker, hidden events that have shaped the town. Dave’s belief that these documents could expose something sinister is entirely accurate, though no one has dared to investigate further.

title: Prairie Hall
draft: false
publish: true
tags:

  - Horror

# Overview
![[Prairie Hall with the Qubit Tower in the background.png]]
*Prairie Hall with the Qubit Tower in the background.*
Prairie Hall is a small, historical log cabin located at the heart of [[Caroline College|Caroline College]] campus. Originally built in 1856 as part of Prairieville Academy, it holds the distinction of being the first permanent structure associated with the college. Over the years, it has served various functions but is now preserved as a museum celebrating the early history of the school and the surrounding region.
The building is 20' x 12' and features simple, frontier-style construction with logs and a stone chimney. Inside, visitors will find artifacts from the 19th century, including tools, books, and furnishings that reflect early Wisconsin pioneer life. The museum provides a glimpse into the lives of the school’s founders and the region’s history. Below the cabin, two basement levels house additional exhibits and storage, where older records and artifacts are carefully maintained for educational purposes.
The Prairie Hall Museum is a favorite among history majors and tourists alike, offering a quiet retreat from the busier parts of campus. Some students debate whether the current building is the original cabin or a reconstruction following its near destruction during the 1860 conflict that devastated the academy. While it’s a topic of discussion, no official documents confirm either theory.

# Keeper Version
While [[WCTU]] appears to be a typical college radio station, it harbors a darker purpose. Some of its broadcasts, especially during the late-night shifts, carry hidden occult messages. These messages, usually masked by the music or obscured by garbled signals, often serve as instructions for cult members or warnings for impending rituals. Certain broadcasts can trigger mild time distortions or altered states of consciousness in listeners.
- **Location**: The cramped basement of the McElhenney Journalism School is an ideal spot for covert activities. Its labyrinth of storage rooms and soundproofed walls make it perfect for cult meetings, occult rituals, and other secretive actions without drawing attention from the broader campus.
- **Cult Influence**: The station is influenced by _The Brotherhood of the Gate Unveiled_, a cult that seeks to manipulate time and space. Michelina Plum’s "Night Vibes" is known to have a hypnotic effect on listeners, occasionally allowing subtle time manipulations or even moments of déjà vu in those who regularly tune in.
- **Disappearing DJs**: Several DJs, particularly those working the night shift, have mysteriously vanished over the years. The local authorities attribute these disappearances to accidents or students running away, but in truth, these individuals often stumbled too close to the station’s secret purpose and were silenced by the cult.
- **Hidden Broadcasts**: Occasionally, WCTU picks up strange signals late at night—cryptic voices, eerie sounds, or broadcasts that seem to originate from other times. Some of these signals are accidental, while others are deliberate messages sent by cultists to guide or summon members.
- **Game Hooks**:
    - A DJ disappears after a late-night broadcast, and their last words over the airwaves were cryptic and unsettling, leading the players to investigate.
    - The players receive a strange transmission while listening to WCTU, full of static and distorted voices, giving them clues to the next stage of their investigation.
    - Old WCTU broadcasts contain secret messages pointing to occult rituals and locations hidden within the town of Watashuka.
By day, WCTU is a quirky, student-run station, but by night, it becomes a subtle tool of occult manipulation, with its signals influencing the town and its students in dangerous ways.
### **Notes on Replacements (Past 12 Months)**
1. **Sam Lang** (host of "Lunch Break Jams") – _Disappeared in March 1983_
2. **Ron Sterling** (host of "Golden Oldies") – _Vanished in July 1983_
3. **Mark Philips** (host of "Soundtrack Saturdays/Sundays") – _Missing since February 1983_
4. **Melissa Young** (host of "Mystery Hour") – _Disappeared in May 1983_
5. **Amy Lewis** (host of "Underground Echoes") – _Last seen in November 1982_
These disappearances are especially concerning for those hosting late-night or isolated shows, with many speculating on the link between their vanishing and the occult activities rumored to be connected to the station.

# Overview
![[WCTU Studio.png]]
WCTU is the student-run radio station of [[Caroline College]], broadcasting on AM radio. Its slogan, "*The Heartbeat of Watashuka*," highlights its connection to the campus and the surrounding community. WCTU features a wide range of shows, from music to talk radio, often showcasing indie bands and student discussions. The station is a popular place for college students to unwind, either by tuning in or by participating as DJs.
- **Location**: Housed in the basement of the McElhenney Journalism School, the WCTU studio is small, cluttered, and packed with old records, tapes, and broadcasting equipment. The walls are lined with posters of bands and events, creating a vibrant yet somewhat chaotic atmosphere. The station operates 24/7, with students rotating shifts.
- **Popular Programs**:
    - **"Night Vibes"**: A late-night show hosted by [[Michelina Plum]] that plays classical and ambient music, providing a calm, relaxing soundtrack for late-night studying or sleep.
    - **"News and Roots"**: A morning show hosted by Albert Hawkins, blending local news, weather, and folk music. It's a favorite for students and early risers who prefer a mellow start to their day.
    - **"College Chaos"**: A high-energy, student-hosted talk show featuring the latest in college gossip, pranks, and music. It’s often the go-to for Caroline College students looking to blow off steam.

title: Dr. Amy Mann

### **Dr. Amy Mann (Ph.D. Physicist, Government Operative)**
![[Dr. Amy Mann ID Photo.jpg]]
- **Background**: Dr. Amy Mann is a prodigy, having completed her doctorate in temporal physics by the age of 21. Recruited by the _Office of Technological Assessment (OTA)_ right out of graduate school, she has been sent to Watashuka under the guise of a faculty member at Caroline College. Her groundbreaking research on time manipulation is of great interest to Project Caroline, which seeks to exploit the ley lines for military use. Unbeknownst to her, Amy's work is directly tied to the eldritch forces lurking beneath the town.
- **Age**: 23 (1983)
- **Appearance**: Amy's striking presence is one of grace and intelligence. She has delicate yet determined features: fair skin with a soft glow, large expressive blue-green eyes framed by long lashes, and golden-blonde hair that cascades in soft waves. Despite her brilliance, she maintains an air of innocence and naivety about the world beyond academia. Amy often dresses in professional yet understated attire, favoring dark, minimalist outfits with sharp collars, as if her clothing reflects the precision of her scientific mind.
- **Personality**: While exceptionally intelligent and focused, Amy is quiet and introspective, preferring the company of her research over socializing. She tends to be reserved, avoiding unnecessary attention, but is passionate about solving the mysteries of time and the universe. Her curiosity is both her greatest strength and her undoing, as it leads her deeper into the occult forces she doesn’t fully comprehend. Despite her genius, in 1983, she has a vulnerable side—being so young, Amy is still somewhat naïve about the political and supernatural machinations surrounding her.
- **Connections**:    
    - Project Caroline: Amy was recruited by the OTA to work on secretive government experiments tied to time manipulation and the ley lines beneath Watashuka. Her research is invaluable to the project, though she is unaware of the true extent of the eldritch entities that influence both her work and the town.
- **Fate**: Amy disappears on **August 29, 1983**, after witnessing a ritual by Church of the Delayed Blossom. Her disappearance is the catalyst for the time loop that resets the town’s reality every few years. In each cycle, Amy’s fate is sealed—whether she is killed, pulled into another dimension, or sacrificed. She unknowingly serves as the **temporal anchor** for the loop, her life and death entwined with the supernatural forces at play.
- **Role in the Time Loop**: As the anchor, Amy is crucial to breaking the loop. Players may encounter echoes of her throughout different cycles, or even uncover fragmented memories she has left behind in the form of notes, messages, or recorded experiments. If they can save her or prevent her disappearance, they might find a way to disrupt the cycle—though doing so may unleash even greater dangers.
- **Potential Hooks for Investigators**:    
    - **Missing Person**: Investigators can be drawn into the mystery by following leads related to her disappearance, piecing together her connection to Project Caroline and the cults.
    - **Personal Journals**: Amy’s research journals, scattered throughout Watashuka, contain clues not only to her scientific work but also to the rituals and cults operating around her. Some pages may hold cryptic notes that reveal her growing awareness of the loop.
    - **Visions and Dreams**: Amy may appear to players in dreams, fragmented across time, desperately trying to warn them about what’s to come. These visions often carry a sense of urgency but are incomplete, leaving the players to fill in the blanks.
- **Final Goal**: Breaking the time loop requires either rescuing Amy from her fate or successfully completing the temporal experiments that trapped the town in the first place. However, even if she is saved, the eldritch horrors may still find a way to break through the fabric of reality.
	- If the cults ever break free from the time loop and are able to complete their ritual, which must happen on 23 Feb 1987, just as a new light source in the Large Magellanic Cloud (LMC) reaches Earth, they will awaken their 'original god'. What they do not understand is that this 'original god', Cthulhu, will, as a first act, wipe out all of the cults... then the region, then the world.
	- This happened in at least two iterations of the time loop
		- Amy initiated the time loop on purpose to stop such an event with the hope that she and her team could disrupt the ritual from ever being able to be completed. Unfortunately, her presence at a major cult ritual became the anchor for one end of the loop; her initiating it became the other. She is stuck at the two ends of the loop unable to warning anyone about the dangers our the consequence of failure. 
	- Each iteration of the time loop shuffles the initial conditions and as such people, places and events may change. But each campaign starts with a ritual that Amy is present for, and her disappearance shortly after that. If Amy's disappearance could be stopped, the time loop is broken. But the players would still have only a few years to stop the final ritual.

title: Dr. Daniel J. Stanton - Keeper Notes
draft: true
publish: false
tags:

  - Horror

**[[Dr. Daniel J. Stanton]]**  
**President of Caroline College (1974-Present)**  
**Class of 1937**
**Physical Description**: Dr. Stanton is a tall man, standing around 6'2", with silvering hair slicked back in an old-fashioned style. He has a robust build but carries himself with the stiff, formal posture of someone used to authority. His dark suits are always tailored, emphasizing his wealth and status. His hands are frequently adorned with gold rings, and his confident, almost smirking expression hides the ambition that drives him.
Dr. Stanton's rise to the presidency of Caroline College in 1974 was orchestrated by the **[[Church of the Delayed Blossom]]** as part of a larger strategy to eliminate government interference, particularly Project Caroline, from the campus. This move coincided with the Nixon administration’s decision to withdraw the project, a victory for the cult and a step forward in their manipulation of the college.
Stanton himself is not a cultist but has become a convenient puppet for the Church. His obsession with wealth and fame makes him easy to manipulate. He despises big government, despite the fact that his entire fortune is rooted in post-war contracts and lucrative deals with government agencies during the economic boom. Stanton’s import business after WWII, which involved Asian markets, helped him accumulate vast wealth, largely due to questionable dealings, though he publicly spins this as his contribution to the war effort.
**Cult Handler**: **Margaret "Maggie" Laurent**  
Margaret Laurent, posing as a senior faculty member in the business department, is Stanton’s handler within the Church of the Delayed Blossom. A high-ranking cult member, Maggie has been placed strategically close to Stanton, feeding him suggestions and using flattery and promises of fame to keep him on the path the cult desires. She interacts with him subtly, using faculty meetings, casual dinners, and business advice to maintain her influence without raising suspicion. Maggie is adept at framing her manipulations as if they align with Stanton’s personal ambitions, ensuring that he remains unaware of her true motives.
**World War II Role**: Stanton did not serve in the war but instead profited from it, establishing lucrative import contracts and expanding his business empire under the guise of contributing to post-war recovery. This narrative has been spun into a tale of patriotic duty, allowing Stanton to position himself as a supporter of the war effort despite his opportunistic profiteering.
**Personality**: Stanton is driven by personal ambition. Though he is competent at managing the college, his real interest lies in furthering his own reputation and amassing more wealth. The cult knows this and uses it to their advantage, keeping him focused on business expansions and financial growth rather than delving too deeply into the college’s darker undercurrents. He let's people believe that he is too humble to put on his CV the name of the university he got his honorary doctorate from; preferring them to assume it was Harvard or MIT. It was Miskatonic. And it was part of business business bribe engineered but the Church of the Delayed Blossom. It is also more than passingly racist against people of Asian heritage. 
**Influence by the Cult**: Stanton's anti-government stance, though seemingly personal, is shaped by the Church of the Delayed Blossom. They use his paranoia about big government to keep him aligned with their goals, particularly the removal of any remaining government presence at Caroline College.

**Dr. Daniel J. Stanton**  
**President, Caroline College**  
**Class of 1937**
![[Dr. Daniel J. Stanton.png]]
Dr. Daniel J. Stanton has been the president of [[Caroline College]] since 1974. A proud alumnus, Dr. Stanton returned to his alma mater to lead the college into a new era of growth and innovation. Under his leadership, Caroline College has expanded its programs, modernized its facilities, and strengthened its ties with the local community. His contributions to the college’s advancements include the development of the **Philip Love Aquatic Center**.
Dr. Stanton earned his doctorate in internal business affairs, building on his successful career in international trade and commerce. He holds and honorary doctorate in education from a major university in Massachusetts.  After World War II, he established a thriving import business, focusing on Asian markets, which supported post-war economic recovery efforts. Through his business acumen, Dr. Stanton has made significant contributions to both the educational and business worlds, and his leadership has helped Caroline College rise to new heights.
Known for his charismatic leadership style and business expertise, Dr. Stanton is a vocal proponent of small government, believing in the power of private enterprise and individual initiative. His commitment to both the college and the greater [[Watashuka]] community reflects his deep sense of duty and dedication to education.

title: Katherine Coates-Secrets

[[Katherine Coates]]
**Role/Title:**  
Head of the Journalism Department at Caroline College, Faculty Advisor for _The Crier_  
Unwitting protector of the college’s secrets, blind to the supernatural forces at play
**Description:**  
Professor Katherine Coates is an idealist at heart, believing that journalism can be a force for good in the world. However, her idealism has left her with significant blind spots. Katherine is completely unaware of the darker forces at work within [[Caroline College]] and [[Watashuka]]. She suspects there is some level of governmental corruption on campus—perhaps linked to outdated funding agreements with the now-defunct [[Watashuka Initiative]] —but she dismisses any talk of supernatural occurrences or secret experiments as conspiracy theories.
**Her Role in the Cover-Up:**  
In her attempts to protect the integrity of the journalism department, Katherine has inadvertently contributed to the very problems she’s trying to solve. She is particularly frustrated by the ongoing pirate radio broadcasts from **[[WCTU]]**, which she sees as a blemish on the college’s reputation. Katherine has gone so far as to deny the existence of these broadcasts to administrators, assuming they are nothing more than rebellious pranks. In doing so, she has unknowingly shielded some of the college’s more dangerous underground activities, including the cult presence tied to [[Brotherhood of the Gate Unveiled|The Brotherhood of the Gate Unveiled]]**.
**Blind to the Truth:**  
Katherine believes that any problems at Caroline College are purely bureaucratic or financial in nature. She’s convinced that her investigative efforts will uncover corruption, but she has no concept of the supernatural forces manipulating events on campus. Her investigation into **[[Project Caroline]]** has been surface-level, focusing on financial records and outdated military contracts rather than the eldritch experiments that the project was truly built upon. Her resistance to the idea of anything beyond governmental corruption makes her an unwitting obstacle for those trying to uncover the truth.
**Potential Hooks for Investigators:**
- **A Barrier to Progress:** Katherine’s insistence on dismissing pirate broadcasts and rumors about supernatural events could make her an obstacle for investigators. If the investigators attempt to expose the truth about the college’s hidden dangers, they may need to convince Katherine to abandon her idealistic but limited worldview.
- **A Potential Ally:** Despite her blindness to the supernatural, Katherine is highly principled and could become a powerful ally if convinced of the true depth of the corruption. Investigators may need to present her with concrete evidence that her suspicions about the college are just the tip of the iceberg, showing her how her efforts to cover up certain activities are playing into a larger conspiracy.
- **Access to Records:** Katherine’s position as head of the Journalism Department and her interest in archival research give her access to valuable information about the college’s history. Investigators who gain her trust could use this access to uncover hidden details about **Project Caroline** and other dark elements of Watashuka’s past.
**Hobbies and Interests:**
- **Literature and Philosophy:** Katherine spends much of her free time reading literature and philosophical texts, particularly works on ethics and truth. She is a fan of **George Orwell** and **Hannah Arendt**, authors whose works focus on corruption and totalitarianism, though she remains unaware of how her own actions mirror some of the behaviors she critiques.
- **Archival Research:** Katherine enjoys combing through historical records, both for academic purposes and to give her students access to valuable sources. However, she tends to view this research through a narrow lens, focusing on financial and administrative corruption rather than the broader, more dangerous forces at play in Watashuka.
- **Nature Walks:** Katherine often takes long walks in Watashuka’s parks and nearby woodlands, using these moments of solitude to reflect on her work and her students. Though she enjoys the peace of nature, she sometimes feels uneasy when walking alone, as if she’s being watched. She attributes this discomfort to the stress of her job.
**Public Perception:**  
To most of the college’s staff and students, Katherine is a serious but approachable figure, someone who holds herself to high ethical standards and expects the same from those around her. While her attempts to quash the pirate broadcasts have frustrated some of the more rebellious students, her dedication to investigative journalism has earned her respect on campus. However, those who have worked with her closely may notice that her desire to protect the journalism department’s reputation sometimes causes her to overlook uncomfortable truths.

## Older
# **Professor Katherine Coates (Head of Journalism at Caroline College, Idealist with Blind Spots)**
- **Role**: Professor Katherine Coates is the head of the _Journalism Department_ at _[Caroline College](Caroline%20College.md)_, where she also serves as the faculty advisor for _The Crier_, the college’s student-run newspaper. A passionate idealist, Katherine believes deeply in the power of journalism to expose corruption and hold institutions accountable. She suspects that some level of governmental corruption is affecting the college, but she remains unaware of the true depth of the government’s activities on campus. She assumes that _[Project Caroline](Project%20Caroline.md)_ ended long ago and dismisses rumors of ongoing secretive experiments or cult involvement as unfounded conspiracy theories. Ironically, by attempting to protect the integrity of the department and her own reputation, she has unknowingly become a part of the problem—often covering up the existence of the pirate radio station broadcasts from _WCTU_ out of embarrassment, further distancing herself from the truth she so desperately seeks.
- **Age**: Mid-30s (1983)
- **Appearance**: Katherine Coates has a distinctive look that matches her intellectual nature. She has short, curly dark hair, wears large round glasses, and often dresses in practical, slightly vintage-style clothing, favoring patterned blouses and cardigans. Her appearance suggests someone deeply engaged in academic life—focused on ideas rather than appearances. Her calm, serious expression reflects her constant state of thought and introspection. She exudes an unassuming air, and while she might seem approachable to students, there’s an underlying intensity to her idealism.
- **Personality**: Katherine is driven by a strong sense of justice and believes in the ethical power of journalism. She pushes her students at _Caroline College_ to investigate stories that expose corruption, inspire change, and give voice to the voiceless. However, her idealism often blinds her to the deeper and more dangerous forces at play in [Watashuka](Watashuka.md). She is particularly frustrated by the _pirate radio broadcasts_ that come out of WCTU, seeing them as a stain on the journalism department's reputation. To maintain her pride, she has begun downplaying or outright denying their existence, not realizing that in doing so, she’s becoming a source of misinformation—exactly what she despises in others. Katherine’s desire to protect her department’s image overrides her instincts, causing her to miss key clues about the strange occurrences happening around campus and the town.
- **Public Role**:
    - **Head of Journalism Department**: Katherine runs the journalism department with an iron focus on ethics and investigation, encouraging her students to dig deep and challenge authority where necessary. Under her guidance, _The Crier_ has earned a reputation for hard-hitting journalism—at least within the confines of campus life. She is proud of the work the students produce and fiercely defends the department’s reputation from internal and external criticism.
    - **Overseeing WCTU**: As the faculty advisor responsible for the campus radio station, Katherine is particularly frustrated by the ongoing pirate radio broadcasts. These underground shows have become a thorn in her side. Katherine has made several attempts to silence the broadcasts, believing them to be nothing more than juvenile acts of rebellion. In her attempts to suppress the problem, however, she inadvertently mirrors the authoritarian tendencies she loathes in corrupt governments, often denying to administrators and others that the pirate broadcasts even exist.
- **Investigating Corruption**: Katherine suspects that something is not right at Caroline College, but her investigations into this suspected corruption remain shallow. She assumes the problems are merely governmental—perhaps related to funding mismanagement or outdated agreements with former military projects. She doesn’t yet understand that the forces she’s up against are far more dangerous and intertwined with occult activities happening under the radar. Her belief that the _Project Caroline_ experiments ended long ago has left her unprepared for the deeper horrors at play.
- **Interaction with Watashuka**:
    - **Interactions with Students**: Katherine is deeply involved in the lives of her students, often acting as a mentor and role model. She encourages them to pursue truth, even when it’s uncomfortable, and her open-door policy makes her popular among those in the journalism department. However, her idealism sometimes causes friction with students who are more interested in sensationalism or entertainment. She sees herself as a protector of the journalistic craft, which can put her at odds with those who view journalism as more of a business or career than a calling.
    - **Tension with [Dave](Dave.md)**: Katherine is very vocal about her disdain for Dave and his pirate broadcasts. She sees him as reckless and irresponsible, a figure who undermines the integrity of the journalism program. This tension has created a somewhat adversarial relationship between her and the [Metalheads](Metalheads.md) community, though she remains unaware of the depth of their involvement in the town’s supernatural struggles.
    - **Covering for WCTU**: In her attempts to protect the department’s image, Katherine has gone as far as to deny the existence of the pirate broadcasts to other college administrators, claiming that any complaints about the broadcasts are baseless. She believes that by quashing the controversy, she is protecting the reputation of the journalism program. This puts her in the uncomfortable position of inadvertently spreading misinformation—a role she would detest if she realized the full extent of her actions.
- **Hobbies and Interests**:
    - **Literature and Philosophy**: Outside of her work at the college, Katherine is an avid reader of both classic literature and philosophical works. She spends much of her free time studying texts on ethics, truth, and justice, often incorporating these ideas into her lectures. She particularly admires figures like _Hannah Arendt_ and _George Orwell_, authors whose works focus on the dangers of corruption and totalitarianism—though she is blind to how some of these critiques may apply to her own behavior.
    - **Archival Research**: Katherine enjoys sifting through historical records and archives, both for personal interest and to find stories for her students. This hobby, however, is more academic than investigative; while she uncovers interesting facts about the town and its history, she doesn’t delve deep enough to see the larger, darker forces at work.
    - **Walking in Nature**: Katherine often takes long walks through Watashuka’s parks and nearby woodlands, enjoying the quiet solitude. These walks allow her to clear her mind and reflect on her work, though she often feels uneasy when alone in the woods—an unexplained discomfort she tends to dismiss as stress.
- **Potential Hooks for Investigators**:
    - **Unintentional Obstacle**: Katherine could become an unintentional obstacle to investigators trying to expose the truth about Watashuka’s supernatural undercurrents. Her efforts to cover up pirate broadcasts or downplay student rumors could mislead investigators or slow their progress, as she inadvertently shields the deeper corruption she hasn’t yet uncovered.
    - **A Source of Information**: Once her trust is earned, Katherine could be a valuable ally, especially given her knowledge of journalism, ethics, and corruption. Her access to historical records and her academic connections could help investigators piece together parts of the mystery. However, convincing her of the supernatural truth will be a significant challenge, as she’s resistant to accepting anything outside of rational, governmental corruption.
    - **Potential for Growth**: As events in Watashuka escalate, Katherine’s idealism could either become a strength or lead to her downfall. Investigators might have the chance to push her to open her eyes to the deeper, more sinister forces at play, or they might find themselves working around her if she stubbornly refuses to see beyond her own preconceptions.
- **Public Perception**: Katherine is respected as a dedicated and principled educator, though some find her overly idealistic and occasionally rigid in her views. Her clashes with the _Metalhead_ community and her attempts to silence pirate broadcasts have created a divide between her and the younger, more rebellious students. Despite this, she is seen as a champion of journalistic integrity, someone who holds herself and her students to high ethical standards, even if that means stepping on a few toes in the process.

![[Professor Katherine Coates.png]]
# **Professor Katherine Coates**
*In a cluttered office filled with stacks of newspapers and journalism textbooks, a woman is angry; very angry. She sits at her desk, tapping her pencil against a file of student stories. Her short, curly hair bounces slightly as she leans forward to read an article submission more closely. "This needs more depth," she mutters to herself before scribbling notes in the margins. She pushes her glasses up the bridge of her nose and looks out the window. She is fuming. She's going to reject this article for the Crier. She knows it. She also knows its wrong. "Not enough reference material. No interviews. Topic is not worth exploring further." Stacy is a good student and she'll be hurt that her article was rejected for unfair reasons but she'll get over it. She'll rise above it.*
*Coates puts the marked up document in her out box. The title "What Happens On Campus After Midnight?" can be seen sticking out. The professor turns on the campus radio and calms down. "College Chaos". Right show, right time. No interruptions.*
**Role/Title:**  
Head of the Journalism Department at Caroline College, Faculty Advisor for _The Crier_ (student newspaper)
**Description:**  
Professor Katherine Coates is the head of the Journalism Department at [[Caroline College]], where she teaches investigative journalism and ethics. Known for her no-nonsense approach to journalism, Katherine is deeply passionate about the role of the press in society and its potential to expose corruption and inspire change. Her idealism and dedication to journalistic integrity make her a well-respected figure among students, though some find her methods rigid. Katherine also serves as the faculty advisor for _The Crier_, the college’s student-run newspaper, where she pushes students to dig deeper and challenge the status quo.

title: Michelina Plum-Secrets
draft: true
publish: false
tags:
  - TTRPG
  - Horror
---
[[Michelina Plum]]
- **Age**: 36 (in 1983)
- **Role**: While Michelina Plum presents a composed and conservative image on the air, her private life tells a different story. Behind the scenes, she leads a secretive, decadent lifestyle filled with alcohol, swinging, and hidden vices that are in stark contrast to her public persona. She graduated from the **University of Wisconsin-Madison** in 1980 and quickly secured her position in [[Watashuka]], where she’s been hiding her more personal secrets ever since. Despite her conservative leanings, her personal life is filled with vices and secrets, which she works hard to keep hidden from the public eye.
- **Disturbing Calls**: Since early **1982**, Michelina has been receiving eerie, anonymous phone calls at **2:15 a.m.** during her broadcasts. The caller speaks in a strange, guttural language that unsettles her deeply. While Michelina initially assumed it was a prank, and assumes that the person was speaking Arabic, the reality is far more sinister—the language is mythos in origin. These calls have left her paranoid and frightened, and despite reporting them to **[[Jan Ducochik|Sgt. Jan Ducochik]]**, no leads have been uncovered.
- **Hidden Connections**:
    - **Captain Bernard Miller**: Michelina is one of the few people in town who knows the truth about **[[Bernard Miller|Captain Bernard Miller]]** and his trips to Milwaukee. She has accompanied him on some of these trips, though whether out of camaraderie or shared secrets remains unclear. Their relationship is built on mutual understanding and the protection of each other’s reputations.
    - **[[Mothers Opposing MetalMothers Opposing Metal (MOM)]]**: Michelina uses her role in **MOM** to reinforce her conservative image, though she has little genuine interest in the group’s moral crusades. Her participation is primarily to distract from her own behavior, helping her maintain her façade while hiding her true lifestyle.
    - [[Dave]]: Her hatred for Dave is so great that she has, jokingly, said she should put a hit on him. It is only jokingly for now, but if escalated, Michelina is not above blackmailing Miller to see that Dave is taken out of the picture.
- **Personality**: Michelina is a master at maintaining her double life. To the public, she is a composed and calming presence, projecting conservative values and a love for order. In private, however, she is deeply conflicted, constantly balancing her public image with her hidden vices. She uses alcohol to cope with the stress of her double life, and while she is highly political, her actions often conflict with the values she preaches.
- **Potential Hooks for Investigators**:
    - **The 2:15 A.M. Calls**: Investigators may be drawn into Michelina’s world through the anonymous calls she receives during her broadcasts. These mythos-origin calls could provide a clue to the supernatural forces at play in Watashuka.
    - **Double Life**: Michelina’s hidden lifestyle is filled with secrets that could unravel her public image. Players investigating her background could uncover her connection to **Captain Bernard Miller** or her hidden vices, which may tie into larger town secrets.
    - **MOM Involvement**: As a vocal member of **Mothers Opposing Metal**, Michelina has influence in town, especially among conservative residents. Investigators might use her role in the group to sway public opinion or gain information, though her volatile personality makes her a tricky ally.
- **Public vs. Private**: Michelina is deeply invested in keeping her private life hidden. Any revelations about her double life could destroy her reputation and lead her to drastic actions, making her both a potential ally and a threat to investigators.

![[Michelina Plum.png]]
# **Michelina Plum**
- **Age**: 36 (in 1983)
- **Role**: Michelina Plum is the sultry host of _Night Vibes_, a late-night radio show on **[[WCTU]]**, Watashuka’s college radio station. Her program, running from **10:00 p.m. to 5:00 a.m.**, features soothing instrumental music and classical tracks aimed at helping her listeners relax during the long, quiet hours of the night. Michelina’s smooth, calming voice has earned her a dedicated following, particularly among students and night-shift workers.
- **Appearance**: Michelina is an attractive woman with striking red hair that falls in loose waves around her shoulders. She has sharp features and bright green eyes that stand out against her glamorous, if somewhat disheveled, appearance. Often dressed in silky, low-cut blouses, she exudes an air of confidence and mystery, especially when she’s behind the microphone. On air, Michelina’s polished, professional persona is in contrast to the sharp, more intense side of her character that only those close to her see.
- **Personality**: On the radio, Michelina is known for her calm, reassuring tone, a voice that seems to ease the worries of her late-night listeners. Off-air, however, she is a different person entirely—witty, foul-mouthed, and with a sharp sense of humor. Michelina is highly political, frequently expressing her admiration for President Reagan and her disdain for the local counterculture. 
- **Public Role**:
    - **WCTU Radio Host**: Michelina is well-known in the community for her late-night radio show, which provides a soothing soundtrack to the town’s quieter hours. She is regarded as an intellectual and a voice of reason, offering a space for Watashuka’s insomniacs, students, and night workers to find comfort in the music she plays.
    - **[[Mothers Opposing Metal-Keeper|Mothers Opposing Metal (MOM)]]**: Michelina is a vocal member of **Mothers Opposing Metal**, a conservative group that fights against the influence of heavy metal music and other perceived corruptions of youth. She frequently speaks out against the local pirate radio DJ, **Dave**, and the **Metalheads**, blaming them for the town’s moral decline.
- **Public Perception**: Most people in [[Watashuka]] see Michelina as a respected, conservative figure who upholds traditional values and provides a calming presence through her radio show. She is known for her intelligence and her involvement in **MOM**, which reinforces her image as a defender of the town’s moral standards. Her sharp political views and vocal support for Reagan resonate with many of the town’s conservative residents, though there are whispers about her hidden wild side from those who know her better.

---
title: History of Watashuka
draft: false
publish: true
tags:
  - TTRPG
  - Horror
---
# **History of [[Watashuka]]**
- **May 1856** – Founding of **Prairieville Academy**
	- **Prairieville Academy** is established as a teacher-training school (normal school) to educate future educators. The academy becomes the heart of the town of Prairieville, which later becomes Watashuka. The academy was the dream of three educators Walter Mann, Eleazar Root and John W. Sterling. There dream was to work with the local Ho-Chunk people to bring forth a new era for the region. That dream is still alive today despite setbacks. 
	- **Founding Members**
		- Walter Mann: German immigrant, artist, head founder of the academy
		- Eleazar Root: Co-founder. Massachusetts school teacher, relocated
		- John W. Sterling: Co-founder, English businessman, relocated 
		- Elias Haskins: Co-founder, local prominent cavalrymen
		- Jonathan Whitmore: Co-founder, local esteemed teacher and theologian
		- Sarah Johnson: Co-founder, local wealthy widow and philanthropist
- **August 1860** – Destruction of **Prairieville Academy**
	- The academy is destroyed during a violent conflict between the settlers and a rogue native tribe who attacked the school. During the attack many of the educators and founders were killed; only Eleazar Root and John Sterling survived. The academy burned down. Many blame local tensions with indigenous people on the attack. Most records from this time are lost, and it remains a tragic, but poorly understood, event in local history.
- **September 1862** – Rebuilding of **Prairieville School**
	- In the wake of the academy’s destruction, the **Prairieville School** is built to continue the region’s educational mission. Under the leadership of Eleazar Root and John W. Sterling the school thrives and grows as part of the effort to revitalize education in the region, attracting settlers to the area. Eleazar served as the school's first principal while John provided the financial and political support.
- **Blizzard of 1888 - Humanitarian Aid**
	- After the [[Blizzard of 1888]], large numbers of members of the [[Lutheran Church]] immigrate to the region. The first settlers arrive to provide humanitarian assistance but soon took to calling the region home.
- **April 1895** – **Caroline Religious Teaching College** Founded
	- Due to the influence of Lutheran immigrants, the **Caroline Religious Teaching College** is established, expanding the former school into a larger institution focused on religious education. This school subsumed the Prairieville School and most agree that this was more of a renaming than a new school. 
	- At the same time, the town of **Prairieville** is renamed **Watashuka** out of respect of the native peoples. 
		- A minor controversy emerged years later when it was found that name was a wild misinterpreted of the [[Ho-Chunk]] language. The intend was to have the name mean friendship or unity; symbolizing the area's different cultural influences. By the time the mistake was found the name had stuck.
- **1939-1945** – World War II Efforts
	- Caroline Religious Teaching College contributes to the war effort, with local industry and students engaging in patriotic duties. The college’s science and engineering departments grow due to wartime funding. After the war, the college continues expanding its academic programs.
- **1943** – **Caroline College** Renamed
	- The college is officially renamed **[[Caroline College]]** after WWII, reflecting its role as a modern liberal arts institution. The post-war years brought growth and new facilities, including **Sister Sarah’s Medical Center**, a teaching hospital for nursing and healthcare students.
- **1969** – Population Decline
	- Watashuka’s population begins to decline in the late 1960s due to changing economic conditions; notably the closing of several government projects now deemed complete. People start leaving for larger cities like Madison and Milwaukee. The closing of some industries and the general economic downturn are seen as the reasons for this decline.
	- The [[Watashuka Initiative|Watashuka Initiative's]] ending dealt a major blow to the region.
- **1983-Present** – Present Day Watashuka
	- Watashuka is a quiet rural town with Caroline College as its centerpiece. The town struggles economically, but the college brings new students and some level of vibrancy. Residents are largely unaware of any significant issues beyond normal small-town troubles.
