![[Dave.png]]
# **Dave**
- **Name**: Unknown (only referred to as "Dave")
- **Age**: Unknown
- **Role**: Dave is the enigmatic, and elusive, pirate radio host of the underground show _Metal At Midnight_. He hijacks **[[WCTU]]**, [[Caroline College|Caroline College's]] AM radio station, for sporadic, late-night broadcasts that combine heavy metal music with wild, conspiracy-laden rants about the government, secret societies, cults, and the supernatural forces lurking in Watashuka. The show starts at exactly midnight and runs until it is abruptly cut off, never airing past **6:14 a.m.** Despite multiple attempts by the college and local authorities to trace his signal, no one has successfully uncovered Dave's identity or location.    
- **Personality**: Dave is a charismatic and chaotic presence on the airwaves, blending metal anthems with conspiracy theories. His rants are erratic and filled with stoner slang like "bro," "man," and "dude." He jumps between topics with manic energy, often weaving real-world issues with his paranoid theories about government surveillance, cult activity, and the occult. Dave frequently laughs maniacally during his broadcasts and mocks those in positions of power, particularly conservative figures like **[[Mothers Opposing Metal-Keeper|Mothers Opposing Metal|MOM]]** and the local police.    
- **Beliefs**: Dave believes shadowy forces are tracking him, particularly the government and various secret societies. He sees himself as a voice for the oppressed, fighting back against the powers that be by spreading the truth through heavy metal music. He regularly mocks the satanic panic of the era, claiming that the real evil is something far worse, hiding in plain sight within Watashuka.    
- **Appearance**: No one knows what Dave looks like. His identity remains a mystery to the authorities, students, and his listeners. Rumors swirl about who Dave might be—some believe he’s a former student or professor, others think he’s an outsider who’s taken up residence on the outskirts of town.    
- **Public Role**:    
    - **Pirate Radio Host**: Dave’s show, _Metal At Midnight_, has a devoted following among the town’s [[Metalheads]] and outcasts. His broadcasts encourage rebellion and defiance against Watashuka’s conservative forces, particularly **[[Mothers Opposing Metal]]**. Through his rants, Dave inadvertently reveals pieces of truth about the town’s occult activity, though listeners must wade through his chaotic monologues to find useful information.
    - **Counterculture Symbol**: To many of Watashuka’s younger, more rebellious residents, Dave is a symbol of defiance against the town’s conservative establishment. His show has become a rallying point for the town’s metalheads, who see him as a voice speaking out against the hypocrisy and hidden darkness of the town.
- **Public Perception**: To most of the town, Dave is nothing more than a nuisance, a conspiracy-theorist pirate radio host whose broadcasts are both hard to find and hard to take seriously. While his rants seem like wild paranoia, some of Watashuka’s youth have come to idolize him as a champion of their anti-establishment mindset. Most adults, particularly those in positions of authority, view him as a disruptive force, but they can’t seem to track him down.
- **Rumors About Dave**:    
    - **The Ghost Broadcaster**: Some say Dave died years ago in a car accident, and his spirit now broadcasts from beyond the grave, using old radio frequencies.
    - **An Old Professor**: One theory suggests Dave is a disgruntled former professor from [[Caroline College]], possibly one who dabbled in occult studies.
    - **In League with the Occult**: Some residents claim Dave is a Satanist himself, using his broadcasts to send coded messages to his followers.
    - **A Rebel Student**: Others believe Dave is a current student, using the college’s equipment to run his show without the administration’s knowledge.
    - **Government Spy**: A few conspiracy theorists think Dave is actually an undercover agent for the secret [[Watashuka Initiative|Project Caroline]], secretly monitoring the town under the guise of a pirate radio host.
    - **Lives in the Tower**: A rumor persists that Dave broadcasts from **Qubit Tower**, hiding in its unused rooms.
    - **The Forgotten Son**: Some believe Dave is the illegitimate child of a prominent family, using his show to exact revenge on the town.
    - **Amish Defector**: There’s speculation that Dave fled the local [[Amish]] community and now rebels against his former life.
    - **A Dark Ritual Survivor**: Some claim Dave was the only survivor of a failed occult ritual in the 1970s and now uses his show to expose the supernatural forces in [[Watashuka]].
    - **A Ho-Chunk Teacher**: A rumor that Dave is a member of the [[Ho-Chunk]] people who is trying to share secret knowledge.

title: Dexter Colby-Secrets
draft: true
publish: false
tags:
  - TTRPG
  - Horror
---
[[Dexter Colby]]
Dexter Colby has lived in Watashuka since the 1880s, hiding from a relentless **Hound of Tindalos**. Originally from England, Dexter fled to the American West in the mid-19th century, where he encountered a powerful necromancer (who Dexter believes was a vampire). After killing the mage, Dexter was cursed, setting the Hound on his trail. Only the town's strange occult protections, including the influence of the [[Ho-Chunk]] and [[Amish]] rituals, have kept the Hound from reaching him. Dexter has lived in perpetual fear, unable to leave [[Watashuka|Watashuka’s]] borders, and while he outwardly appears calm and collected, he remains constantly vigilant.
Dexter avoids [[Caroline College]], where the occult experiments of the [[Brotherhood of the Gate Unveiled]] have weakened the protective barrier that keeps the Hound at bay. He has developed a strong aversion to the campus and subtly steers customers away from discussions that might lead to questions about the school. Despite his fears, Dexter maintains his cover as a mild-mannered bookseller, passing himself off as the latest in a long line of Colbys who have run the store for generations. He carefully cultivates relationships that keep his past from being questioned and avoids photography or long-term acquaintances who might notice his lack of aging.
## Keeping The Truth Hidden
### Hiding His Age
Dexter Colby, having lived in Watashuka since the 1880s, would need to be particularly clever and meticulous in maintaining his cover. Over the decades, he has likely employed a number of subtle strategies and crafted convincing stories to prevent suspicion. Here are some methods Dexter might use to keep his true identity hidden from the town's residents:
- **Frequent Name Changes (Within the Family Line)**
	- Dexter cycles through different variations of his name, claiming to be different generations of the "Colby" family. Every few decades, he might introduce himself as "Dexter Colby Jr." or "D. Colby," telling the town that the bookstore has been passed down from father to son. He regularly updates the store's business license and paperwork to reflect these generational changes.
	- **Story:** "My father started this bookstore, and now I'm keeping the family tradition alive."
- **"Out-of-Town" Trips**
	- Dexter occasionally claims to travel for long stretches of time to visit family or pursue rare book acquisitions. During these absences (which could range from several weeks to even a year), people don’t notice the passage of time as much. He might return with tales of far-off places, lending to his mystique while providing an excuse for any perceived changes in appearance or behavior.
	- **Story:** "I've just returned from Europe, hunting down rare first editions for the shop. It's good to be back."
- **Low Profile and Private Life**
	- Dexter purposefully avoids being the center of attention. He doesn’t attend community events, weddings, or funerals regularly, and when he does, he blends in and leaves quickly. By not becoming deeply involved in personal relationships, most people see him as a slightly reclusive bookworm, which suits his low-key lifestyle.
	- **Story:** "I prefer to keep to myself—books are my real friends."
- **Claiming to Age Slowly (Family Trait)**
	- Dexter can explain his youthful appearance as part of a long-lived family, where members tend to age more slowly than others. He downplays any concerns about his lack of visible aging by referencing distant relatives who also lived into their 90s while looking younger than their years.
	- **Story:** "My family has always been blessed with good genes. I guess I’m lucky to take after my grandmother—she still looked 50 at 80."
- **Strategic "Retirement" and "Reopening"**
	- Every few decades, Dexter might "retire" briefly, closing the shop or handing it off to a fictional family member. During these periods, he rebrands himself slightly and then reopens the store under the guise of a new "generation" of Colbys. Any residents who question this shift are told that the "new" Dexter is simply a younger relative.
	- **Story:** "I’m the nephew of the original Dexter. I’ve inherited the store after my uncle’s retirement."
- **Sparse Historical Record**
	- Dexter is cautious about keeping minimal public records, avoiding excessive paperwork or social engagements that could leave too much evidence. He might pay in cash, avoid the use of modern banking systems, and steer clear of situations that could tie him to past eras.
	- **Story:** "I prefer to keep things simple—no need for too much bureaucracy in running a small shop."
- **Limiting Photographs and Public Appearances**
	- Dexter subtly avoids being photographed or attending public events where photographs might be taken. He’s been known to "not look right in pictures" and has a knack for subtly dodging photos, making sure there’s little visual evidence of his presence over the years.
	- **Story:** "I’ve never been one for photos—I’m not very photogenic, and I feel out of place in them."
- **Friends in the Right Places**
	- Over the years, Dexter has befriended certain individuals who may unknowingly help shield him from suspicion. These could be local officials, clerks, or even older residents who simply vouch for him as an upstanding, long-term resident. By fostering goodwill with select town members, Dexter creates a network of people who never question his longevity.
	- **Story:** "Old Mr. So-and-So always spoke highly of the Colby family—he knew them better than anyone."
- **Fostering Misinformation**
	- Occasionally, Dexter might encourage rumors about his family or store that explain any oddities. For instance, some residents might think he had a reclusive brother or uncle who ran the shop during times when Dexter disappeared. Over time, these rumors become part of the town’s lore, helping mask any inconsistencies in his story.
	- **Story (spread by town gossip):** "Did you hear? I think it was Dexter’s uncle who was in charge of the store back in the 1920s. They’ve always kept the business in the family."
- **Claiming Ancestral Ties to the Town**
	- Dexter often refers to old photographs or documents (which he could easily forge or acquire) to establish a history of his family in Watashuka. The town might have a rich history, but Dexter has been careful to claim that his family has been tied to the town’s growth, making it believable that the Colby lineage has been around for generations.
	- **Story:** "The Colbys have been here since the town was Prairieville Academy. We’ve always been part of Watashuka’s history."
### Example Deflections
Here are some example conversations where **Dexter Colby** deflects or sidesteps questions about his past, while maintaining his cover as the unassuming owner of _The Prince: New & Used Books_:
- **Customer**: "Dexter, how old _are_ you, really? You don’t seem to age!" 
	- **Dexter**: _chuckles_ "Oh, you know, good genes and a quiet life surrounded by books can work wonders. My family’s always looked younger than our years. Just lucky, I suppose."
- **Customer**: "So, how long has your family owned this bookstore? Since the 1800s, right?" 
	- **Dexter**: "Yes, quite a while. My great-grandfather opened the shop. I’m just carrying on the family tradition, you know? The Colbys have always been fond of literature."
- **Curious Student**: "I swear, there’s an old photo of a man who looks exactly like you hanging in the library. Is that your ancestor?" 
	- **Dexter**: _smiles_ "We Colbys do have a family resemblance that runs strong. That’s probably my great-uncle, or someone from a few generations back. Funny how history repeats itself, isn’t it?"
- **Customer**: "You’ve been here as long as I can remember, but I don’t think I’ve ever seen you take a vacation. Don’t you get tired of running the shop?" 
	- **Dexter**: "Oh, I take little trips now and then. Europe, mostly, for rare book acquisitions. I guess I just keep a low profile while I’m away. The bookstore keeps me grounded."
- **Newcomer**: "Wow, this place feels like a time capsule. How do you manage to keep everything so... untouched?" 
	- **Dexter**: "Well, when you’ve been in business for as long as we have, you learn to respect tradition. Besides, old things have a charm that new things can’t quite replicate, don’t you think?"
- **Old Friend**: "Dexter, I’ve known you for 30 years, and you haven’t changed a bit! What’s your secret?" 
	- **Dexter**: _laughs_ "Oh, please, I’ve got more gray hairs than I care to admit. You’ve probably just got a better memory than I do."
- **Customer**: "I was talking to Mr. Habersham, and he mentioned he knew your father? Isn’t that a bit... odd? Habersham’s been around forever." 
	- **Dexter**: "Oh yes, Norm was quite good friends with my father. I guess I take after him—quiet and reserved. He loved this bookstore just as much as I do."
- **Curious Resident**: "There’s a rumor you’ve been running this shop for over a century, Dexter. Any truth to that?" 
	- **Dexter**: _smiles politely_ "I wish! No, the shop’s been in the family for a long time, but it’s been passed down. We Colbys have a tendency to stick around Watashuka."
- **Customer**: "How do you know so much about local history? You talk like you were actually there." 
	- **Dexter**: "I’ve read just about every book on Watashuka’s past. You can learn quite a bit if you spend enough time with your nose in the right pages."
- **Student**: "Have you ever thought about teaching at Caroline College? With your knowledge, you’d make a great professor!" 
	- **Dexter**: "Ah, I’m flattered, but the academic world’s a bit too... complicated for me. I prefer the quiet life here, surrounded by good books and good company."
### Created Family Tree
- **Edward Colby** (born 1820s, died 1882)
    - **Relationship**: Dexter's supposed great-grandfather, the "founder" of _The Prince: New & Used Books_.
    - **Story**: Edward Colby is the original owner who migrated to Watashuka from England in the mid-1800s, bringing with him a passion for books and literature. He is said to have opened the bookstore in the 1880s. Dexter would claim to have never met Edward but knows family stories of his great-grandfather’s strict but wise demeanor. This is the name of Dexter's actual father. 
    - **Key Lie**: "Edward Colby’s dedication to the written word is what started the store, and I’m proud to carry on his legacy."
- **Jonathan Colby** (born 1850s, died 1923)    
    - **Relationship**: Dexter’s supposed grandfather.
    - **Story**: Jonathan Colby, the second-generation owner, took over the shop from his father in the late 19th century. Jonathan expanded the business, sourcing rare books from all over the country. He’s described as a quiet man with a love for historical texts, much like Dexter himself. He passed away in the 1920s, which would align with Dexter’s "current" persona being the third generation of Colbys.
    - **Key Lie**: "My grandfather Jonathan always had a keen eye for rare books—he's the one who turned _The Prince_ into a true collector's paradise."
- **Thomas Colby** (born 1880s, died 1954)    
    - **Relationship**: Dexter’s supposed father.
    - **Story**: Thomas Colby, the third-generation owner, took over from Jonathan after World War I. Thomas was known to be more outgoing and social than his predecessors, frequently attending local events and donating to the library. Thomas supposedly ran the bookstore through the Great Depression and World War II, though Dexter will often downplay his father’s involvement, claiming that "running a bookstore was much simpler back then."
    - **Key Lie**: "My father, Thomas, was a people person—he loved this town and always kept the store thriving, even during the tough times."
- **Dexter Colby Sr.** (born 1910s, "died" 1975)    
    - **Relationship**: Dexter’s supposed uncle or father, depending on what generation Dexter claims to be in at the time.
    - **Story**: Dexter can claim to be the son of this Dexter Colby Sr., who ran the store through the mid-20th century. Dexter Sr. was a private man, described as somewhat reclusive, though known for his love of British literature. He supposedly passed away in the early 1980s, conveniently when the "current" Dexter Colby took over the shop.
    - **Key Lie**: "Dexter Sr. was a quiet man, kept mostly to himself. I’m named after him, though I’ve tried to be a bit more involved in the community."
- **Dexter Colby** (born 1950s, currently alive)
    - **Relationship**: This is the current "Dexter" that townspeople interact with—the fourth generation of Colbys to run _The Prince: New & Used Books_.
    - **Story**: The current Dexter, named after his father/uncle, took over the store in the 1980s after Dexter Sr. passed away. He claims to be carrying on the family legacy with pride, and while he maintains a quiet demeanor, he’s known for his vast knowledge of literature, much like the Colbys before him.
### Strategy for Covering the Timeline:
- **Death Dates**: Dexter Colby ensures that each "generation" has a clear beginning and end, with deaths or retirements happening conveniently at the start of new decades. This provides a buffer if anyone looks into records but avoids specific dates to reduce risk of scrutiny.
- **Personality Variations**: Dexter can attribute slight personality changes between generations to explain why he is different from his supposed father or grandfather (e.g., one was a recluse, another a socialite).
- **Historical Context**: Dexter weaves in real historical events to keep the stories believable—mentioning the Great Depression or World Wars when discussing the hardships or success of previous Colbys.
- **"Out-of-Town" Trips**: Dexter occasionally claims to travel for long stretches of time to visit family or pursue rare book acquisitions. During these absences (which could range from several weeks to even a year), people don’t notice the passage of time as much. He might return with tales of far-off places, lending to his mystique while providing an excuse for any perceived changes in appearance or behavior. **Story:** "I've just returned from Europe, hunting down rare first editions for the shop. It's good to be back."
- **Low Profile and Private Life**: Dexter purposefully avoids being the center of attention. He doesn’t attend community events, weddings, or funerals regularly, and when he does, he blends in and leaves quickly. By not becoming deeply involved in personal relationships, most people see him as a slightly reclusive bookworm, which suits his low-key lifestyle. **Story:** "I prefer to keep to myself—books are my real friends."
- **Claiming to Age Slowly (Family Trait)**: Dexter can explain his youthful appearance as part of a long-lived family, where members tend to age more slowly than others. He downplays any concerns about his lack of visible aging by referencing distant relatives who also lived into their 90s while looking younger than their years. **Story:** "My family has always been blessed with good genes. I guess I’m lucky to take after my grandmother—she still looked 50 at 80."
- **Strategic "Retirement" and "Reopening"** Every few decades, Dexter might "retire" briefly, closing the shop or handing it off to a fictional family member. During these periods, he rebrands himself slightly and then reopens the store under the guise of a new "generation" of Colbys. Any residents who question this shift are told that the "new" Dexter is simply a younger relative. **Story:** "I’m the nephew of the original Dexter. I’ve inherited the store after my uncle’s retirement."
- **Sparse Historical Record** Dexter is cautious about keeping minimal public records, avoiding excessive paperwork or social engagements that could leave too much evidence. He might pay in cash, avoid the use of modern banking systems, and steer clear of situations that could tie him to past eras. He is also not opposed to reverting to his old gunfighter life to take a less than honest option to destroy records. **Story:** "I prefer to keep things simple—no need for too much bureaucracy in running a small shop."
- **Limiting Photographs and Public Appearances** Dexter subtly avoids being photographed or attending public events where photographs might be taken. He’s been known to "not look right in pictures" and has a knack for subtly dodging photos, making sure there’s little visual evidence of his presence over the years. **Story:** "I’ve never been one for photos—I’m not very photogenic, and I feel out of place in them."
- **Friends in the Right Places** Over the years, Dexter has befriended certain individuals who may unknowingly help shield him from suspicion. These could be local officials, clerks, or even older residents who simply vouch for him as an upstanding, long-term resident. By fostering goodwill with select town members, Dexter creates a network of people who never question his longevity. **Story:** "Old Mr. So-and-So always spoke highly of the Colby family—he knew them better than anyone."
- **Fostering Misinformation** Occasionally, Dexter might encourage rumors about his family or store that explain any oddities. For instance, some residents might think he had a reclusive brother or uncle who ran the shop during times when Dexter disappeared. Over time, these rumors become part of the town’s lore, helping mask any inconsistencies in his story. **Story (spread by town gossip):** "Did you hear? I think it was Dexter’s uncle who was in charge of the store back in the 1920s. They’ve always kept the business in the family."
- **Claiming Ancestral Ties to the Town** Dexter often refers to old photographs or documents (which he could easily forge or acquire) to establish a history of his family in Watashuka. The town might have a rich history, but Dexter has been careful to claim that his family has been tied to the town’s growth, making it believable that the Colby lineage has been around for generations. **Story:** "The Colbys have been here since the town was Prairieville Academy. We’ve always been part of Watashuka’s history."
### Example Dialogue to Maintain Consistency:
- **"Oh, that would’ve been my grandfather, Jonathan. He was the one who started collecting rare books. I just wish I’d been around to meet him."**
- **"The Colbys have always been in Watashuka. We’ve seen the town change so much since my great-grandfather opened the shop in the 1880s."**
- **"My father—Thomas Colby—ran this place through the 30s and 40s. I’m lucky he left me such a strong foundation."**

# Dexter Colby
*The bell above the door jingles as a customer steps into The Prince. Dexter, with his salt-and-pepper hair neatly combed, looks up from the old novel he’s been reading, offering a subtle smile. "Looking for something in particular?" he asks in his calm, deep voice. He moves gracefully around the shelves, his fingers brushing the spines of books that seem older than the building itself. Dexter may not be the most outgoing shopkeeper, but there’s something about him that makes his quiet bookstore feel like a timeless haven.*
Dexter Colby is the owner of [[The Prince-New & Used Books|The Prince: New & Used Books]], a charming, slightly dusty bookstore filled with an eclectic selection of literature. Dexter is known for his vast knowledge of rare and antique books, and his quiet but engaging presence behind the counter. According to local lore, the Colby family has been running the store for generations; arriving shortly after the [[Great Influx]]. Dexter often speaks fondly of his ancestors who established the business in the late 1800s. While Dexter can be a bit reclusive, preferring the company of books over people, he’s always willing to help a customer find that perfect read.

Secrets for [[Jan Ducochik]]
- **Role**: Since joining the police force in **1980**, Jan has become increasingly aware of supernatural events happening in [[Watashuka]]. He believes dark forces are manipulating the town and is secretly investigating these occurrences. He is highly suspicious of his colleagues, fearing many are involved in occult activities. He works closely with [[Norm Habersham]], investigating behind the scenes to expose occult influences and uncover hidden truths.
- **Suspicion of Captain Bernard Miller**: Jan is particularly wary of his superior, **Captain Bernard Miller**, suspecting the captain of occult involvement due to frequent absences and an apparent lack of interest in investigating strange events. However, Jan has misread Miller’s secret trips to Milwaukee, which are tied to Miller's hidden personal life rather than supernatural activities. This misinterpretation heightens Jan’s paranoia, fueling tension between them.
- **Religious Conviction**: Though outwardly respectful of the town’s Lutheran traditions, Jan believes his Catholic faith is superior. He views the [[Lutheran Church]] as spiritually weak and lacking depth but keeps these feelings carefully concealed, only allowing his true thoughts to surface in moments of extreme stress. This internal conflict adds to his sense of isolation, particularly as his investigations grow more dangerous.
- **Investigator of the Unexplained**: Jan has compiled a secret file documenting bizarre events in Watashuka—disappearances, strange symbols, and mysterious deaths—and quietly investigates them, convinced the town is hiding something dark. His growing paranoia makes him distrustful, even of those closest to him, which complicates his work. However, his drive to protect Watashuka keeps him dedicated to uncovering the truth.

![[Sgt. Jan Ducochik.png]]
# **Jan Ducochik**
*Sergeant Jan Ducochik, in his early 30s, cuts an imposing yet composed figure in Watashuka’s police department. Standing tall and well-groomed, Jan’s sharp blue eyes reflect both his intense focus and the quiet burdens he carries. His chiseled face, framed by a thick, well-kept mustache, lends him an air of authority that is only heightened by his neatly pressed police uniform. His dark blonde hair is meticulously combed, and every aspect of his appearance speaks to a man who values discipline and precision. Jan’s build is athletic, with the lean strength of someone who remains physically active and ready for whatever may come his way. There is a seriousness to his demeanor, his sharp gaze constantly observing and assessing his surroundings, as though he’s always alert for something more than the everyday crimes of small-town life.*
*In the station or on patrol, Jan moves with a purpose that reveals his deep sense of duty. His uniform, spotless and well-fitted, reflects his commitment to his role as a protector of Watashuka. He speaks little but listens intently, giving off a sense of calm, calculated vigilance.*
- **Role**: Sergeant Jan Ducochik serves in the [[Watashuka]] Police Department. Since joining the force in **1980**, he has become a reliable officer, well-liked by the community for his professionalism and dedication. Over the last few years, he has taken a more active interest in the town’s safety, particularly focusing on strange events that others dismiss as coincidences. He has earned a reputation for being diligent, though some colleagues find him overly suspicious.
- **Age**: Early 30s (1983)
- **Appearance**: Jan is a sharp, well-groomed man with striking blue eyes, a chiseled face, and a thick mustache. His dark blonde hair is neatly combed, and his police uniform is always pristine, reflecting his disciplined nature. He has an intense gaze, which locals find reassuring in his position of authority.
- **Personality**: Jan is serious, dutiful, and moral. He is devout in his Catholic faith, though respectful of Watashuka’s predominantly Lutheran traditions. His strict moral code shapes his work, and he often views things in black-and-white terms, always striving to protect the town. However, his more focused approach to uncovering unusual events in Watashuka makes him stand out from his colleagues, some of whom think he is overreacting.
- **Public Role**: Jan is a respected sergeant who actively investigates unusual occurrences around town. His suspicions have led him to dig deeper into strange events, but he presents himself as calm and controlled. He collaborates with the local newspaper editor, [[Norm Habersham]], when needed, gathering tips on town rumors and unexplained occurrences.

![[Leonid Kuznetsov.png]]
# Leonid "Lenny" Kuznetsov
**Role/Title:** Night Stock Boy at Dominick's Grocery, Unwilling Recruit of the **[[Church of the Delayed Blossom]]**
**Description:** Lenny Kuznetsov, known as "Lenny," is an 18-year-old high school dropout who works the night shift at Dominick’s Grocery. With greasy black hair, a sallow complexion, and a perpetual scowl, Lenny exudes anger and resentment, traits that have made him easy prey for the cult. Raised by an abusive father and abandoned by his mother, Lenny has learned to trust no one and uses violence to assert what little control he feels he has in life.
**Background:** Lenny was born into a Russian immigrant family and had a difficult upbringing. His mother left when he was young, and his father’s physical abuse turned Lenny into a bitter and angry young man. He dropped out of school to work, becoming isolated from his peers and finding solace in violent tendencies. It was during his job at Dominick’s that he met Randolph Tomaszewski, who recognized Lenny’s potential for manipulation and brought him into the **Church of the Delayed Blossom**.
**Cult Role:** Lenny was recruited by [[Randolph Tomaszewski-Keeper]], who used Lenny’s rage and desperation to his advantage, making him a loyal, if reluctant, pawn of the Church. While Lenny is not fully aware of the cult’s true nature or goals, he has been drawn into their orbit, believing that by serving them he will eventually gain the power and respect he craves. Lenny resents Randolph’s control over him but also fears what might happen if he defies him. His fear of both Randolph and the cult keeps him obedient, but he harbors dreams of breaking free.
**Goals:**
- **Power and Respect**: Lenny’s primary goal is to gain power within [[Watashuka]], eventually freeing himself from Randolph’s control and establishing himself as someone others fear and respect.
- **Break Free from Randolph**: Lenny’s resentment toward Randolph is growing, and though he continues to serve him for now, he secretly hopes to find a way to break free of the cult’s influence.
- **Win Over Ronnie Regan**: Lenny harbors an unhealthy crush on [[Ronnie Regan]], the young assistant at Peach Street Library. Though Ronnie is unaware of his feelings, Lenny has been secretly stalking her. He is torn between wanting to impress her and his darker urges, making him a volatile and dangerous presence in her life.
**Personality:**
- **Aggressive and Violent**: Lenny’s first instinct is always to resort to violence, especially when he feels threatened or belittled.
- **Manipulative**: Though not particularly intelligent, Lenny has learned how to use intimidation and manipulation to get what he wants from others, especially those he sees as weaker.
- **Resentful and Selfish**: Lenny resents anyone who has what he doesn’t—whether that’s authority, power, or control. He has little regard for others’ well-being, prioritizing his own needs and desires.
**Relationships:**
- **[[Randolph Tomaszewski]]**: Lenny serves Randolph grudgingly, acting as an apprentice and enforcer for the cult. Though he follows Randolph’s orders, Lenny resents the control Randolph has over him and dreams of the day he can exact revenge on both Randolph and the cult.
- **[[Ronnie Regan|Ronnie "Moonglow" Regan]]**: Lenny’s obsession with Ronnie is unhealthy and dangerous. Though he has not yet acted on his feelings, he stalks her from a distance, watching her movements and fantasizing about ways to win her over. His violent nature makes this crush all the more dangerous, especially as Lenny becomes more frustrated with his inability to approach her.
## Brief Description: 
Lenny, as he prefers to be called, is a lanky and unkempt 18-year-old with greasy black hair and a perpetual scowl. His eyes are a dull blue, and his skin appears sallow from years of late nights and poor diet. He often wears a stained Dominick's apron over threadbare clothes, giving him an overall disheveled appearance.
## Biography:
- Background: Lenny was born to a Russian immigrant family who moved to Watashuka when he was young. His mother left the family when he was just a child, leaving him and his older brother, Sasha, to be raised by their abusive father. As a result of these hardships, Lenny developed a deep-seated resentment towards authority figures and a tendency towards violence.
- Meeting Randolph: Lenny encountered [[Randolph Tomaszewski]] at Dominick's Grocery when he found Randolph stealing food, supplies and animals fresh from the slaughter house meant for the butchers. Randolph, recognizing Lenny's violent tendencies and the potential for manipulation, decided to recruit him into the Church of the Delayed Blossom.
## Personality:
- Aggressive: Lenny is prone to outbursts of anger and violence, often directed at those he perceives as weaker than himself.
- Manipulative: He enjoys exercising power over others and will often use intimidation or force to achieve his goals. 
- Selfish: Lenny prioritizes his own needs and desires above all else, with little regard for the well-being of others.
## Relationships:
- [[Randolph Tomaszewski]] recruited Lenny. Randolph is Lenny's mentor and controller. Lenny resents Randolph's control over him but also fears the consequences of defying his orders. This leads to a complex dynamic between them, as Lenny struggles against his cult duties while seeking opportunities to assert his independence. Despite his resentment, Lenny remains loyal to Randolph due to their shared experience of both being controlled by cult.
- [[Ronnie Regan]] is the subject of Lenny's unhealthy crush. Ronnie does not know about Lenny's interest and Lenny is not ready to make his dark fascinations known to others; especially Ronnie. But he has been stalking her secretly.
## Goals:
Lenny's primary goal is to amass power and influence within Watashuka, allowing him to exact revenge on those who have wronged him or his family. As Lenny becomes more aware of the cult's true nature, he is beginning to hope to break free of Randolph's control.

title: Margaret Wilkins-Secrets

---
[[Margaret Wilkins]]
- **Age**: 66 (in 1983)
- **Background**: Margaret’s career began in **1939**, when at the age of 22, she covered the supernatural disaster known as **[[The Baptism of '39]]**. This event was the first of three that convinced her of the existence of forces far darker than she could have imagined. Margaret never fully recovered from what she witnessed at Lake Mary, and it set her on a path of quiet investigation into [[Watashuka|Watashuka's]] secrets. Her firsthand experiences of supernatural events left her deeply wary, though she kept these beliefs to herself, carefully watching from the shadows as her journalism career flourished.
- **The Three Events**:
    - **The Baptism of ’39**: The mass baptism turned tragedy, in which parishioners were pulled into Lake Mary by strange forces, was her first brush with the unexplainable. While she wrote about it as a natural disaster for the paper, the sights and strange phenomena she witnessed stayed with her, making her a secret believer in the supernatural.
    - **The Winter of '47**: Margaret covered a series of mysterious disappearances during the harsh winter of 1947. Though officially attributed to severe weather, Margaret uncovered strange symbols near the victims' homes and became convinced that something much more sinister was behind the disappearances. Her reporting on the event was careful and vague, but she continued to investigate privately.
    - **The Summer of ’49**: In the summer of 1949, Margaret witnessed the collapse of an old warehouse near the Watashuka train station under bizarre circumstances. Survivors spoke of eerie noises and shifting shadows moments before the collapse. Though her investigation hinted at cult activity in the area, she chose to report it as a tragic accident to avoid drawing attention to the truth.
- **Retirement and Caution**: After retiring from _The Prairie_ in **1950**, Margaret decided to distance herself from the increasingly dangerous forces at work in Watashuka. She handed the reins to **Norm Habersham**, a man she trusted to continue quietly investigating the town’s darker mysteries. However, Margaret chose not to involve herself directly anymore, fearing that her investigations had already led her too close to something she couldn’t escape. She keeps a close eye on strange events from the safety of her newsstand but avoids direct involvement, believing that further entanglement might cost her more than just her life.
- **Reluctance to Act**: Margaret’s reluctance to get involved stems from her past experiences, where her brush with the supernatural left her shaken and afraid. She remains a source of information for those in the know but refuses to actively investigate anymore, feeling that whatever she witnessed in the past could pull her back in if she isn’t careful.
- Margaret wears a wedding band but there is no record of her ever being married. During a cult ritual, her husband was pulled into a time stream, leaving no history of their marriage in this time line. Norm was her husband. He was restored 'out of time', Norm never went to the navy... he was lost in time.
- **Key Relationships**:
    - **Norm Habersham**: Margaret was Norm’s mentor and the one who helped him transition into his role as senior editor after she retired. Though she respects Norm’s continued investigations, she often cautions him against pursuing the truth too closely, fearing he may end up suffering the same terrors she once faced. They maintain a quiet, mutual respect, though Margaret rarely speaks about her own supernatural experiences.
- **Legacy**: Margaret’s work remains influential in Watashuka, though few know the extent of what she truly saw during her time as a reporter. Her hoarded newspapers and meticulous notes might contain clues to the town’s hidden history, but for now, they remain locked away, just as Margaret keeps her fears and knowledge hidden from the rest of the town.

![[Margaret_Wilkins.png]]
# **Margaret Wilkins**
*Margaret Wilkins, at 66 years old (in 1983), stands behind the counter of her cozy newsstand on the corner of Main Street in Watashuka. Her silver-gray hair is neatly styled in a short, no-nonsense bob, with a few loose strands framing her face. Margaret's sharp brown eyes, still full of keen observation, peer out from behind thick, square-framed glasses, giving her a serious yet approachable look. Her face is lined with years of both worry and laughter, showing the deep creases of someone who has lived a life full of quiet contemplation and unspeakable experiences. She wears a patterned cardigan over a light blouse, a modest but practical outfit fitting for the fall weather. A string of pearls around her neck adds a touch of elegance, a reminder of her former stature as Watashuka's first female senior editor. Her posture is slightly hunched from age, but her hands, still quick and steady, sort through newspapers and magazines with practiced ease. Margaret’s fingers are adorned with a simple gold wedding band, though she was never married—an object of curiosity among the townsfolk.*
*The newsstand itself is a tight space packed with neatly stacked papers, magazines, and candy bars. The shelves behind her are filled with rows of unsold copies of The Prairie Press, each one a piece of history she refuses to part with. She is a woman who knows far more than she lets on, standing guard over the town’s stories with both caution and care.*
- **Age**: 66 (in 1983)    
- **Role**: Former journalist and the first female senior editor of _The Prairie Press_ (retired in 1950), Margaret Wilkins is a fixture of Watashuka’s history. She now runs the Press Newsstand in town, selling magazines, newspapers, and small sundries. Despite her seemingly mundane post-retirement life, Margaret’s keen eyes and sharp mind have never dulled.    
- **Background**: Margaret began her career as a young and determined journalist in the late 1930s, starting with a pivotal assignment at the age of 22. Her story on the infamous **[[The Baptism of '39|Baptism of '39]]** was her first major piece for _The Prairie_, setting the stage for her future career. Margaret went on to cover some of the town’s most notable events during her tenure at the paper, gaining a reputation as a diligent, brave, and sometimes tenacious reporter. She eventually became the first female senior editor of _The Prairie Press_, a position she held until her retirement in **1950**, when she passed the role to **[[Norm Habersham]]**.    
- **Press Newsstand**: Since retiring, Margaret runs the small Press Newsstand in downtown Watashuka, quietly observing the town she once wrote about. She’s known for hoarding unsold copies of newspapers, often storing them in the back of her shop. Locals see her as a curious relic of a bygone era, but Margaret continues to follow the news and keeps up with local happenings, even if she no longer writes about them.    
- **Public Perception**: To the town, Margaret is a beloved figure from Watashuka’s journalistic past, a pioneer in her field and a woman who stood her ground in a male-dominated profession. Though she no longer engages in investigative journalism, many still remember her early work and come to her newsstand for both gossip and news. She is respected, if occasionally pitied for her reclusive nature.

title: Max and Maxine McElhenney-Secrets

tags:

[[Max and Maxine McElhenney]]
#### **Max McElhenney**
**Secret:**  
Max’s laid-back, stoner persona is largely a mask. In truth, he’s been haunted by recurring dreams about his parents' involvement in occult rituals. These dreams suggest that Max may have been more involved than he realized, possibly as a vessel or participant in dark rituals conducted by the **[[Brotherhood of the Gate Unveiled]]**. These memories have surfaced slowly, and though Max hasn’t shared them with anyone—not even Maxine—he’s growing increasingly paranoid that the cult might still be watching. His time working alone at night in the hospital has only deepened his fears, as he sometimes hears whispers in the empty halls that remind him of the chants in his dreams.
**Background:**  
When Max and Maxine were 5 years old, their parents died in what was reported as a car accident. What Max does not know is that his parents were deeply entangled with the **Brotherhood of the Gate Unveiled**, and their deaths were part of a staged accident orchestrated by the cult to prevent them from leaving. The cult planned to use Max and Maxine in future rituals, but their youth spared them at the time. Now, Max’s memories are returning, and he fears he might unknowingly still be tied to the cult.
---
#### **Maxine McElhenney**
**Secret:**  
Unlike Max, Maxine has taken a more direct approach to the mystery of their parents' deaths. She’s been secretly investigating the circumstances surrounding the accident and has discovered dark truths that she hasn’t shared with her brother. Maxine found her parents’ hidden journals in the attic of their inherited home, and these texts reveal their involvement with the **Brotherhood of the Gate Unveiled**. The journals outline the rituals they participated in and hint at a grander, long-term plan involving the twins. Maxine is horrified by the implications, but also fascinated by the power the cult seemed to hold. She hasn’t decided what to do with this knowledge yet—whether to continue her research or destroy the journals. Part of her is even tempted to see what the rituals could offer, though this dark curiosity frightens her.
**Background:**  
Maxine hides her investigation from Max, fearing he’ll either not understand or try to stop her. Though she is usually composed and rational, this secret has put a strain on her, leading her to sometimes isolate herself. Maxine's discovery of her family’s connection to Watashuka’s dark history has deeply unsettled her, but she continues to keep up appearances, focusing on her studies and maintaining a normal life, even as the weight of her secret grows heavier.
---
### **What Really Happened to Their Parents**
The twins' parents were deeply involved in the **Brotherhood of the Gate Unveiled**, a cult experimenting with dangerous rituals tied to time and dimensional manipulation. When they tried to flee the cult’s control, they were killed in a staged car accident. The cult spared Max and Maxine, intending to use them in future rituals. The twins were sent away to live with relatives, only to return to Watashuka at 18, inheriting their parents' home and the dark legacy that came with it.
Max’s repressed memories and Maxine’s investigation are drawing both siblings closer to the truth of what happened, though they remain unaware of each other’s involvement. The cult has not forgotten about them, and the twins are unknowingly caught in a web of supernatural forces and hidden agendas that may soon resurface.
---
## Older
# Max and Maxine McElhenney
![](Max%20and%20Maxine%20McElhenney.png)
## **Max McElhenney**
**Overview**:  
Max McElhenney is a 19-year-old who returned to [Watashuka](Watashuka.md) with his twin sister Maxine after inheriting their parents’ old house. Though he enrolled in [Caroline College](Caroline%20College.md) at 18, he put his studies on "hold" and now works as a janitor at the local hospital. Max is laid-back and reserved, often perceived as a stoner due to his slow speech and distant demeanor, even though he’s never touched drugs in his life. This misconception has become a running joke among his co-workers and the town’s youth. Max is an avid heavy metal fan and a loyal listener of _Metal at Midnight_. He plays the drums and frequently practices with his sister, Maxine. Despite his seemingly carefree exterior, Max harbors a dark secret tied to his family’s past.
**Public Perception**:  
To most of Watashuka, Max is the quiet, brooding type who seems to be drifting through life. People often dismiss him as "wasting his potential" after leaving college, though his consistent work at the hospital has gained him a reputation as a reliable, if peculiar, employee. Some think he’s hiding from something, but no one can quite figure out what.
**Family**:  
Max and Maxine share a family name, **McElhenney**, tied to the local Journalism School. Their name is constantly mispronounced, much to their irritation. Their parents died in a car accident when they were just 5 years old, under mysterious circumstances. They were sent to live with family outside of Wisconsin, only to return at 18 when they inherited their childhood home.
---
## **Maxine McElhenney**
**Overview**:  
Maxine McElhenney is Max’s twin sister, and unlike her brother, she has stayed in school. At 19, she’s continuing her education at Caroline College, pursuing a degree in sociology. She’s intelligent, sharp-witted, and often keeps her emotions in check, but shares Max’s passion for heavy metal. Maxine plays the bass guitar, and though she and Max practice together, she has always envied the local Metalheads, longing to belong to their group but never quite fitting in. Like her brother, she is haunted by the mysterious death of their parents, though she hides her deeper feelings behind a composed exterior. Despite her driven academic focus, Maxine harbors a secret that even Max doesn’t know.
**Public Perception**:  
Maxine is seen as the more "successful" twin, continuing her education and working hard. Professors and students alike appreciate her intellect, though she often keeps others at arm’s length. Despite her academic achievements, Maxine seems disconnected, as if she’s always carrying some weight on her shoulders. Her heavy metal interests and aloof personality make her both intriguing and intimidating to her peers.
**Family**:  
Maxine and Max share the McElhenney name, famously tied to the journalism school at Caroline College. She’s as tired as Max of people mispronouncing it. Their parents’ untimely death and the air of mystery around it have left both twins with more questions than answers, though Maxine has tried to focus on her studies to avoid thinking about it.
---
## **What Really Happened to Their Parents**
Max and Maxine’s parents died in a car accident in Watashuka when the twins were just 5 years old. **What really happened** is far darker than what was reported. Their parents had become deeply entangled with a local cult, **The Brotherhood of the Gate Unveiled**, which was conducting dangerous experiments on time and dimensional manipulation. The McElhenneys were trying to escape the cult’s grasp when they were killed in a staged accident meant to silence them.
**Why the Twins Were Spared**:  
Max and Maxine were spared from the cult’s reach because they were still too young to understand the rituals their parents were involved in. However, there’s an eerie detail: the cult intended to use them later. The accident wasn’t a random tragedy; it was orchestrated to remove the parents while keeping the children alive for future use in a ritual that hasn’t yet come to pass.
---
## **Max’s Dark Secret**
**Max’s Secret**: Though Max plays dumb and goes along with the stoner rumors, he’s not as aloof as he seems. Max has begun **remembering strange dreams from his childhood**, dreams where he recalls his parents taking part in occult rituals. He hasn’t told anyone, not even Maxine, because these dreams imply that **he was involved**, even as a young child, possibly as a vessel or participant in these rituals. He’s terrified that whatever happened to his parents is somehow connected to him, and that the cult might still be watching.
---
## **Maxine’s Dark Secret**
**Maxine’s Secret**: Maxine maintains a calm, controlled demeanor, but she’s secretly been investigating her parents' deaths on her own. What she’s uncovered scares her: her family’s lineage goes back to some of the original founders of Watashuka’s darker elements, including those tied to the **Journalism School** that bears their name. What Maxine doesn’t tell Max is that she’s found **hidden journals** of her parents in the attic of their childhood home, which outline the cult activities they were involved in. She hasn’t told him because she’s considering **using the knowledge herself**—a thought that horrifies and fascinates her.
---
## **Professions and Skills**
- **Max McElhenney**
    - **Occupation**: Hospital Janitor
    - **Skills**: _Stealth, Listen, Drums (Art)_
    - **Connections**: Hospital staff, late-night workers
    - **Hobbies**: Drumming, heavy metal, practicing with Maxine
- **Maxine McElhenney**
    - **Occupation**: College Student (Sociology)
    - **Skills**: _Library Use, Bass (Art), Psychology_
    - **Connections**: Professors, classmates, student groups
    - **Hobbies**: Playing bass, research, collecting records

# Max and Maxine McElhenney
#### **Max McElhenney**
**Overview:**  
Max McElhenney, 19, returned to [[Watashuka]] with his twin sister, Maxine, after inheriting their late parents' home. Max enrolled at [[Caroline College]] at 18 but put his studies on hold to work as a janitor at the local hospital. With his laid-back demeanor, slow speech, and love of heavy metal, Max is often mistaken for a stoner, a misconception he is quick to correct. He plays drums and frequently jams with Maxine. Despite his carefree appearance, there’s a quiet depth to him that most people overlook.
**Public Perception:**  
Max is viewed by the locals as quiet, if somewhat aloof. His decision to step away from college is seen as "wasting potential," though those who know him at the hospital recognize him as dependable and diligent. His reputation as a [[Metalheads|metalhead]] and his easygoing attitude make him popular with the town’s youth, who appreciate his relaxed, nonjudgmental nature.
---
#### **Maxine McElhenney**
**Overview:**  
Maxine McElhenney, also 19, is Max’s twin sister and the more academically inclined of the two. She continues her education at Caroline College, majoring in sociology, while Max works. Though she’s sharp-witted and focused on her studies, Maxine shares her brother’s passion for heavy metal, playing bass guitar alongside him. Maxine is intelligent and driven, but she keeps a certain emotional distance from others, often hiding behind her calm and composed exterior.
**Public Perception:**  
Seen as the more "responsible" twin, Maxine is well-regarded by her professors and peers for her academic achievements. Despite her success, there’s a certain air of aloofness about her—people find her both intriguing and a bit intimidating. Her musical tastes and love for metalheads make her stand out, but she’s never quite fit in with the scene as much as she would like to.

# **Mike and Ruth Garrison**
![[Mike and Ruth Garrison At The Frozen Cow.png]]
*It’s another sunny afternoon at the Frozen Cow Burger Stand. The line stretches down the sidewalk as locals and students eagerly await their favorite meals. Mike stands at the counter, laughing with customers and cracking jokes, his long-ago hippie roots showing in his relaxed demeanor. Ruth, ever the efficient one, works the grill with practiced ease. She glances at Mike, shaking her head with a fond smile. Despite all the hustle, the two seem perfectly in sync, their connection a comforting fixture in the town of [[Watashuka]].*
Mike and Ruth Garrison are the proud owners of the Frozen Cow Burger Stand, a beloved 1950s-style diner in Watashuka. Mike, a former hippie who drifted into town in the late 60s, fell in love with Ruth when he stopped at a burger stand where she worked. Mike was lost and in need of a meal. When taking his order, Ruth asked Mike what he was doing in town. Mike said, under the influence, that he was on his way to Alaska. "Why would you want to go way up there?" she asked politely.  “I'm heading up north to check out a free commune.” Ruth misheard him over the noise of the diner - thinking he said he was "heading up north to check out a frozen cow." This was the funniest thing she ever heard and busted out laughing. Mike thought the sound of her laughter was the most beautiful thing *he* ever heard. 
From that moment on, Mike worked hard to buy Ruth her own burger stand. That misunderstanding has become a staple in the community for decades now. And while he gave the drugs up a long time ago, his memory never fully recovered. He readily admits that Ruth is the brains of the outfit. 
**Mike Garrison** is in his early 60s, with a stocky build and a weathered, easygoing face that often carries a big, friendly smile. His thick, silver-gray hair still hints at the carefree days of his youth, and he usually sports a well-worn ball cap or the classic paper diner hat while working at the stand. Mike's style is a blend of practical and nostalgic, often seen wearing a white short-sleeved button-up shirt, tucked into his faded jeans or diner uniform. His voice is warm and booming, quick to share a joke or story from his hippie days, though his past drug use often leads to some comically hazy recollections.
**Ruth Garrison** is in her late 50s, shorter and more slender than Mike, with neatly styled salt-and-pepper hair often tied back in a simple bun. Her face has a warm yet practical expression, and while she doesn’t smile as often as Mike, when she does, it’s with a quiet, knowing grace. Ruth’s sharp blue eyes seem to notice everything around her, including the details Mike often misses. Her attire is always neat and functional, typically a white blouse beneath a striped apron, making her look like the efficient, hardworking heart of the Frozen Cow. While Ruth is more reserved, she’s also quick-witted and known for her dry sense of humor, especially when it comes to teasing Mike.
Together, they’re a contrasting but complementary pair—Mike, the talkative charmer, and Ruth, the quiet but sharp backbone of the operation.

title: Norm Habersham-Secrets
draft: true
publish: false
tags:

---
[[Norm Habersham]]
- **Secret Role**: While publicly Norm is a no-nonsense journalist, behind the scenes he is much more than that. Norm has spent decades quietly investigating the supernatural occurrences in [[Watashuka]], gathering evidence on the strange and dangerous forces at play. His years of carefully collecting information have made him one of the most knowledgeable figures on the town’s hidden history. He works closely with **[[Jan Ducochik|Sgt. Jan Ducochik]]** to unravel the mystery of Watashuka’s dark undercurrents, though he remains careful not to draw too much attention to their efforts.
- **Key Events Witnessed**:
    - **The Cold Flames at Stratton Mill** (1955): Norm arrived at the scene of the fire just as firefighters were struggling to contain what appeared to be a cold, unnatural flame that didn’t behave like ordinary fire. The mill had been used by the **[[Brotherhood of the Gate Unveiled]]** for rituals, and the fire was the result of a failed attempt to tear open a dimensional gateway. Norm suspected this, though his official reporting avoided any mention of cults or supernatural phenomena. However, in his private notes, Norm documented accounts of strange symbols and ghostly apparitions seen at the mill, knowing that the fire was far more than a simple industrial accident.
    - **Destruction of South High School** (1971): Norm’s investigation into the explosion at South High School left him convinced that it wasn’t just a boiler malfunction caused by students’ pranks. Eyewitnesses described unusual lights and noises in the building the night of the explosion, and some students claimed to have seen shadowy figures moving through the halls. Norm believes the explosion was tied to occult activity—perhaps even a ritual gone wrong. To this day, he keeps files on the incident, including sketches of symbols found in the wreckage.
    - **The Parade Storm** (1959): Norm suspected supernatural interference when a sudden storm hit Watashuka during a parade. The storm seemed unnaturally focused on the parade route, with some attendees reporting a feeling of being watched or manipulated by unseen forces. Norm kept his suspicions out of print, but his notes describe strange winds and patterns that didn’t match any normal weather phenomena.
    - **The Harvest Moon Disappearance** (1967): Norm dug deeper into the disappearance of a local farmer during the Harvest Moon Festival than the police were willing to. Strange symbols were found on the farmer’s land, and rumors swirled about cult activity in the area. Norm connected the disappearance to older legends of the land, which speak of rituals and sacrifices tied to the moon’s cycle. Though his official article remained neutral, Norm kept detailed records of the symbols and witness accounts that pointed to something far darker than a simple disappearance.
- **Personality and Methodology**: Norm is patient, methodical, and cautious. He believes in slow and careful investigation, letting evidence accumulate until a full picture emerges. Unlike **Sgt. Ducochik**, who is more willing to confront the unknown directly, Norm prefers to work in the shadows, documenting everything and connecting the dots without drawing too much attention. His calm demeanor is a cover for his deep knowledge of the occult forces at work in Watashuka, and he takes great care to keep his true investigations secret.
- **Key Relationships**:
    - **[[Jan Ducochik|Sgt. Jan Ducochik]]**: Norm and Jan have formed an unlikely but effective partnership. Norm’s cautious approach often balances Jan’s more direct methods, and they share information on the strange events happening in Watashuka. Norm provides Jan with valuable context from his decades of research, and in return, Jan helps Norm access leads within the police force.
    - **[[Margaret Wilkins]]**: Though Margaret retired long ago, Norm continues to visit her at her newsstand, knowing that she has hoarded newspapers from decades past. Margaret’s keen eyes and experience in supernatural investigations make her a valuable, if reluctant, source of information. They share a mutual respect, though both are wary of becoming too deeply involved in the town’s darker mysteries.
- **Legacy**: Norm’s quiet but thorough investigations have made him one of the most informed people in Watashuka about the supernatural. His work is a slow, methodical accumulation of knowledge, carefully hidden from the town’s leadership and cults. He remains dedicated to uncovering the truth, even if it means working in the shadows for the rest of his life.

![[Norm Habersham.png]]
# **Norm Habersham**
*Norm Habersham, now in his early-60s, stands at the editorial desk of The Prairie Press, a figure both familiar and respected in Watashuka. His graying hair is neatly combed, though thinning on top, and his face bears the wrinkles of a life spent both in service and in thought. His sharp blue eyes, which once scanned the horizon as a Navy sailor, now focus intently on the papers and notes before him, always keen and observant. His serious expression give him the look of a man who has seen more than he lets on. Norm is dressed simply, wearing a button-down shirt with short sleeves, the look of someone who values practicality. His well-worn brown slacks show the signs of a man who has spent years in the field. His once-strong frame has diminished with age, but there is still a sense of purpose in the way he carries himself. A wristwatch and a leather notebook always seem to be at hand, tools of a journalist who is ever ready to document a story.*
*Behind Norm is the cluttered office of The Prairie Press, where stacks of newspapers and files lie in organized chaos. The atmosphere is one of quiet focus, much like Norm himself—calm, thoughtful, and always working, whether it’s on the next headline or a small-town mystery.
- **Age**: 61 (in 1983)    
- **Role**: Norm Habersham is the senior editor of _The Prairie Press_, [[Watashuka|Watashuka's]] local newspaper. A WWII Navy veteran, Norm returned to his hometown after the war and dedicated himself to journalism. He has been at _The Prairie_ for over 30 years, gaining a reputation as a reliable and steadfast figure in the town’s media landscape. Norm is highly respected for his thorough reporting, calm demeanor, and no-nonsense approach to both journalism and life.    
- **Public Career**: Over the decades, Norm has covered countless events, both big and small. His dedication to documenting the town’s history, from civic improvements to local tragedies, has made him an integral part of Watashuka’s fabric. He succeeded **[[Margaret Wilkins]]** as senior editor in **1950** and has carried on the paper’s legacy with diligence. Norm’s focus is primarily on local news, keeping residents informed about school board meetings, town hall decisions, and community events.    
- **Key Events Covered**:
	- **The Cold Flames at Stratton Mill** (1955): Norm was one of the first on the scene after the historic Stratton Mill burned down in a mysterious cold fire. Official reports attribute the blaze to a malfunction in the mill’s equipment, but Norm’s careful documentation of eyewitness accounts—mentioning ghostly flames that neither spread nor consumed—has left some readers puzzled to this day.
    - **Destruction of South High School** (1971): South High School’s destruction in a boiler explosion shook the town. The official story points to students tampering with the boiler after a heated basketball game against Delavan High School, but Norm’s in-depth investigation at the time raised questions about unusual circumstances surrounding the incident.
    - **The Parade Storm** (1959): A freak storm hit Watashuka during a summer parade, injuring several attendees. Norm reported on the suddenness of the storm and the way it seemed to focus on the parade route. Witnesses spoke of strange winds and a sensation of being watched, though Norm’s article stuck to the basics, leaving the oddities out of print.
    - **The Harvest Moon Disappearance** (1967): A local farmer vanished without a trace during the annual Harvest Moon Festival. Norm’s story was the first to suggest that his disappearance might be linked to strange symbols found on his land—a detail the police chose not to publicize.
- **Public Perception**: Norm is widely seen as the last of the old guard in Watashuka. To the townspeople, he is a fixture of the community—someone who has always been around and who is trusted to get the facts straight. He is known for being reliable, discreet, and composed, even in the face of strange occurrences. Many see him as the voice of reason, especially when bizarre rumors circulate through town.

# Randolph Tomaszewski
**Role/Title:** Member of the **Church of the Delayed Blossom**
**Description:** Randolph Tomaszewski is a tall, gaunt young man in his early twenties, with a once-handsome face now marred by deep-set scars. His jerky, disjointed movements hint at his struggle to maintain control over his own body, a sign of the transformation he has undergone since falling under the influence of the **[[Church of the Delayed Blossom]]**. Once a bright and promising medical student, Randolph’s academic and medical career was cut short when the cult ensnared him. Now, he teeters on the edge of madness, driven by the curse that has turned him into a ghast—an undead creature with a decaying body and a mind slowly unraveling.
**Background:** Randolph was born to a Polish immigrant family and, despite facing hardships, excelled academically. He was on track to become a doctor before encountering the Church. Now, Randolph lives in the shadows, avoiding authorities and seeking both to understand his condition and to free himself from the cult’s control. His transformation into a ghast has left him obsessed with necromancy, and he is working tirelessly to perfect rituals that will allow him to raise a zombie army to fight back against the cult. However, this goal has slowly consumed him, leaving Randolph increasingly paranoid and detached from reality.
**Cult Role:** Within the Church of the Delayed Blossom, Randolph is valued for his medical knowledge and his burgeoning skills in necromancy. His curse, though debilitating, has made him a useful tool to the cult’s leaders, who view him as a harbinger of what they can achieve through their twisted rituals. Though Randolph resents the control the Church exerts over him, his dependence on their knowledge and resources leaves him trapped. He dreams of breaking free, but the dark magics of the Church have woven too tightly around him, both physically and mentally.
**Goals:**
- **Freedom from the Church**: Randolph's primary goal is to sever his connection with the Church of the Delayed Blossom, reversing or at least controlling his transformation into a ghast.
- **Necromantic Power**: His fascination with raising the dead has overtaken him, and he now seeks to create the perfect zombie under his control, believing it to be the key to freeing himself from the cult.
- **Destroy the Church**: Randolph secretly harbors a desire to strike back against the cult that turned him into this monster, but his actions are erratic, and his mental state deteriorates as he delves deeper into forbidden knowledge.
**Relationships:**
- **[[Leonid Kuznetsov-Keeper|Leonid "Lenny" Kuznetsov]]**: Randolph met Lenny during one of his thefts from Dominick’s Grocery, where Lenny works the night shift. Recognizing Lenny’s violent tendencies, Randolph manipulated him into joining the Church, taking him under his wing as a kind of enforcer and apprentice. Though Lenny serves him, Randolph struggles to control the young man, whose violent nature may one day become more of a liability than an asset.
- **[[Jan Ducochik|Sgt. Jan Ducochik]]**: Randolph has had limited interactions with Ducochik, who once showed him kindness when they crossed paths. Though he harbors no loyalty to the officer, Randolph has considered reaching out to Ducochik as a potential ally in his fight against the Church, despite the risk of revealing his cursed nature.
## Role/Title:
- Member of [[Church of the Delayed Blossom]]
## Brief Description: 
Randolph is a tall, gaunt young man in his early twenties with a mop of dark hair and haunted eyes. His once-handsome face is now marred by deep-set scars, making him appear older than his years. He moves with an almost jerky motions, as if he's not entirely in control of his body.
## Biography:
- Background: Randolph was born to a Polish immigrant family who moved to Watashuka when he was a child. Despite facing hardships growing up, he managed to excel academically and was on track to become a doctor before falling under the influence of the Church of the Delayed Blossom.
- Personality: Randolph is introverted, often appearing withdrawn or disoriented due to his medication. He can be charming when he wants to be but also has a tendency towards volatility and aggression, especially when stressed or provoked. His once-sharp mind now seems clouded, and he struggles with memory and focus.
- Motivations: Randolph's primary goal is to find a way to free himself from the Church of the Delayed Blossom's control. He wants to regain his independence and protect others from the cult's influence. Additionally, he seeks insight into his condition and a means to strike back against those who have wronged him.
- Secrets: Randolph has been experimenting with necromancy, attempting to create a zombie that will obey his commands. He believes this creature will help him fight against the Church of the Delayed Blossom and uncover the truth behind his transformation into a ghast.
## Relationships:
* Sgt. Jan Ducochik: Randolph has had some limited interactions with Sgt. Ducochik, who has shown him kindness and concern despite not knowing about his involvement in the cult. This interaction has left a positive impression on Randolph, making him more likely to trust or confide in the police officer.
* Leonid "Lenny" Kuznetsov: Randolph met [[Leonid Kuznetsov]] while Randolph was stealing food and supplies from the store, Dominick's, where Lenny works. Randolph recognized something about Lenny and began to take him under his wing. Within weeks, Lenny was recruited into the cult. Lenny acts as both Randolph's apprentice and servant. 
## Hobbies (or rather, obsessions):
- Necromancy: Randolph is fixated on raising the dead and harnessing their power to further his goals. He spends much of his free time researching ancient rituals and experimenting with corpse reanimation.
- Underground Exploration: Randolph has developed an interest in exploring the extensive tunnel system beneath Watashuka, inspired by his escape from the medical facility where he was being held.
## Fears:
- Fear of Manipulation: Randolph is terrified of being controlled or manipulated by others, especially those within the Church of the Delayed Blossom. This fear drives much of his behavior and motivates him to find a way to break free from their influence.
- Fear of Failure: Randolph fears that he will not be able to complete his plans against the cult or find a way to reverse his transformation into a ghast. This fear often manifests as self-doubt or indecision.
## Goals:
- Freedom from the Church of the Delayed Blossom: Randolph's ultimate goal is to sever his connection with the cult and gain control over his own life once again.
- Uncovering the Truth: He wants to discover what caused his transformation into a ghast and find a way to reverse or manage it, ultimately using this knowledge to strike back against those who have harmed him.

[[Ronnie Regan]]
## Overview
Ronnie Regan’s life appears innocent and carefree on the surface, but her growing interest in the occult has already drawn the attention of dangerous forces in Watashuka. Her insatiable curiosity and eagerness to uncover hidden truths have led her to start asking questions that might be better left unanswered. As the assistant to [[Sly Coolstein]], Ronnie is unknowingly protected from darker forces by the librarian himself. Sly, a member of the [[Brotherhood of the Gate Unveiled]], shields her from the cult’s influence, recognizing the rare purity she represents in a town tainted by eldritch corruption.
However, there is a shadow over Ronnie's life she doesn’t even realize: [[Leonid Kuznetsov-Keeper|Lenny Kuznetsov]] has developed a dark obsession with her, secretly stalking her without her knowledge. While Lenny has not yet made his intentions known, his dangerous fixation adds a layer of threat to her otherwise carefree world.
Despite her enthusiasm for the occult, Ronnie is unaware of how close she truly is to the supernatural forces at work in [[Watashuka]]. She is drawn to the strange, unable to resist the allure of old rituals and forgotten legends. Some cult members have started to take notice of her. There are whispers within the Brotherhood that Ronnie could either be recruited as an asset or removed as a potential threat. But for now, Ronnie remains blissfully unaware of the dark paths she treads, her only aim being to uncover the mysteries that fascinate her so much.
Sly continues to protect Ronnie as best he can, carefully curating her access to certain texts, and quietly steering her away from dangerous knowledge. But as Ronnie grows older and more determined in her search for the truth, it’s only a matter of time before she stumbles onto something that Sly—or the cult—won’t be able to hide from her.
## *Biography:*
- *Background:* Ronnie was raised by her free-spirited parents, who moved back to Watashuka after living in various communes and counterculture hubs around the country. She grew up surrounded by stories of their adventures and became captivated by the idea of hidden knowledge and secret histories. Her love for books and the occult led her to volunteer at the Peach St. Library, where she now works as an assistant.
- *Personality:* Ronnie is curious, imaginative, and always eager to learn more about the world around her. She's a bit clumsy and often loses track of time when engrossed in a book or conversation. Her enthusiasm can sometimes border on naivety, but she has a good heart and genuinely cares for others.
- *Motivations:* Ronnie's primary goal is to uncover hidden truths about the world and its history, especially those connected to the occult. She hopes that her experiences at the library will lead her to discover something extraordinary. Additionally, she wants to protect Watashuka from any threats lurking in its shadows.
- *Secrets:* Ronnie has started to notice strange occurrences around town but hasn't yet put all the pieces together. Unbeknownst to her, some of the cult members have taken an interest in her curiosity and are considering whether they should recruit or eliminate her.
## **Hobbies:**
- *Drawing and Painting:* Ronnie enjoys expressing her creativity through art, often incorporating occult symbols and creatures from mythology into her work.
- *Investigative Journalism (in spirit):* Alongside her friends, Ronnie conducts informal investigations into local legends and rumors, hoping to uncover hidden truths about Watashuka's past.
## **Fears:**
- *Fear of Ridicule:* Ronnie fears being laughed at or ridiculed for her beliefs, especially regarding politics. Due to her parents' hippie background, she has faced teasing because of her name and their shared dislike for President Ronald Reagan.
- *Claustrophobia:* Ronnie harbors a deep-seated fear of being trapped or confined, stemming from a childhood incident involving an old root cellar.
## **Goals:**
- *Publishing Her Discoveries:* One of Ronnie's long-term goals is to write and publish a book about her experiences and discoveries in Watashuka, hoping that it will inspire others to explore the mysteries hidden within their own towns.
- *Protecting Watashuka:* Ronnie wants to use her growing knowledge of local lore and legends to safeguard her hometown from any supernatural threats or cult activity.

# **Ronnie "Moonglow" Regan**
*As the afternoon sun filters through the dusty windows of the Peach Street Library, Ronnie hums softly to herself while shelving a stack of books. Her fingers trace over the spines of old volumes as if they hold untold secrets waiting to be discovered. She pushes her glasses up her nose, curls falling across her face as she eagerly flips through a dusty tome of local legends. "Have you ever heard of the Cold Flames at Stratton Mill?" she asks Sly, her green eyes lighting up with curiosity. It's clear that Ronnie's passion for the unknown runs deep, and those who know her find it hard not to get caught up in her excitement.*
**Role/Title:** Assistant Librarian at [[Peach Street Library]], Junior at [[North High School]]
**Description:** Ronnie Regan, a 17-year-old junior at North High School, has a vibrant personality and an infectious curiosity about the world, especially the mysteries hidden within it. With her cascade of curly red hair and her round glasses, Ronnie is known for her distinctive thrift-store style, inspired by her parents' hippie past. She spends most of her free time volunteering at the Peach Street Library, assisting the head librarian, [[Sly Coolstein]], in organizing books and cataloging old manuscripts. Though young, Ronnie is already becoming somewhat of a local expert on Watashuka’s folklore, thanks to her boundless enthusiasm for the occult.
