[[Sly Coolstein]]
## Overview
Beneath his scholarly, absent-minded persona, **Sly Coolstein** is more than just a harmless librarian. As a long-time member of the [[Brotherhood of the Gate Unveiled]], Sly has spent decades studying eldritch lore and arcane rituals, though his motivation is not power, but knowledge. For Sly, the cult’s activities are an academic pursuit, an extension of his deep fascination with ancient texts and forgotten mysteries. His involvement in the Brotherhood stems from intellectual curiosity rather than ambition, but this detachment makes him dangerous. He often fails to recognize the full consequences of dabbling in forbidden powers, treating them as abstract concepts rather than real threats.
Sly maintains his position in the library as both a cover and a means of accessing rare occult manuscripts. [[Peach Street Library]] houses an impressive collection of books, including some that hold dark and dangerous knowledge. Most of the town’s residents view him as an eccentric and harmless figure, which suits him perfectly. They have no idea that some of the "old books" he guards so carefully contain rituals capable of opening gates to other dimensions.
Though Sly is a loyal member of the Brotherhood, there is one person he protects above all else: [[Ronnie Regan]], his young assistant. Sly has developed a paternal affection for Ronnie, seeing her as a symbol of the innocence he lost long ago. While the Brotherhood often views Ronnie’s curiosity in the occult as a potential tool, Sly works quietly behind the scenes to shield her from the cult’s darker practices. He carefully curates the knowledge she’s exposed to, preventing her from stumbling upon anything truly dangerous.
However, Sly’s protective efforts are becoming more strained. He knows that the Brotherhood may eventually take notice of Ronnie’s growing involvement in local occult matters. Though he tries to keep her out of harm’s way, the forces in Watashuka are difficult to avoid. Sly is aware that Ronnie’s naive curiosity could put her at risk, and he dreads the day when he may have to choose between his loyalty to the Brotherhood and his desire to protect her.
Sly also hides a deep fear that his detachment from real-world consequences may one day lead him to make a catastrophic mistake. His mind is filled with rituals and forbidden knowledge, and though he sees himself as an observer of the occult, he knows that simply observing is sometimes enough to invite disaster.
- **Role**: Sly Coolstein is the head (and only full-time) librarian at the _Peach Street Library_, [[Watashuka]]’s only public library. An older, bookish man, Sly is deeply committed to the academic world, fascinated by texts both ancient and modern. His life revolves around the library, and he can often be found pouring over obscure reference books and historical documents. Despite being a member in good standing with [[Brotherhood of the Gate Unveiled]], Sly seems harmless at first glance. He’s often teased by children who frequent the library, but he rarely seems bothered by it, retreating into his books to avoid confrontation. Despite his allegiance to the Brotherhood, he protects his assistant, _[[Ronnie Regan]]_..
- **Age**: Early 60s (1983)
- **Appearance**: Sly has the stereotypical appearance of a scholarly recluse. He is thin and pale, with thinning gray hair and large, round glasses that seem perpetually perched on the end of his nose. He typically wears outdated suits or sweater vests, often a bit frayed at the edges, giving him the appearance of someone who cares little for personal presentation. His hands are almost always stained with ink, and he carries the smell of old books with him wherever he goes. Sly’s appearance is largely forgettable, which suits him fine, as it allows him to blend into the background of the town’s happenings while he quietly pursues his own interests.
- **Personality**: Sly is the epitome of the absent-minded academic—intensely knowledgeable but completely inept at handling real-world situations. He has a passion for arcane knowledge and historical texts, and his mind is often so preoccupied with esoteric subjects that he struggles to make basic connections in everyday life. Despite being involved in the _Brotherhood of the Gate Unveiled_, he approaches the cult with the same academic detachment as he does any other subject, focusing more on the knowledge and rituals rather than the consequences of their actions. Sly is not malicious by nature, but his involvement in the cult stems from a desire to learn, not from a desire to wield power. This detachment makes him somewhat of an enigma—dangerous in his ignorance but not inherently malevolent.
- **Public Role**:
    - **Peach Street Library**: Sly has been the head of the _Peach Street Library_ for decades, and most of the town sees him as little more than a quirky, eccentric figure who lives among the books. The library itself is a small, underfunded institution, and Sly spends much of his time organizing books, cataloging old documents, and occasionally helping the few patrons who visit. He takes pride in the library's collection, especially the older, rarer texts, some of which are connected to the occult—though he never advertises that fact.
    - **Teasing by Children**: Sly’s name, _Sly Coolstein_, has long been a source of amusement for the town’s children, who come up with a variety of nicknames to tease him. Common taunts include:
        - **“Sly Foolstein”**
        - **“The Cool Nerd”**
        - **“Sneaky Sly”**:
        - **“Dewey Decimal Dingus”**
        - "NOT Coolstein"
    - Sly is largely unfazed by these teases, though there is a part of him that longs for more respect. He typically responds by muttering under his breath or feigning indifference, but the constant teasing has made him even more reclusive.
- **Relationship with Ronnie Regan**: Despite being deeply entrenched in the _Brotherhood of the Gate Unveiled_, Sly has a soft spot for his assistant. Though Ronnie is very interested in the occult, Sly has worked hard to make sure she does not suspect him. In return, he has protected her many times over the years. Most recently from a stalking attempt by [[Leonid Kuznetsov-Keeper|Lenny Kuznetsov]].  Sly sees her as a rare source of innocence and purity—qualities that are increasingly hard to find in Watashuka. Sly protects Ronnie out of a paternal instinct, seeing her as someone who needs to be shielded from the darker forces at work in the town and works hard to keep her away from the Brotherhood’s activities.
    - **Ronnie’s Loyalty**: Ronnie often helps Sly with various tasks at the library, from shelving books to assisting with the cataloging of ancient texts. She has no idea of Sly’s involvement with the Brotherhood or the dangerous knowledge hidden within the library’s more obscure collections. Sly goes out of his way to keep Ronnie from discovering the darker secrets of his life. When she seeks out new occult information, Sly carefully curates what information she has access to.
- **Cult Involvement**:
    - **Brotherhood of the Gate Unveiled**: Sly is a member of the _Brotherhood of the Gate Unveiled_, a cult dedicated to using eldritch knowledge and rituals to access forbidden powers. While other cult members are motivated by ambition or a thirst for power, Sly is primarily driven by academic curiosity. To him, the rituals and texts are simply extensions of his study, things to be cataloged and analyzed rather than feared. This detachment makes him dangerous, as he often fails to grasp the full consequences of the dark forces he’s aligning himself with.
    - **Knowledge-Seeker, Not a Leader**: Sly’s position in the Brotherhood is that of a scholar rather than a leader. He is valued for his deep knowledge of ancient texts and his access to the library’s rare collections, but he has little interest in wielding power or influence. His primary concern is the preservation and understanding of knowledge, even if that knowledge is forbidden or dangerous. Sly’s fellow cultists view him as useful but somewhat out of touch with the true goals of the Brotherhood.
- **Potential Hooks for Investigators**:
    - **Access to Forbidden Knowledge**: Sly’s vast knowledge of ancient texts and occult rituals could make him a valuable ally for investigators—if they can get past his absent-minded demeanor and recognize the depth of his involvement in the Brotherhood. Sly’s library contains rare texts that might hold the key to understanding the supernatural forces at work in Watashuka, though gaining his trust will be a challenge.
    - **Protecting Ronnie**: If investigators discover Sly’s protective relationship with Ronnie, they may use it as leverage to convince him to share what he knows. Sly’s desire to keep Ronnie safe could be a point of vulnerability, one that investigators might exploit to get him to cooperate.
    - **Unintentional Villainy**: Sly’s academic curiosity and inability to connect the dots make him a dangerous figure, even if he is not overtly malevolent. His involvement with the Brotherhood might lead him to unwittingly release dark forces or initiate rituals that threaten the town. Investigators might need to decide whether to stop Sly outright or try to guide him away from the more dangerous aspects of his research.
- **Public Perception**: To most of Watashuka’s residents, Sly is a harmless oddball—a reclusive librarian who spends more time with books than with people. The town’s children enjoy teasing him, seeing him as an easy target, but adults generally view him as harmless and eccentric. His connection to the Brotherhood is known only to a select few, and most of the town has no idea that the unassuming librarian is involved in something far more sinister.

# Sly Coolstein
On any given day, Sly can be found behind the library’s main desk, surrounded by stacks of old books and the faint smell of aging paper. He adjusts his glasses and peers at an ancient tome, engrossed in its contents, oblivious to the children giggling behind him as they whisper yet another teasing nickname. One of the kids calls out, "Hey, Sly Foolstein!" He mumbles something incomprehensible under his breath but doesn’t look up. He’s too deep into a translation of an obscure 15th-century manuscript to care. Ronnie, his bright-eyed assistant, pokes her head out from between the shelves and gives him a grin. She knows Sly’s mind is a maze of ancient knowledge, and though she tries her best to keep up, she’s content to let him get lost in his books.
**Description:** Sly Coolstein, the head librarian of [[Watashuka|Watashuka’s]] [[Peach Street Library]], has been a fixture in the town for decades. With thinning gray hair, large round glasses, and a perpetually ink-stained vest, Sly is the picture of a bookish recluse. His unassuming nature and deep knowledge of obscure literature make him a quiet, though essential, part of the community. Despite his awkward demeanor and forgettable appearance, Sly is always willing to help those who share his love for books and history.

[[Amish]]
# **Amish Protectors (Keeper Entry)**
- **Secret Role**:  
    Unbeknownst to the people of [[Watashuka]], the Amish are far more than simple farmers. They are the covert guardians of ancient knowledge passed down through generations, tasked with protecting the region from supernatural forces. The Amish were drawn to Watashuka because of its ley lines and the convergence of dark powers in the area. Their role is to act as the last line of defense against malevolent entities, dangerous cults, and even the U.S. government’s secret operations under **[[Project Caroline]]**. The Amish view themselves as protectors of the land, using their knowledge of the supernatural to combat the evil forces that others, either unwittingly or deliberately, attempt to unleash.
- **Methods**:  
    The Amish employ ancient rituals, herbal remedies, and spiritual practices to keep dark forces at bay. They have developed a network of hidden sanctuaries and spiritual sites throughout the region, where they conduct their rituals in secret. These sites are protected both physically and spiritually, making them difficult for outsiders to discover or infiltrate. Only a select few within the Amish community are fully aware of the supernatural threats they are facing, and they maintain strict secrecy about their true purpose.
    - **Disrupting Cult Rituals**: The Amish actively work against the local cults, particularly the **[[Church of the Delayed Blossom]]**. They sabotage rituals and attempt to neutralize the mystical energies that the cults are trying to harness. Their focus is primarily on preventing the summoning of **[[Shub-Niggurath]]**, whom they see as the greatest threat to the region.
    - **Guarding Sacred Sites**: The Amish protect certain ley line intersections and other spiritually significant locations, which they believe are key to maintaining balance and keeping dark forces from gaining too much power. These sites are carefully guarded, with some overlapping Ho-Chunk sacred grounds, leading to occasional tension between the two groups.
    - **Monitoring the [[Ho-Chunk]]**: While the Amish respect the Ho-Chunk’s ancient spiritual practices, they remain wary of their methods. The two groups have an uneasy alliance, cooperating when necessary to counteract supernatural threats but keeping their distance otherwise. The Amish keep a close eye on Ho-Chunk rituals to ensure that they don’t inadvertently unleash the forces both groups are fighting.
- **Interactions with Other Factions**:
    - **[[Project Caroline]]**: The Amish view the U.S. government’s experiments under **Project Caroline** as reckless and dangerous. They are particularly concerned about the government’s attempts to manipulate time and space using the ley lines, believing these efforts could lead to catastrophic consequences. While the Amish avoid direct confrontation with government agents, they work quietly to disrupt these operations, using their deep knowledge of the land and its supernatural properties to undermine the government’s experiments.
    - **The Cults**: The Amish are locked in a quiet but active battle against the two primary cults in the region: the **Church of the Delayed Blossom** and the **Brotherhood of the Gate Unveiled**. They see **Shub-Niggurath** as the greater of the two threats, though they remain vigilant against both. The Amish attempt to rescue individuals targeted by the cults, offering them sanctuary within their community, though these actions are always done in secrecy to avoid drawing attention.
    - **Lutheran Church**: The Amish see the **Lutheran Church** as potential allies in the fight against the supernatural, though they are aware that the church is largely unaware of the true scope of the conflict. The Amish occasionally provide subtle guidance to Lutheran leaders, hoping to strengthen the church’s spiritual defenses, but they are careful not to reveal too much, fearing that the church’s naivety could make it a target for manipulation by dark forces.
    - **Ho-Chunk**: The Amish respect the Ho-Chunk’s ancient knowledge, but their relationship remains one of cautious cooperation. Both groups share a common goal in protecting the land from supernatural threats, but they have different methods and traditions. The Amish monitor Ho-Chunk activities to ensure that their rituals do not accidentally unleash the very forces both groups are trying to contain.
- **Impact on Watashuka**:  
    The Amish’s covert activities contribute to the strange and sometimes inexplicable phenomena around Watashuka. Their efforts to disrupt cult rituals and protect ley lines have kept the worst of the supernatural forces at bay, though their secrecy has led to rumors and speculation among the townspeople. Their presence plays a critical role in maintaining a delicate balance between the supernatural forces in the region, though few outsiders are aware of the full extent of their involvement.
- **Activities**:
    - **Sabotaging College Research**: The Amish quietly infiltrate Caroline College’s agricultural programs to slow down research that might accidentally tap into the dark forces hidden within the land. They see the college’s experiments as dangerous meddling with forces that are better left undisturbed.
    - **Combating Created Monsters**: The Amish take it upon themselves to destroy the **Dark Young** and other creatures created by the cult of **Shub-Niggurath**. These battles are fought in secret, with the Amish using their knowledge of ancient rituals and herbal remedies to neutralize the monstrosities.
# Amish Protectors
 The Amish in the Watashuka region are covert protectors, using ancient knowledge to defend against supernatural forces. They have a complicated relationship with the Ho-Chunk people and the Lutheran Church, which remains largely unaware of the true threat.
## Overview  
   - The area surrounding Watashuka is home to a large and seemingly traditional Amish population. They are known for their simple, agrarian lifestyle, shunning modern technology and maintaining a close-knit, self-sufficient community. The Amish are generally seen as peaceful and reserved, with little interaction with the broader town beyond necessary trade and commerce.
## **Secret Role:**
  - Unbeknownst to the locals, the Amish presence in the Watashuka region is far from accidental. They are the guardians of an ancient knowledge passed down through generations, tasked with protecting the world from the malevolent forces that others unknowingly or deliberately seek to unleash. The Amish view themselves as the last line of defense against the supernatural entities and dark powers at play in Watashuka.
  - The Amish are particularly focused on countering the efforts of the two warring cults as well as the U.S. government's ongoing operations under **Project Caroline**. They believe these factions are meddling with forces beyond human comprehension, threatening to bring about catastrophic consequences.
  - The Amish see the **Lutheran Church** as potential allies, albeit ones who are largely unaware of the true scale of the supernatural conflict and one who is often misled, fooled or manipulated by forces of evil. Similarly, they have a complicated relationship with the **Ho-Chunk people**, who possess their own ancient knowledge and spiritual practices. While the Amish respect the Ho-Chunk's traditions, they remain cautious, recognizing that the Ho-Chunk have their own goals and methods for dealing with the supernatural.
## **Methods:**
  - The Amish use a combination of ancient rituals, herbal remedies, and a deep understanding of the supernatural to keep the dark forces at bay. Their methods are subtle and often go unnoticed by the untrained eye, appearing as mere traditions or superstitions to outsiders.
  - They have developed a network of hidden safehouses, sanctuaries, and spiritual sites throughout the region, where they conduct their rituals and plan their strategies. These locations are well-guarded, both physically and spiritually, making them difficult for outsiders to discover or infiltrate.
  - The Amish maintain strict secrecy about their true purpose, even among their own community members. Only a select few within the community—those chosen and trained in the ancient ways—are fully aware of the ongoing supernatural battle and their role in it.
## **Interactions with Other Factions:**
  - [[Project Caroline]]: The Amish view the government's continued experiments as reckless and dangerous. While they generally avoid direct confrontation, they work quietly to undermine the government's efforts, using their knowledge of the land and supernatural to disrupt operations.
  - The Cults: The Amish are actively working against the cults, using their own rituals and protective measures to neutralize the cults' influence. They have been known to rescue individuals targeted by the cults, though these actions are always done in secrecy. There primary 'enemy' is the [[Church of the Delayed Blossom]]. While [[Brotherhood of the Gate Unveiled]] is a concerning group for the Amish, they see [[Shub-Niggurath]] as the bigger threat.
  - [[Lutheran Church]]: While the Lutheran Church is largely unaware of the supernatural dangers lurking in Watashuka, the Amish see them as potential allies. The Amish may occasionally influence church leaders or provide subtle guidance, hoping to strengthen the church's spiritual defenses. However, they also are very aware of how fragile the church is in regard to that defense. The Lutherans are potential allies that are being manipulated into possibly becoming the enemy. 
  - [[Ho-Chunk]] The Amish respect the Ho-Chunk's ancient knowledge and spiritual practices. However, they remain wary, understanding that the Ho-Chunk have their own agenda in dealing with the supernatural. The two groups have an uneasy alliance, cooperating when necessary but keeping their distance otherwise.
## **Impact on Watashuka:**
  - The Amish's covert activities contribute to the strange and sometimes inexplicable phenomena that occur around Watashuka. Their presence, while largely unnoticed by the town’s population, plays a critical role in maintaining the delicate balance between the forces at work in the region. They also try to protect the town by offering untainted foods and goods.
  - Their actions also add a layer of mystery and tension to the town's atmosphere, with rumors and whispers circulating about odd occurrences or unexplained events near Amish farms. However, few would suspect the true nature of the Amish’s involvement in the supernatural struggle.
## Activities
### **Disrupting Cult Rituals:**
   The Amish are secretly sabotaging rituals performed by the cult of [[Shub-Niggurath]], particularly around the farmlands. They work quietly to neutralize mystical energies without drawing attention.
### **Guarding and Creating Sacred Sites:**
   The Amish maintain hidden sanctuaries in the countryside, where they conduct rituals to keep malevolent entities at bay. These sites sometimes overlap with Ho-Chunk sacred grounds, creating tension between the two factions.
### **Recruiting Allies in the Lutheran Church:**
   The Amish are quietly identifying sympathetic members within the Lutheran Church to form a secret alliance against the cults. They work to reveal hidden truths to certain key figures, hoping to bolster the church’s resistance to evil forces.
### **Monitoring the Ho-Chunk People:**
  While respecting their traditions, the Amish are secretly keeping tabs on the Ho-Chunk, ensuring that their own ancient rituals don’t accidentally unleash the very forces both groups are fighting.
### **Using Agricultural Connections:**  
The Amish manipulate the agricultural supply chains in Watashuka to subtly disrupt the cult’s efforts to use local resources for their dark rituals.
### **Sabotaging College Research:**
   By infiltrating Caroline College’s agricultural programs, the Amish slow down research that might unwittingly tap into dark forces hidden in the land.
### **Combating Created Monsters:**
   The Amish attempt to destroy the Dark Young and other monstrosities that the cult create.

### **Amish Community**
- **Overview**:  
    The Amish in the [[Watashuka]] region are known for their simple, agrarian lifestyle, adhering to traditional values and shunning modern technology. They live in close-knit, self-sufficient communities and are largely seen as peaceful, humble farmers who avoid interacting with the outside world except for essential trade and commerce. To the people of Watashuka, the Amish represent a way of life removed from the complexities of modern society, focused on faith, family, and farming.
- **History in the Region**:  
    The Amish first arrived in the Watashuka region in the late 19th century, following the destruction of **Prairieville Academy** in 1860. Drawn to the fertile farmlands and the opportunity to live a quiet, devout life, the Amish settlers established their community on the outskirts of town. Their migration to the region was seen as part of a broader movement of Amish groups across the Midwest, seeking isolated areas where they could practice their faith and maintain their traditional ways without interference from modern society.
    The Amish quickly became a respected part of the community, known for their hardworking nature and their ability to produce high-quality agricultural goods. Over the years, they have maintained their cultural and religious identity, staying separate from most of Watashuka’s daily life, though their presence at local markets and interactions with the townspeople have remained constant. Their farms, with their iconic horse-drawn buggies and simple wooden houses, have become a familiar sight in the area, adding to the rural character of the region.
    Despite their isolation, the Amish have seen the area change drastically around them, especially with the expansion of **[[Caroline College]]** and the growing influence of modern technology in Watashuka. While they have largely avoided getting involved in the town’s political or social issues, their commitment to their way of life remains steadfast.
- **Public Role**:  
    The Amish are respected by many in Watashuka for their hard work and strong moral principles. They are seen as devout Christians who have little interest in the town’s social or political matters, preferring to remain isolated within their own communities. They maintain a small presence at local markets, where they sell produce, handmade goods, and dairy products to the townspeople. While they are a part of the fabric of Watashuka life, the Amish keep a polite distance from most public affairs, rarely involving themselves in town events or controversies.
- **Traditional Values**:  
    The Amish are known for their emphasis on family, religious devotion, and a lifestyle free from modern conveniences. Their plain clothing, horse-drawn buggies, and lack of electricity make them stand out, but their dedication to their faith earns them the respect of the broader community. They are seen as honest, hardworking people who live simply and avoid the distractions and corruptions of modern life.
- **Public Perception**:  
    While they are generally well-regarded, the Amish are often seen as mysterious by the people of Watashuka. Their strict separation from modern society leads to occasional rumors and misconceptions, with some townspeople viewing them as overly rigid or old-fashioned. However, most interactions with the Amish are positive, and their contributions to the local economy through farming and crafts are appreciated. Their quiet, humble presence adds a sense of rural tranquility to the area.

---
# The Brotherhood of the Gate Unveiled
This cult follows **[[Yog-Sothoth]]**, the Outer God of time, space, and dimensional gates. The cult is focused on manipulating time and summoning eldritch powers. It was founded by **John W. Sterling** after the destruction of Prairieville Academy. They are focused mainly in the science complex, the communications building and the maintenance buildings.
## Activities
### **Manipulating Time Anomalies:**
The cult is attempting to manipulate the time loop to summon [[Yog-Sothoth]] more directly. Their actions could destabilize the loop further, attracting the attention of [[Project Caroline]] and the [[Amish]].
### **Recruiting College Students:**
The cult is targeting students at [[Caroline College]] for recruitment, using promises of power and knowledge. This scheme is monitored by both the [[Lutheran Church]] and Project Caroline operatives, who are quietly attempting to intervene.
### **Gaining Control of the Obelisk:**
The cult of Yog-Sothoth is waiting to gain control over the Obelisk of Nekhbet, believing it to be a key to unlocking their god’s power. This goal brings them into conflict with both the [[Ho-Chunk]] and the Amish. They ultimate goal is to complete a their final ritual to awaken the 'original god'. They believe a key to this ritual involves the Obelisk as well as other structures on campus.
### **Sabotaging Project Caroline:**
The cult is undermining Project Caroline’s efforts to contain supernatural forces, hoping to further their own agenda. However, some factions within Project Caroline may secretly be working with the cult for their own benefit.
### **Influencing Local Politicians:**
The cult is using its influence to control local politics, ensuring that laws and decisions benefit their long-term plans. This manipulation is largely unknown to other factions, though Project Caroline is beginning to suspect.
### **Gathering Forbidden Knowledge:**
The cult is infiltrating libraries, museums, and archives to collect ancient texts and occult knowledge. This puts them at odds with the Ho-Chunk and the Amish, both of whom seek to keep such knowledge hidden or neutralized.
### **Summoning Eldritch Entities:**
The cult is actively trying to summon smaller eldritch entities as part of larger rituals. These attempts often clash with the Amish’s efforts to stop such activities.
### **Targeting Ho-Chunk Leaders:**
The cult is targeting influential members of the Ho-Chunk community, believing them to be obstacles in their plans. This strategy risks igniting open conflict with the Ho-Chunk people.
### **Undermining the Lutheran Church:**
The cult is quietly working to destabilize the Lutheran Church’s influence in town, hoping to weaken its role as a moral and spiritual guide. They have often placed their own cult members in positions of power within the church over the years (see [[The Baptism of '39-Keeper]]).
### **Experimenting with Time Distortions:**
The cult is conducting experiments to manipulate time for their rituals. It is these rituals that caught the attention of the government and was the catalyst for Project Caroline.

# The Church of the Delayed Blossom
This cult venerates **[[Shub-Niggurath]]**, the "Black Goat of the Woods with a Thousand Young." They practice rituals related to fertility and nature, often in twisted, corrupted forms. The cult was founded by **Eleazar Root** after the destruction of the academy.
## Activities
### **Corrupting the Land:**
The cult is using forbidden rituals to corrupt farmland around [[Watashuka]], feeding their god through desecration of the earth. This scheme brings them into conflict with the [[Amish]] and the [[Ho-Chunk]], who are working to purify the land. This work includes manipulation of the food sources in the town (via interference with local grocery stories and food processing facilities), the manipulation of crops and the creation of Dark Young. To this end, the cult has great control over the agricultural and environmental buildings on campus. The Dark Young can be mistaken for trees. These monsters hide in the experimental orchards, farms and environmental preserves around the area. 
### **Creating Hybrid Creatures:**
The cult is experimenting with dark rituals to create hybrid creatures. These experiments take place in both humans and animal experiments. As such the cult has great control over the teaching hospital and the veterinarian school. They have actively worked to ensure that no other medical faculty, human or animal, is allowed in the region. They are actively experimenting on pregnant humans and animals.  
### **Summoning Shub-Niggurath’s Spawn:**
The cult is attempting to summon smaller spawn of Shub-Niggurath, Dark Young, to strengthen their presence in the region. These rituals are often stopped by the Amish or disrupted by the Ho-Chunk people.
### **Sabotaging the Amish:**
The cult is working to undermine the Amish Protectors, trying to discover their hidden safehouses and spiritual sites. This covert war between the two factions is largely unknown to outsiders.
### **Desecrating Sacred Ho-Chunk Sites:**
The cult is actively desecrating Ho-Chunk sacred sites, using these locations to fuel their dark rituals. This creates direct conflict with the Ho-Chunk people, who work to protect these lands. These sacred sites are one of the reasons the two cults do not expand beyond the region.
### **Spreading Influence through Decadence, Health and Family:**
The cult is subtly infiltrating the people of Watashuka via controlling medical facilities, adult entertainment (see [[The Baptism of '39-Keeper]] and reproductive services.
### **Creating Ghasts:**
The cult is actively attempting to perfect a way of creating ghasts from adult, human, males. These monsters could form an expendable army to project the cult's will.

[[Ho-Chunk]]
### **Ho-Chunk Guardians of the Ley Lines (Keeper Entry)**
---
**Overview:**  
The **Ho-Chunk Nation** holds a far more important and secret role in Watashuka than the public realizes. They are the **guardians of the ley lines**—powerful spiritual pathways that crisscross the region, connecting it to other dimensions and realms of existence. The Ho-Chunk have always known the land they inhabit is a place where the veil between worlds is thin, and for centuries they have worked to protect the region from those who seek to manipulate these energies for dark purposes.
Their spiritual practices, rituals, and deep connection to the **spirit world** have allowed them to defend Watashuka from supernatural forces long before European settlers arrived. The Ho-Chunk view themselves as the last line of defense against the eldritch entities that seek to corrupt the land and enter this world through breaches in the ley lines. These **"Hungry Ones"**, as the Ho-Chunk refer to them, are malevolent beings that feed on the energy of the ley lines and pose a threat to all life.
**Beliefs and Role as Guardians:**  
The Ho-Chunk believe the **ley lines** are conduits of spiritual energy that flow between the physical world and the realms of the **Hungry Ones**. Certain points along these lines, known as **"power nodes"**, are places where the veil between worlds is weakest. If left unguarded, these nodes can be used to summon ancient, destructive entities.
- **Rituals of Protection:** The Ho-Chunk perform sacred rituals to maintain the balance of the ley lines. These rituals include **chanting**, the burning of **sacred herbs**, and the drawing of protective **symbols** on the earth. These traditions are passed down through generations of Ho-Chunk shamans, known as **Wąąk Toošewe**, who are responsible for safeguarding the land’s spiritual energy.
- **Communication with Spirits:** The Ho-Chunk have a profound connection to the **spirit world**, and their shamans are able to communicate with the spirits of nature to maintain harmony between the physical and spiritual realms. These spirits help warn the Ho-Chunk of disturbances in the ley lines and assist in protecting the land from supernatural threats.
- **Awareness of Eldritch Forces:** Unlike the general population of Watashuka, the Ho-Chunk have been aware of the **eldritch entities** that threaten the land for centuries. They refer to these beings as the **Hungry Ones**, who were banished from the natural world long ago but seek to return through the ley lines. The Ho-Chunk believe that once the Hungry Ones are allowed into this world, they will consume all life, and preventing their return is the central mission of their spiritual guardianship.
**Relationship with Other Factions:**
- **Amish:** The Ho-Chunk have a tense but cooperative relationship with the **Amish** community, who arrived in the region in the late 19th century. Both groups share a common goal—protecting the land from supernatural threats—but have vastly different methods and beliefs. The two groups have occasionally worked together to stop particularly dangerous rituals but generally keep their distance, each preferring to operate within their own spiritual frameworks.
- **Project Caroline:** The Ho-Chunk view the government’s **Project Caroline** as a reckless intrusion into the spiritual balance of the region. They are particularly concerned with the project’s experiments involving the manipulation of time and space, which they believe have caused significant disruptions in the ley lines. The Ho-Chunk have repeatedly warned government agents about the dangers of their experiments, but their warnings have gone unheeded.
- **Cults:** The Ho-Chunk are well aware of the **Church of the Delayed Blossom** and the **Brotherhood of the Gate Unveiled**. Both cults seek to exploit the ley lines for their own dark purposes, and the Ho-Chunk see them as constant threats to the land. They have intervened on several occasions to stop rituals conducted by the cults, though they prefer to remain in the shadows, avoiding direct confrontation unless absolutely necessary.
**Key Figures:**
1. **Chief John Nąąhųc (Tree Bear):**
    - **Role:** The spiritual and community leader of the Ho-Chunk in Watashuka, Chief Nąąhųc is responsible for overseeing the protection of the ley lines and ensuring the balance between the physical and spiritual realms is maintained. He is wise and cautious, preferring to observe the encroaching threats before acting decisively.
2. **Jane Deerwalker:**
    - **Role:** One of the most powerful shamans in the Ho-Chunk Nation, Deerwalker is known for her ability to communicate with the spirits and sense disturbances in the ley lines. She is deeply committed to protecting the land from supernatural forces and is actively involved in countering the time loop created by Project Caroline’s experiments.
3. **Keith Redfeather:**
    - **Role:** A young warrior and apprentice to Deerwalker, Redfeather serves as a scout and protector for the Ho-Chunk. He is highly suspicious of outsiders and is quick to act when he perceives a threat to the land. Though inexperienced, his loyalty to his people and the land drives him to confront those who would harm it.
**Key Locations:**
- **Grove of the Two Trees:** A sacred ley line node protected by the Ho-Chunk, where ancient rituals are performed to keep the balance between worlds. The **Church of the Delayed Blossom** has repeatedly attempted to corrupt this site, but the Ho-Chunk have successfully defended it each time.
- **Caves of Lake Mary:** Believed to be a gateway to the spirit world, these caves are guarded by the Ho-Chunk and are considered one of the most important spiritual sites in the region. The caves hold ancient carvings that map the ley lines and warn of the **Hungry Ones**.
**Current Threats:**
- **Project Caroline’s Time Loop:** The Ho-Chunk are deeply concerned with the time loop created by **Dr. Amy Mann**’s experiments. They believe this loop has thrown the ley lines out of balance and threatens to weaken the barriers between worlds, making it easier for the **Hungry Ones** to return.
- **Cults of Watashuka:** The Ho-Chunk are constantly monitoring the activities of the **Church of the Delayed Blossom** and the **Brotherhood of the Gate Unveiled**, whose rituals could open breaches in the ley lines, allowing ancient entities to enter the physical world.
**Activities:**
- **Protecting Sacred Sites:** The Ho-Chunk work quietly to protect their sacred sites from exploitation by the government and the cults. They conduct regular rituals to maintain the spiritual balance and prevent the ley lines from being corrupted.
- **Neutralizing Cult Rituals:** The Ho-Chunk are actively working to disrupt the rituals of the cults operating in Watashuka, using their spiritual knowledge to neutralize dark powers before they can take root.
# **Ho-Chunk Guardians of the Ley Lines**
(_The Silent Protectors of Watashuka’s Ancient Power_)
## **Overview**:  
The **Ho-Chunk Nation**, also known as the **People of the Sacred Voice**, have lived on the land surrounding Watashuka for centuries, long before European settlers arrived. Deeply connected to the natural world and the spiritual energies that flow through the earth, the Ho-Chunk are the ancient protectors of the region’s **ley lines**—the powerful, invisible pathways that connect the land to the **supernatural realms**.
The Ho-Chunk have always known that the land they call home is special, a place where the boundaries between worlds are thinner, and where spiritual energy pools in certain sacred sites. These ley lines are both a blessing and a curse, offering great power but also attracting dark forces that seek to exploit them. The Ho-Chunk’s traditional role has been to guard these sites, using their spiritual knowledge and rituals to protect the land from those who would misuse its power—whether they be human or something far older and more dangerous.
Though their numbers have dwindled, the Ho-Chunk continue to fulfill this ancient duty, even in the face of growing threats from government projects, local cults, and the encroaching modern world.
## **Beliefs and Role as Guardians**:
The Ho-Chunk believe that the **ley lines** are pathways that connect the natural world to the **spiritual realms**, channels through which energy flows between different dimensions. Certain points along these lines, known as **"power nodes,"** are places where the veil between worlds is thinnest, and where great spiritual power can be harnessed—either for good or ill.
For the Ho-Chunk, these sites are sacred. They see themselves as the appointed guardians of the land, responsible for maintaining the balance between the natural and supernatural worlds. Their role is to ensure that the ley lines remain undisturbed, and that the **ancient entities** that dwell beyond the veil are not summoned or awakened.
- **Rituals of Protection**: The Ho-Chunk use **rituals** passed down through generations to safeguard the ley lines. These rituals involve chanting, the use of **sacred herbs**, and the drawing of protective **symbols** on the earth. The Ho-Chunk know that certain rituals must be performed regularly to keep the ley lines in balance, preventing any one group from harnessing too much of their power.
- **Communication with Spirits**: The Ho-Chunk maintain a deep connection to the **spirit world**. Their shamans, known as **"Wąąk Toošewe,"** act as intermediaries between the human world and the spirits of the land. These shamans can sense disturbances in the ley lines and are able to communicate with the **spirits of nature** to help keep the land protected.
- **Eldritch Awareness**: Unlike the local settlers, who only recently discovered the dangers of the **eldritch forces** lurking beneath Watashuka, the Ho-Chunk have long been aware of the presence of these beings. They refer to these ancient entities as **"the [[Hungry Ones]]"**, spirits who were banished from the natural world long ago and now seek to return through breaches in the ley lines. The Ho-Chunk believe that once the Hungry Ones are allowed into this world, they will consume all life, and their return must be prevented at all costs.
---
## **Relationship with the Amish**:
Though the Ho-Chunk and the [[Amish]] come from vastly different cultural backgrounds, they have shared a common purpose since the late **19th century**: the protection of the land from **supernatural threats**. The alliance between the two groups was born out of necessity in the **1890s**, when a failed ritual by [[Church of the Delayed Blossom]] nearly brought an **eldritch entity** into the world.
- **The Alliance**: At first, the Amish and the Ho-Chunk were wary of one another. The Amish, with their Christian beliefs, were initially suspicious of the Ho-Chunk’s spiritual practices, while the Ho-Chunk saw the Amish as outsiders who did not understand the land’s deeper significance. However, after the **Blizzard of 1888**, the two groups found common ground in their shared desire to protect the land from the forces that sought to corrupt it. Though the alliance is largely unspoken, both groups respect one another and often work together in secret to combat threats to the ley lines.
- **Maintaining Distance**: Despite their cooperation, the Ho-Chunk and Amish maintain separate spheres of influence. The Ho-Chunk focus on the **ley lines** and **sacred sites**, while the Amish use their **herbal magic** and **symbolic protections** to guard their farmlands and the surrounding area. The two groups communicate infrequently, but when major disturbances occur, they come together to combine their knowledge and abilities.
## **Recent Conflicts**:
### **Government Encroachment (1930s-Present)**:  
The Ho-Chunk have become increasingly concerned with the **U.S. government’s** activities in the region, particularly the founding of [[Project Caroline]] in the 1940s. Though the government claims its experiments are purely scientific, the Ho-Chunk know that the government is tampering with forces beyond their control, disturbing the ley lines in dangerous ways. The Ho-Chunk elders have issued warnings to the local authorities, but these have been ignored or dismissed as superstitious nonsense.
### Shamanic Observations:
The Ho-Chunk shamans have noted strange fluctuations in the ley lines ever since [[Amy Mann|Dr. Amy Mann]] experiments in the early 1980s. They believe that the creation of the **time loop** in 1983 is a direct result of the government’s meddling with the ley lines, and they have been working tirelessly to find a way to break the loop and restore balance to the land.
### **Cults of Watashuka**:  
The Ho-Chunk have long been aware of the two rival cults operating in Watashuka. Both cults seek to exploit the ley lines for their own dark purposes, and the Ho-Chunk view them as a constant threat. 
- [[Church of the Delayed Blossom]]: The Ho-Chunk see the **Church of the Delayed Blossom**, followers of [[Shub-Niggurath]], as dangerous because of their focus on corrupting the natural world. The church’s fertility rituals threaten to warp the land, and the Ho-Chunk have intervened on numerous occasions to stop these rituals before they could come to fruition.
- [[Brotherhood of the Gate Unveiled]]: The Ho-Chunk are more wary the **Brotherhood of the Gate Unveiled**, whose experiments with time manipulation could have catastrophic consequences for the entire region, the world or even the universe. The Brotherhood’s attempts to create rifts in time threaten to unravel the fabric of reality, and the Ho-Chunk have dedicated themselves to preventing these rituals from succeeding.
### **Key Ho-Chunk Figures**:
1. **Chief John Nąąhųc (Tree Bear)**:
    - **Role**: The current leader of the Ho-Chunk in the Watashuka region, Chief John Nąąhųc is a respected elder who has guided his people through many hardships. He is deeply connected to the spiritual forces of the land and takes his role as guardian of the ley lines very seriously. Nąąhųc is stoic and cautious, believing that the best way to protect the land is through quiet vigilance and careful intervention. He has worked closely with the Amish when necessary but prefers to keep his people out of the town’s politics. He is known for his love of Dr. Pepper.
2. **Jane Deerwalker**:
    - **Role**: One of the most powerful **Wąąk Toošewe** (shamans) in the Ho-Chunk community, Jane Deerwalker is responsible for maintaining the spiritual balance of the ley lines. She has the ability to sense disturbances in the spiritual realm and often serves as the first line of defense when the cults or government experiments cause disruptions. Jane is known for her wisdom and is often consulted by Chief Nąąhųc on matters related to the supernatural. She is particularly wary of the time loop created by Dr. Amy Mann and has been working on a way to counteract its effects.
3. **Ketih Redfeather**:
    - **Role**: A young Ho-Chunk warrior and apprentice to Deerwalker, Keith Redfeather is fiercely protective of his people and the land. He often serves as a scout, keeping an eye on the activities of both the cults and the government. Though he lacks the spiritual experience of his elders, Keith is brave and quick to act, often clashing with his more cautious superiors. He is deeply suspicious of outsiders and is particularly hostile toward Project Caroline, seeing it as a direct threat to the ley lines.
---
## **Key Locations**:
### **Grove of the Two Trees**:
This **sacred site** is a powerful ley line node where two ancient oak trees stand, their roots intertwined in a way that suggests they have grown together for centuries. The Ho-Chunk believe this grove is one of the most important power points in the region and perform regular rituals here to maintain balance. [[Church of the Delayed Blossom]] has attempted to use this site for mutation rituals, but the Ho-Chunk have successfully defended it each time.
### **The Caves of Lake Mary**:
These caves, located near Lake Mary, are believed to be an entry point to the spirit world. The Ho-Chunk used to use the caves for their most sacred ceremonies before the events of [[The Baptism of '39-Keeper]]. Now only **Wąąk Toošewe** are allowed to enter. The caves are said to contain **ancient carvings** that map the ley lines and predict the coming of the Hungry Ones if the ley lines are ever fully corrupted.
## **Legacy**:  
The Ho-Chunk’s presence in Watashuka has been largely overshadowed by the town’s more visible history, but their role as guardians of the ley lines remains vital. In a town filled with hidden dangers—government conspiracies, warring cults, and supernatural entities—the Ho-Chunk continue to protect the balance, often without recognition or thanks. Their vigilance is all that stands between the land and the ancient forces that seek to consume it.
## Activities
### **Preserving Sacred Sites:**
The Ho-Chunk are quietly protecting their sacred sites from government and cult interference. This effort puts them at odds with Project Caroline, which is conducting experiments on or near these locations.
### **Sharing Knowledge with the Amish:**
Some members of the Ho-Chunk are working with the Amish to exchange ancient knowledge. This uneasy alliance is based on mutual respect but could fall apart if trust is broken.
### **Break the Time Loop:**
Elders of the tribe have detected the time loop and attempt to either break the loop or at least pass knowledge from loop to the next. 
### **Combating Created Monsters:**
The Ho-Chunk attempt to destroy the monstrosities that the cult create.
### **Sabotaging Cult Rituals:**
The Ho-Chunk are actively working to disrupt the cult rituals, particularly those that desecrate the land. They may use their spiritual knowledge to neutralize dark powers, unknowingly aligning with the Amish in these efforts.
### **Advising Caroline College Faculty:**
Certain Ho-Chunk leaders are offering subtle guidance to faculty at Caroline College, steering them away from research paths that might inadvertently lead to supernatural dangers. This puts them in quiet conflict with Project Caroline operatives.
### **Fostering Cultural Awareness:**
The Ho-Chunk people are working to promote cultural awareness through the Ho-Chunk Cultural Heritage Museum, hoping to protect their traditions from external influences. This brings them into indirect conflict with Project Caroline’s attempts to exploit their knowledge. It is through this awareness that the tribe hopes to pass knowledge from one time loop to the next. They make use of the various museums and heritage centers in the region for this.
### **Monitoring Project Caroline:**
The Ho-Chunk are aware of the government attempts to make use of eldritch magic. They are actively attempting to stop this exploitation as they believe that the government does not understand the dangers they are putting every at risk of.
### **Neutralizing Government Technology:**
The Ho-Chunk are using their spiritual practices to subtly interfere with government surveillance and experiments, particularly in areas they deem sacred.
### **Guarding Against Yog-Sothoth Followers:**
The Ho-Chunk are closely watching the cult of Yog-Sothoth, believing that their summoning rituals could unleash devastating forces. They are actively working to stop these rituals but may come into conflict with the Amish over methods and intentions.

# **Ho-Chunk People**
**Overview:**  
The **Ho-Chunk Nation**, also known as the **People of the Sacred Voice**, are the original inhabitants of the land surrounding [[Watashuka]]. Their ancestors have lived in the region for centuries, long before European settlers arrived. The Ho-Chunk have a deep connection to the land, its natural resources, and its spiritual significance. Though their population has diminished over time, the Ho-Chunk remain an integral part of the region’s cultural and historical landscape.
**Cultural Significance:**  
The Ho-Chunk people have long believed that the land around Watashuka is sacred. Their traditions emphasize harmony with nature, and they hold regular ceremonies to honor the spirits of the earth. For generations, they have passed down their knowledge of the land’s unique spiritual energy, teaching that certain locations are sites of great power. These beliefs continue to influence the Ho-Chunk’s way of life, as they strive to preserve their cultural heritage and protect the land from further exploitation.
**Community and Economy:**  
In modern times, the Ho-Chunk maintain a presence in the region through their **cultural centers** and participation in local events. They are known for producing traditional crafts, offering educational programs on Ho-Chunk history, and organizing cultural festivals that attract visitors from surrounding areas. The Ho-Chunk people also operate businesses in and around Watashuka, including agriculture and tourism, which provide them with economic stability while preserving their connection to the land.
**Challenges:**  
The Ho-Chunk community, like many Indigenous groups, faces ongoing challenges related to land rights, cultural preservation, and the encroachment of modern society. Government projects, such as the construction of **[[Caroline College]]** and various agricultural developments, have threatened Ho-Chunk sacred sites over the years. Despite these challenges, the Ho-Chunk remain resilient, working to protect their traditions while engaging with local and state authorities to ensure that their voice is heard in decisions impacting the region.
**Cultural Preservation:**  
The **Ho-Chunk Cultural Heritage Museum** in Watashuka serves as a focal point for preserving and sharing their history. It offers exhibits on traditional Ho-Chunk life, artifacts from the past, and explanations of their spiritual beliefs, providing both locals and visitors with an opportunity to learn about their culture. Educational programs are also offered to local schools, helping to ensure that future generations understand the importance of the Ho-Chunk people’s connection to the land.

[[Lutheran Church]]
- **Role in the Occult**: Unbeknownst to the church, several members of the leadership are either cultists themselves or have been unknowingly influenced by cult activities. Cults like [[Brotherhood of the Gate Unveiled]] have long infiltrated the institution, manipulating church decisions while keeping the clergy and congregation oblivious to the deeper supernatural forces at work.
- **Exorcisms**: While the church believes it is expelling demons, many of these rituals are targeting individuals affected by real occult influences—sometimes with unintended consequences. In some cases, their exorcisms have accidentally interfered with cult rituals or triggered retaliatory actions from occult groups operating in [[Watashuka]].
- **Engaging the Amish**: Certain clergy have quietly reached out to the [[Amish-Keeper]] for guidance, sensing that the Amish know more about the spiritual disturbances in town than they let on. The Amish, in turn, see the Lutheran Church as a potential ally but remain wary, given the church’s naiveté regarding the true scale of the supernatural threats.
- **Necromantic Influence**: The church maintains the cemetery near Lake View, unaware that it is a hotspot for cultists attempting necromantic rituals. While pastors bless the grounds and offer prayers to protect it, the cemetery remains a contested site between cults and the Amish, both of whom seek to control its mystical power.
- **Dangerous Charity Intersections**: The church’s charity events, while well-intentioned, have at times crossed paths with occult activities. Amish safehouses and rituals occasionally coincide with these events, leading to tension. The church is unaware of these clashes but continues to unknowingly involve itself in supernatural matters.
- **Internal Corruption**: While some pastors genuinely work to protect the congregation, others have unknowingly facilitated cult activities by offering sanctuary to cultists posing as victims. The cultists manipulate the church’s goodwill to hide their true intentions.

# Lutheran Church
- **Role**: The Lutheran Church represents the largest religious institution in [[Watashuka]] and is seen as a stabilizing force in the community. With half of the town’s population attending services, the church plays a crucial role in maintaining the spiritual and moral framework of the town. The congregation is unaware of any real supernatural forces at work and believes their primary concern is protecting the town from ‘devil worshipers’ and cultural shifts infiltrating the college and community.
- **History**: The Lutheran Church’s influence in Watashuka dates back to the **[[Great Influx]]** following the [[Blizzard of 1888]], when large numbers of Lutheran settlers arrived in the region to offer humanitarian aid. Many of these settlers were recent immigrants from Germany, and after helping the region recover from the devastating storm, they decided to make Watashuka their home. Their arrival significantly shaped the town’s religious and cultural identity, as they established churches, schools, and community centers that reflected their Lutheran values. Over time, the church grew to become the dominant religious institution in the area, cementing its place as a cornerstone of Watashuka's life.
- **Community Involvement**: The church is actively involved in organizing charity events, supporting local families, and fostering engagement with youth. They are also quietly helping protect the community, providing sanctuary to troubled individuals and maintaining the town’s cemetery with a sense of reverence. Their work has helped maintain a strong moral foundation in Watashuka, particularly as the town faces economic decline.
- **Protecting Congregants**: The church leadership has noticed strange behavior among some congregants and is taking steps to protect the flock from potential outside influences, including what they perceive as destructive and unholy. Pastors occasionally perform exorcisms, trying to rid people of what they believe are signs of demonic possession. In each case, those subject to possession all share two common traits; heavy metal music and role-playing games.
- **Supporting the Watashuka Initiative**: Some church leaders previously supported the [[Watashuka Initiative]], a government project designed to bring economic and technological development to the region, officially ending in 1969. They believed it was beneficial to the community and even offered prayers for its success. However, with the initiative's end, the church has continued to focus on local outreach, charity efforts, and new government initiatives being considered.
- **Engaging with the Ho-Chunk**: In recent years, some members of the Lutheran Church have cautiously engaged with the local [[Ho-Chunk]] people, seeking to understand their traditions. These interactions are seen as efforts to foster cross-cultural respect, though some view these efforts with suspicion.

[[Metalheads]]
# **The Metalheads (Local Counterculture and Occult Fighters)**
## **Overview**: 
In the early 1980s, Watashuka’s _Metalhead_ community is a tight-knit group of teenagers and young adults who rally around heavy metal music, tabletop role-playing games, and the rebellion of youth counterculture. What makes them unique in Watashuka is their hidden role as one of the few groups actively fighting against the occult forces that threaten the town. Unlike the stereotypes of the time, which painted them as devil-worshipping delinquents, these outcasts use their knowledge of obscure lore, occult symbols, and music to resist eldritch forces, often working in the shadows to prevent horrors that most townspeople never see.
## **Role in Town**: 
Viewed with suspicion and disdain by the more conservative residents of Watashuka, the _Metalheads_ are frequently blamed for vandalism, strange disappearances, and even weather anomalies. Their loud music, punk rock attire, and unconventional interests make them easy targets for the [[Mothers Opposing Metal]] group, the town’s moral watchdogs. However, behind their rebellious exterior, they are actually one of the few factions in Watashuka actively working to combat the cults and dark powers manipulating the town.
## **Base of Operations**: 
Many of the _Metalheads_ hang out at _Jack’s Surfer: Comics & Games_ or at the _Blue Heron Pub_. This group is heavily influenced by metal music’s cryptic lyrics and the imagery of fantasy role-playing games like _Dungeons & Dragons_, which have inadvertently led them to discover real occult knowledge hidden within the town's dark history.
## **Notable Figures**:
- **“Raven” Becky Thompson**: One of the few female Metalheads in town, Becky is fiercely independent and well-versed in occult symbols and esoteric rituals. She spends her days researching local folklore at _The Prince: New & Used Books_ and her nights planning counter-attacks against the cultists, using her knowledge of heavy metal and mythology.
- **Eddie “Styx” Delano**: Eddie is the town’s go-to guy for rituals that require certain "artifacts" like skulls, daggers, and ritual books. He’s resourceful, knowing how to procure these items without raising suspicion. Despite his rough appearance, Eddie is serious about fighting the occult forces, and he has a strong moral code, believing they must protect the innocent from the eldritch horrors lurking in the town.
## **Activities**:
- **Occult Research**: The Metalheads spend much of their time researching occult symbols and rituals that can be found in their music and games, giving them an edge when it comes to identifying cult activity.
- **Disrupting Rituals**: They've made it their mission to disrupt local cults by graffitiing occult symbols that interfere with rituals, performing counter-rituals themselves, and even engaging in direct action when necessary.
- **Underground Communication**: Using [[Dave|Dave's]] radio show, the Metalheads pass coded messages to each other about cult movements and activities.
- **Public Perception**: Feared and misunderstood by the general populace, the _Metalheads_ are often accused of satanic rituals themselves, especially by the _Mothers Opposing Metal_ (MOM) group. Their music and games are seen as gateways to evil, even though the reality is that they are often the ones standing between the town and much darker forces.

# **MOM Newsletter: Special Edition – URGENT ALERT**
---
**MOTHERS OPPOSING METAL**  
_Defending Watashuka’s Morals and Protecting Our Children_  
**September 1983 Special Edition: The Metalhead Threat Escalates!**
---
**Dear Concerned Parents and Members of the [[Watashuka]] Community,**
We write to you today with the utmost urgency regarding a disturbing and dangerous trend that has emerged in our beloved town. As you know, our mission in **[[Mothers Opposing Metal|Mothers Opposing Metal (MOM)]]** has always been to protect the innocence of our children and safeguard our community from the ever-present threat of Satanic influence. It is with great sadness and alarm that we must report on a new development in the alarming behaviors of the so-called "Metalheads" in our midst.
We have long been aware of the corrupting influence of **heavy metal music** and **role-playing games**, but recent events have revealed that these youths—already steeped in the glorification of violence, Satanism, and rebellion—are now engaging in criminal activity. Their actions are more than just a public nuisance; they represent a grave danger to our children, our families, and our way of life.
---
### **Metalheads Target Local Children: Reports of Kidnapping in Mackie Recreational Park!**
It has come to our attention that children in **Mackie Recreational Park** have been approached and, in some cases, lured away by members of the **Metalhead subculture**. These individuals, easily identifiable by their long hair, black leather jackets, and offensive band logos, have been seen loitering near the playgrounds and picnic areas, targeting our most vulnerable. **Multiple concerned parents** have reported strange behavior from these Metalheads, who reportedly entice children with promises of "fun" and "games," only to disappear with them into the wooded areas surrounding the park. Parents tell us that their children were abused, forced to bless Satan, and then hypnotized to forget the event.
Although no children have *officially* been reported missing yet, we believe this is only the beginning. The **Watashuka Police Department** has been notified, and we urge all parents to keep a close watch on their children, especially as Halloween approaches—a time when these devil-worshiping youths are known to celebrate their twisted rituals. **We believe the Metalheads are using role-playing games as a way to indoctrinate children into their dark world,** encouraging them to escape reality and immerse themselves in dangerous fantasies of occult power and rebellion.
---
### **Satanic Rituals and Stolen Farm Animals: A New Horror on the Outskirts**
Disturbingly, we have also received **multiple reports from local farmers** who have found their livestock missing or mutilated in recent weeks. It is no coincidence that these incidents coincide with an increase in Metalhead activity in the area. Eyewitness accounts describe groups of these Metalheads gathering near remote barns and abandoned buildings late at night, playing their demonic music at high volumes and conducting what can only be described as **ritualistic ceremonies**.
Our sources indicate that the **Metalheads are using these stolen animals in Satanic rituals,** mimicking the horrific sacrifices described in their heavy metal lyrics and the darkest of their role-playing games. These games, which often feature blood magic, demon-summoning, and the sacrifice of innocent creatures, have desensitized these youths to real-life violence and depravity. **What starts as a game can easily become reality**, and the lines between fantasy and real-life horror are quickly disappearing for those trapped in this lifestyle.
---
### **How You Can Protect Your Children and Our Community:**
We urge all parents and concerned citizens to take the following steps to protect our town from the influence of the Metalheads:
1. **Stay Vigilant in Public Spaces:** Do not allow your children to wander alone in parks or public areas, especially after dark. The Metalheads are known to operate under the cover of night.
2. **Monitor Your Children’s Activities:** Keep a close eye on the music your children are listening to and the games they are playing. If you see any signs of involvement with heavy metal music or role-playing games, intervene immediately.
3. **Report Suspicious Activity:** If you see Metalheads congregating near schools, parks, or your neighborhood, do not hesitate to contact the police. Together, we can put an end to their criminal activity.
4. **Spread the Word:** Share this newsletter with your friends and neighbors. The more people are aware of the Metalhead threat, the better we can defend our community.
5. **Attend Our Next Meeting:** Join us at **All Saints Lutheran Church** this Friday evening for a special prayer service and strategy session on how we can continue to fight back against these dark influences. We must show these Metalheads that our community will not stand for their wicked behavior!
---
### **Closing Thoughts:**
Remember, fellow mothers and fathers, we stand on the front lines in the battle for our children’s souls. The threat posed by these Metalheads is real and growing. Their music, their games, and their lifestyle glorify Satanic rituals and violent rebellion. **We cannot let this evil take root in Watashuka.**
Let us continue to pray for our town, for our children, and for the courage to stand strong in the face of darkness. Together, we will protect Watashuka from the corruption that seeks to destroy it.
**With steadfast resolve,**  
**Nancy Mueller**  
President, Mothers Opposing Metal
---
**Remember:** **Our children are watching. Our future depends on us.**

[[Mothers Opposing Metal]]
- **Overview**:  
    MOM is a well-meaning but misguided group whose focus on fighting metal music, role-playing games, and youth rebellion has blinded them to the real occult forces at work in [[Watashuka]]. Their obsession with the so-called "satanic panic" distracts them from the true dangers posed by the cults secretly operating within the town. While MOM believes they are protecting the youth, their efforts unintentionally shield the activities of groups like the **[[Church of the Delayed Blossom]]** and the **[[Brotherhood of the Gate Unveiled]]**, who continue their dark rituals without interference.
- **Unintentional Harm**:  
    MOM’s fixation on superficial symbols of rebellion—like metal music and games—has created a climate of paranoia in Watashuka, leading to increased tensions between the town’s youth and its more conservative residents. By focusing on scapegoats like the Metalheads, MOM misses the true threats posed by the town’s occult factions. This allows the cults to operate more freely, as the town’s resources are directed towards suppressing harmless expressions of youth culture rather than investigating the real supernatural dangers.
- **Blind to the Occult**:  
    Despite their belief that they are combating satanic forces, MOM is completely unaware of the true occult activity happening under their noses. The real cults in town manipulate the situation to their advantage, allowing MOM to distract the public from their own activities. While MOM views the Metalheads as a dangerous subculture, it is the cults entrenched in the town’s institutions that pose the true threat to Watashuka.
- **Key Figures (Keeper Secrets)**:
    - **Nancy Mueller**: Though Nancy believes wholeheartedly in her cause, she is completely blind to the true supernatural dangers that surround her. Her influence over local politics and the church has allowed her to successfully push forward many of MOM’s agendas, but her efforts inadvertently create cover for the cults operating within the town.
    - **Sandra Pike**: Sandra is passionate about fighting against what she sees as moral decay, but her zeal often causes her to overlook the real danger. She is quick to lead rallies and protests, which further divide the community, allowing the cults to continue operating in the shadows.
    - **Karen Albright**: Karen’s personal vendetta against the Metalheads, fueled by her estranged relationship with her son, makes her one of MOM’s most active members. She often oversteps, spying on teenagers and pressuring local authorities to act on any suspicion, further increasing tensions between the youth and the town’s leadership.
- **Impact on the Town**:  
    While MOM’s actions may seem harmless on the surface, they create a tense atmosphere in Watashuka, especially for the town’s youth. This tension allows the real supernatural dangers to thrive, as the cults and dark forces at work in the town are able to operate unchecked while the public is distracted by MOM’s moral crusade.
- **Potential Hooks for Investigators**:
    - **Misguided Crusade**: Investigators may find themselves at odds with MOM, especially if they are seen as part of the youth counterculture or are involved in activities that MOM deems suspicious. They may need to navigate the group’s influence or convince them of the real dangers at play.
    - **Unwitting Allies**: Investigators could use MOM’s influence in the town to their advantage by redirecting their focus towards the real occult threats. However, MOM’s members are deeply entrenched in their beliefs, making this a difficult task.
    - **Source of Tension**: MOM’s actions create tension within the town, which investigators may need to exploit or navigate to further their own investigations. MOM’s public influence makes them a powerful force, but their focus on the wrong issues makes them both a hindrance and a potential asset if manipulated correctly.
# **MOM: Mothers Opposing Metal (Moral Watchdogs and Anti-Occult Activists)**
## **Overview**: 
_Mothers Opposing Metal_ (MOM) is a group of highly conservative mothers, fathers and community members in Watashuka who believe that heavy metal music, role-playing games, and anything associated with counterculture is a gateway to devil worship and societal decay. Founded in response to the rising popularity of metal music and games like _Dungeons & Dragons_, MOM is determined to root out what they see as the growing influence of the occult, often targeting the [[Metalheads]] and their associated subculture as the prime instigators of evil in the town.
## **Role in Town**: 
MOM holds considerable sway over local politics, religious organizations, and the school system. They have pressured the Lutheran Church, the school board, and local law enforcement to crack down on anything they perceive as occult-related, from album covers to role-playing game paraphernalia. However, unbeknownst to them, their crusade against the _Metalheads_ distracts the town from the real supernatural threats: the secretive cults embedded in Watashuka’s institutions.
## **Base of Operations**: 
The group typically meets at _All Saints Lutheran Church_ or in the living rooms of its more prominent members. These meetings are filled with prayer, discussion of moral purity, and planning sessions to counteract what they see as the satanic influences in town. MOM often organizes public events, like anti-metal rallies, book burnings, and community outreach to "save" the youth.
## **Notable Figures**:
- **Nancy Mueller** (Leader): Nancy is the founder and driving force behind MOM. The wife of Pastor Daniel Mueller of All Saints Lutheran Church, she sees herself as the moral compass of the town. Nancy is deeply religious and believes that Watashuka’s problems stem from allowing corrupting influences like metal music and role-playing games into the community. Though she has good intentions, Nancy is blind to the real evil lurking beneath the surface.
- **Sandra Pike**: Sandra is Nancy’s right-hand woman and an expert at mobilizing local parents to join their cause. A fiery speaker, she often leads public demonstrations against the _Metalheads_ and has a reputation for stirring up fear among the townspeople.
- **Karen Albright**: A zealous member of MOM, Karen is obsessed with monitoring the actions of the _Metalheads_. Her son, who is secretly part of the Metalhead group, has been estranged from her, which fuels her crusade to save other children from the "satanic influences."
## **Activities**:   
- **Public Demonstrations**: MOM holds rallies and prayer vigils in protest of concerts, game nights at _Jack’s Surfer_, and other events associated with the Metalhead community. These events are often loud and gain significant attention from the local media.
- **Moral Crusades**: MOM has successfully pressured local authorities to raid _Jack’s Surfer_ and confiscate game books, music records, and other materials they deem "satanic." They’ve also convinced the school board to ban certain music and literature from the high school, labeling it as dangerous to the youth.
- **Surveillance of Youth**: Members of MOM are notorious for keeping a close eye on their children's activities. They often spy on local teenagers, monitoring their music and friendships, and report any "suspicious" behavior to local authorities.
- **Public Perception**: While they are respected by many of the older and more religious townspeople, MOM is also seen as overbearing and alarmist by younger generations. The _Metalheads_ and other teens view them as clueless moralists who don’t understand the real dangers lurking in Watashuka. Their activities often lead to unnecessary distractions, allowing the true occult forces to operate unchecked.
## **Unintentional Harm**: 
By focusing on the _Metalheads_ and other harmless expressions of youth rebellion, MOM misses the real threat posed by the cults in town. Their obsession with the _Satanic Panic_ creates an atmosphere of paranoia that allows the true cults—like [[Church of the Delayed Blossom]] and [[Brotherhood of the Gate Unveiled]]—to continue their dark rituals without interference.
