# **Mothers Opposing Metal (MOM)**
- **Overview**:  
    _Mothers Opposing Metal_ (MOM) is a highly vocal, conservative group based in [[Watashuka]], comprised of concerned mothers, fathers, and other community members who believe that heavy metal music, role-playing games, and youth counterculture are gateways to devil worship and societal decay. Founded in response to the growing popularity of metal music and games like _Dungeons & Dragons_, MOM seeks to protect the town’s youth from what they perceive as occult influences, primarily targeting the local **Metalheads** and their culture.
- **Role in Town**:  
    MOM has a strong influence over local politics, religious organizations, and the school system. Their efforts are centered on pressuring the **Lutheran Church**, the school board, and law enforcement to crack down on what they see as "satanic" influences in the town. Their public demonstrations, prayer vigils, and moral crusades often succeed in getting certain music, books, and games banned from schools and public spaces.
- **Base of Operations**:  
    MOM holds regular meetings at **All Saints Lutheran Church**, where its members gather for prayer, discussion of moral values, and the planning of public demonstrations. They also meet in the living rooms of prominent members for smaller organizing sessions. These gatherings are focused on protecting the youth and ridding the town of what they see as satanic influences.
- **Notable Figures**:
    - **Nancy Mueller** (Leader): Nancy is the founder of MOM and the wife of **Pastor Daniel Mueller**. She believes that Watashuka’s moral decay is a result of allowing corrupt influences like metal music and role-playing games to take root in the community. Nancy is deeply religious and sees herself as the moral protector of the town.
    - **Sandra Pike**: Sandra is Nancy’s second-in-command, known for her fiery speeches and ability to mobilize the group’s members. She often leads public rallies and demonstrations against the [[Metalheads|metalhead]] culture.
    - **Karen Albright**: A zealous member of MOM, Karen is obsessed with monitoring the actions of the local [[Metalheads]], particularly because her own son has secretly joined the group. Her personal vendetta fuels much of her crusade.
    - **[[Michelina Plum]]**: Local radio personality at [[WCTU]]. Michelina is obsessed with the corrupting impact of heavy metal music and has  special hatred for the pirate radio host known only as [[Dave|"Dave"]].
- **Public Activities**:
    - **Public Demonstrations**: MOM frequently organizes protests and prayer vigils at events they see as promoting occult influences, including concerts, game nights at **Jack’s Surfer**, and gatherings of local Metalheads. These events draw attention from the local media and further the group’s agenda of moral purity.
    - **Moral Crusades**: The group has successfully lobbied local authorities to raid **Jack’s Surfer**, confiscating records, game books, and other materials they deem to be satanic. They have also convinced the school board to ban certain music and literature from **North High School**, believing these materials to be dangerous for the youth.
    - **Surveillance of Youth**: MOM members keep a close eye on the town’s teenagers, monitoring their activities and friendships. They report any "suspicious" behavior—such as listening to metal music or playing role-playing games—to local authorities, often resulting in unwarranted crackdowns on harmless teenage rebellion.
- **Public Perception**:  
    MOM is respected by many of the older, more religious townspeople, who see the group as a moral force protecting the town from corruption. However, younger generations—particularly the Metalheads—view them as overbearing and out of touch with reality. While they succeed in banning certain materials, many see their activities as distractions from more serious issues.

title: Project Caroline
draft: true
publish: false
tags:

# Project Caroline
A covert operation using Caroline College as a front to investigate supernatural phenomena. Agents are embedded throughout the town.
[[Watashuka Initiative]] was a cover for the Project Caroline project. Through leaks, the community began to assume the two were the same. No effort were made to correct this so that future obfuscation would be easier. 
## Office of Scientific Research and Development (OSRD)
The original founding group of Project Caroline. It was founded as a result of investigating [[The Baptism of '39]] **Agent Howard Fitzsimmons** was the first investigator, and later founder, of the project
 ## Office of Technology Assessment (OTA)
- The Office of Technology Assessment took over Project Caroline from the OSRD upon its restart in the mid 70's. The OTA continues to operate covertly, with **Dr. Amy Mann** being one of their key assets. The project involves time manipulation, which has inadvertently created a **time loop** from 1983 to 1987.
## The Time Loop and Project Caroline
### **Time Loop (1983-1987)**
- **Overview:** Due to the experiments conducted by **Dr. Amy Mann** under **Project Caroline**, the universe has become trapped in a time loop spanning from 1983 to 1987. The only way to escape the loop is to rescue Amy Mann, who disappears at the beginning of each loop.
### **Project Caroline**
- **Overview:** A secret government initiative that started during WWII and continues in secret today, overseen by the **OTA**. The project is focused on studying and controlling supernatural phenomena, particularly time manipulation, with the aim of replicating the abilities of eldritch gods. Many at Caroline College are unaware that the project is still active.
# Possible Faction Schemes
### **U.S. Government (Project Caroline)**
1. **Time Loop Experiments:**
    - Project Caroline is continuing time manipulation experiments, hoping to find a way to control the time by exploiting eldritch energy. Their actions attract the attention of the Amish and cultists, who either try to stop or exploit these experiments.
2. **Surveillance of the Amish:**
    - Government agents have begun covertly surveilling the Amish community, suspecting them of harboring knowledge of the supernatural forces at play. This scheme risks tipping off the Amish to the government’s deeper involvement.
3. **Infiltrating Caroline College:**
    - Project Caroline has placed covert operatives among the faculty and students of Caroline College to monitor and influence ongoing supernatural events. These agents are particularly interested in the activities of the cults, activities at campus location that defy traditional surveillance technology, and any Amish involvement on campus.
4. **Weaponizing Supernatural Forces:**
    - The government is experimenting with using eldritch entities and powers as weapons. These efforts occasionally intersect with the cults, who seek to manipulate these same forces for their own ends.
5. **Studying the Buildings:**
    - Project Caroline is researching select buildings their potential ties to ancient powers. This research draws the attention of both cults, who have constructed or obtain the structures over the decades.
6. **Suppressing Cult Activity:**
    - The government is secretly tracking and eliminating high-ranking members of both the [[Yog-Sothoth]] and [[Shub-Niggurath]] cults. However, the cults are becoming aware of this effort and are striking back through more covert means.
7. **Containment of Eldritch Entities:**
    - Project Caroline is working on containment procedures for the eldritch beings they have encountered. Their containment methods often conflict with the Ho-Chunk and Amish’s own rituals to banish or neutralize these entities.
8. **Manipulating Ho-Chunk Knowledge:**
    - The government is attempting to exploit the ancient knowledge held by the [[Ho-Chunk]] people. They offer technological or financial incentives to extract information but face resistance from the community.
9. **Monitoring Time Anomalies:**
    - Project Caroline is keeping close tabs on the time anomalies in Watashuka, particularly around Caroline College. Their efforts to fix or control the time loop bring them into conflict with both the cults and the Amish.
10. **Colluding with Cults:**
- Certain elements within Project Caroline have begun secretly working with the cult of [[Yog-Sothoth]], believing that aligning with the cult could provide them the edge they need in understanding and controlling eldritch powers.
---
# Campaign Setting Secrets
# True Timeline of the Region - The Story Bible
## **Pre-1850s**
- **Ancient History**: The region that would become Watashuka is situated at the convergence of several ley lines, making it a place of supernatural significance. The Ho-Chunk people, who have inhabited the area for centuries, are aware of the ley lines’ power and use their knowledge to protect the land from dark forces. The ley lines are believed to be spiritual conduits, connecting this world to ancient, unknowable cosmic forces.
## **May 1856** – **Prairieville Academy** Founded by Occultists
- **Prairieville Academy** is established by a group of occultists led by **Walter Mann**, **Eleazar Root** and **John W. Sterling**. They recruited three locals, with a less than pristine past, to clear the lands of the local tribes and abduct the first 'students'. The academy’s true purpose is to gather young students, particularly Native American youths, to perform dark rituals on in order to summon what Mann described as the 'original god'. Unknown to him, the god he dreamt of is the eldritch god, [[Cthulhu]].
- The idea for the school came to Mann in a dream. Root and Sterling were his first, and most loyal, recruits.
- The Academy is built at a key ley line nexus, chosen specifically for its supernatural energy.
- Their rituals target young Native American students, attempting to use their connection to the land and its power to fuel a major summoning.
- Unknown to each other, each founder is being influenced by a different eldritch entity but they think they are on the path to summoning the same "original god." They don’t realize they are being manipulated by [[Nyarlathotep]].
- Founding Members
		- Walter Mann: German immigrant, artist, head founder of the academy
		- Eleazar Root: Co-founder. Massachusetts school teacher, relocated
		- John W. Sterling: Co-founder, English businessman, relocated 
		- Elias Haskins: Co-founder, local prominent cavalrymen
		- Jonathan Whitmore: Co-founder, local esteemed teacher and theologian
		- Sarah Johnson: Co-founder, local wealthy widow and philanthropist
## **August 1860** – Destruction of **Prairieville Academy** (Ritual Interrupted)
- The **Ho-Chunk** people, aware of the academy’s dark purpose, attack to stop a major ritual. This ritual involved the transformation of several Ho-Chunk youths for a summoning of the 'original god'.
- The Ho-Chunk succeed in halting the ritual and destroyed the academy in the process. Many die, including Mann and most of the original cult members. However, both **Eleazar Root** and **John W. Sterling** survive.
- The destruction of the Academy opens the way for the arrival of the [[Amish]], who recognize the ley lines and the region's supernatural danger. They quietly establish themselves to act as protectors of the land.
## **September 1862** – **Prairieville School** opened
- Eleazar Root and John W. Sterling, the surviving occultists, believe that the failed ritual must have been due to sabotage due to a deviation from the 'true path'. 
	- Root, following [[Shub-Niggurath]] forms [[Church of the Delayed Blossom]]. This cult focuses on manipulating nature and fertility.
	- Sterling, following [[Yog-Sothoth]], forms [[Brotherhood of the Gate Unveiled]]. This cult focuses on time manipulation and dimensional gates. 
- Both believe they are following the true way to summon the "original god" and view each other as being misled.
- The two cults have an uneasy relationship. Sometime waring against one another and sometimes cooperating; hoping to bring the other back to the 'true path'.
- Both cults compete to control key ley line nodes, conducting rituals at specific locations across the town, especially within Caroline College and its precursor institutions.
- Both cults reestablish themselves in secret under the guise of the rebuilt **Prairieville School**. They slowly gather power and influence over the next several decades, controlling different aspects of the school and infiltrating local society.
## January 1888 - **The Blizzard of 1888**
* The [[Blizzard of 1888]] sparked a turning point for the region. The failed ritual paved the way for a new faction, the [[Lutheran Church]] to enter the area.
## **April 1895 – Creation of **Caroline Religious Teaching College**
- The cults gain power through unsuspecting Lutheran immigrants, who push for the school’s expansion into **Caroline Religious Teaching College**. The immigrants believe they are establishing a religious institution, unaware that the cults are using their influence to mask their occult activities. Many devout Lutherans are tricked into taking part of the cults rituals. The Lutherans believe they have received divine messages from their God when in reality it is cult magic and deception. 
- The town is renamed **Watashuka**, a mistranslation of the Ho-Chunk word **Waceǧi**, meaning "dangerous," reflecting the native people's warning about the area.
## **1930s-1940s** – Cult Influence Spreads and **Project Caroline** Begins
- As WWII approaches, the cults’ activities intensify. The **U.S. government**, becoming aware of strange phenomena tied to the college and town, starts a secret research initiative called Project Caroline.
	- Publicly, this was known as [[Watashuka Initiative|the Watashuka Initiative]]
- Project Caroline is aimed at studying the supernatural phenomena in the region, initially under the guise of wartime research. However, its true focus is on harnessing eldritch power for potential military or espionage purposes.
- The Ostensibly wartime research, its true focus is on studying and controlling the supernatural power of the ley lines for military purposes and later towards winning the space race.
    - **Cult Manipulation**: During this time, the cults increase their influence over the college, using the chaos of the war to mask their own experiments and rituals. The Lutherans are nearly compromised by cult members who infiltrate their ranks, but the end of the war and the expansion of Project Caroline provide a temporary reprieve.
    - **Ritual Failure**: Another major cult ritual fails during this period, [[The Baptism of '39]], leading to another name change for the college. The post-war push for scientific expansion transforms the college into a modern liberal arts institution, **Caroline College**, though the cults remain entrenched. Its failure is what led to the government's involvement in the region.
## **1969 – Project Caroline "Ends," but Cults Step Up Activity**
- **Event**: Under the Nixon administration, Project Caroline is publicly terminated due to concerns over government overreach and having 'won' the space race. However, it is implied that Nixon himself was influenced by the cult of [[Yog-Sothoth]], seeking to end the government's interference and allow the cults to continue their work without oversight.
    - **Cults Take Advantage**: During this period, the cults believe they are finally free from government interference and ramp up their activities. 
    - **Secret Continuation**: After Nixon's removal from office, elements within the government begin quietly restarting Project Caroline, aiming to regain control of the supernatural forces around Watashuka without public scrutiny.
## **1970's - Secret Investigations
- **Secret Continuation**: After Nixon's removal from office, elements within the government begin quietly restarting Project Caroline, aiming to regain control of the supernatural forces around Watashuka without public scrutiny.
- 1975: OTA begins investigation into the records around Caroline College.
- 1976: Special Agent Dayton Hopper goes missing during a cattle mutilation investigation.
- 1978: In December, Special Agent Dayton 'appears' at the bottom of Lake Mann. He is rescued by campus security. For him only a night had passed since his disappearance. He is mutated into a 'part man, part tree' creature. His report was incomplete due to his death as a result of the mutation. It highlighted some cult plans around campus.
- 1979: New funding allocated to Project Caroline
## 1980's - Project Caroline Rebooted
- 1980: Project Caroline, in secret, is restarted under OTA direction this time.
	- With renewed Cold War funding, Project Caroline returns, this time with a stronger focus on using the ley lines to manipulate time and space for military advantage. However, this leads to increasingly dangerous interactions with the cults, who now see the government as a direct competitor for supernatural power.
- 1981: [[Amy Mann]] is recruited to the project out of graduate school. She is a genius was on path to finish her first pH.d at 21. Her field of study is the physics of time. Government influence shaved a year off of her program.
- **1981:**
    - Spring: Shub-Niggurath cult begins experimenting on pregnant women at the teaching hospital.
    - Fall: Dave starts broadcasting "Metal At Midnight" on a pirate radio station.
- **1982:**
    - Spring: Yog-Sothoth cult gains influence within Caroline College, increasing tensions with the Shub-Niggurath cult.
    - Fall: Campus radio broadcasts of "Metal At Midnight" become more frequent but chaotic.
- **1982:** Dr. Amy Mann relocates to Caroline college.
	- Dr. Amy Mann, a brilliant physicist recruited by the OTA, arrives at Caroline College to conduct experiments related to time manipulation. Unbeknownst to her, her work interacts with the ley lines and an ongoing [[Yog-Sothoth]] ritual, resulting in the creation of a **time loop** from 1983 to 1987.
- **1983**: OTA agents, including Dr. Mann hatch a plan to pose as students to gain access to sites of special interest without cult knowledge.
- **1983:** August 22<sup>nd</sup>, Fall semester begins at Caroline College
- **1983**: August 29<sup>nd</sup>, Dr. Amy Mann goes missing (presumed murdered) after witnessing a ritual by [[Church of the Delayed Blossom]]. Local start a manhunt for the student 'Amy Mann'. In reality, Dr. Mann is pulled into an accidental time loop created by unforeseen interactions with the ritual that night and an experiment she was running in 1987.
	- **Time Loop Details**: The loop resets every few years, trapping the region in a repeating cycle. The highest-ranking cultists, aware of the loop, use it to continually attempt their summoning rituals, refining their efforts with each iteration. However, they cannot fully break free from the loop without completing their final ritual.
	- Ho-Chunk Involvement: [[Ho-Chunk]] leaders can sense the loop and attempt to pass information from one loop to the next via dream visions, information left at ley lines and group memories.
	- **Amy Mann’s Role**: Amy becomes the anchor for the time loop, disappearing at the start of each cycle after witnessing a cult ritual. If she can be saved or prevented from initiating the loop, the cycle can be broken, though this would only give the players a limited window to prevent the ultimate summoning of the "original god."
## **1983-1987** – Life in the loop
- **Project Caroline** continues secretly, with government agents posing as students, faculty, and local authorities. The cults remain entrenched within the college and the town, manipulating events to serve their eldritch masters.
- The population of Watashuka continues to experience strange occurrences: hauntings, disappearances, and unexplained phenomena. The time loop ensures that no permanent damage is done, as everything resets after a few years, but the players may be able to break the cycle and uncover the true nature of the town’s cursed existence.
- Each iteration of the loop sees a 'shuffling' of locations, events and some individuals. Key locations, events and individuals remain constant, if slightly changed.
	- Each loop ALWAYS starts with the disappearance of Amy Mann.
## **1987 – The Cults’ Ultimate Goal**
- **Event**: Both cults believe that 1987, specifically **February 23**, is the key date for completing their rituals. The alignment has not been this strong since August of 1860 (when the original school was destroyed). An alignment with the Large Magellanic Cloud provides the perfect opportunity for summoning their "original god," though they do not realize this will summon **Cthulhu**, leading to their own destruction.
    - **Endgame**: If the players fail to prevent the ritual, the time loop will break, and the full force of Cthulhu will be unleashed on the world. The cults, unaware of the true nature of their "god," will be the first to be annihilated, followed by the town and eventually, the planet.
    - **This has happened before**: In an attempt to save humanity, Dr. Mann initiated the original time loop.

# **The Watashuka Initiative**
---
**Report Summary:**
**Project Title:** Watashuka Initiative, colloquially 'Project Caroline'
**Duration:** 1940 - 21 December 1969  
**Location:** Watashuka, Midwest U.S.  
**Primary Focus:** Scientific Research into Agricultural Development and Food Preservation
---
**Background and Purpose:**  
The **Watashuka Initiative** was established in the early 1940s under the auspices of the U.S. government's Office of Scientific Research and Development (OSRD), as part of a broader effort to investigate and develop underutilized rural regions in America. Officially framed as an agricultural research and development project, the Watashuka Initiative focused on improving farming techniques, soil fertility, and maximizing land usage in the fertile Midwest. The program, initially spurred by the needs of wartime agricultural production during World War II, aimed to harness new technologies and scientific advancements to benefit local farming communities, particularly around the **Caroline Religious Teaching College**. The teaching college always had a strong agricultural program so it made a logic choice. Under government directive, the school was renamed to **[[Caroline College]]**.
Beyond agricultural research, the project also explored regional geological and meteorological phenomena, seeking to understand the unusual weather patterns and natural occurrences reported in the area. The combination of scientific curiosity, wartime necessity, and regional investment helped the Initiative gain a reputation as a forward-looking, government-backed research project.
**Major Accomplishments:**
- **Agricultural Development:** The Watashuka Initiative was responsible for significant advancements in agricultural practices in the region. It introduced new crop rotation systems, irrigation methods, and fertilizer technologies that helped increase yields for local farmers. These developments were quickly adopted by the broader Midwest agricultural community.
- **Community Engagement:** The Initiative fostered strong ties between the government and the local population. In addition to improving agricultural output, it funded the construction of local infrastructure, including roads, irrigation systems, and educational facilities associated with **Caroline College**.
- **Scientific Research:** While primarily focused on agriculture, the Watashuka Initiative also conducted research into unusual environmental phenomena reported in the area. These studies were part of an effort to explain the strange occurrences observed by local residents, though no official explanations were ever publicly released.
- **Food Preservation**: In support of the space race, the program began to research new methods of food preservation for long term space travel.
**Closure of the Watashuka Initiative:**  
In 1969, amid growing public scrutiny, and concerns over government overreach, the **Watashuka Initiative** was officially terminated under the directive of **President Richard Nixon**. The decision came as part of a broader effort to scale back federal programs and reduce government intervention in local affairs. Publicly, the closure was framed as a result of the project’s success in modernizing the region’s agriculture and a shift in national priorities following the end of the space race.
However, rumors circulated that the real reason for the closure involved internal government reports indicating the program had strayed from its original purpose. Allegedly, some researchers had begun investigating anomalous phenomena in the Watashuka area, raising concerns about the safety and ethics of continuing such research. Despite these rumors, the official explanation remained that the Initiative had completed its goals and was no longer necessary.
**Legacy:**  
Though officially ended, the legacy of the Watashuka Initiative can still be seen today in the local infrastructure and agricultural techniques implemented during the program. Watashuka remains a hub of rural farming activity, with many of the advancements introduced by the Initiative continuing to benefit the local economy. Additionally, the Initiative's closure led to a lingering sense of mystery in the region, with residents occasionally referencing the program in relation to the strange and unexplained events that continue to occur. To this day, some locals speculate that the government’s decision to close the project may have been influenced by more than just agricultural successes, though no official records support these claims.
---
**Final Status:** Terminated (1969) under presidential directive. All research and operational activities officially ceased.

Secrets of [[Blizzard of 1888]]
- In **January of 1888**, [[Church of the Delayed Blossom]] attempted a grand ritual aimed at corrupting the region's ley lines, intending to use the supernatural power of the land to summon the "original god." This ritual involved a sacrifice that would unleash a torrent of dark energy, warping nature itself to feed [[Shub-Niggurath]]. The ritual’s climax was meant to bring a period of supernatural fertility to the region, but instead, it triggered a catastrophic and unnatural event—the infamous [[Blizzard of 1888]].
- The blizzard was no ordinary snowstorm. It swept across the region, dropping temperatures at an unprecedented rate and covering the land in feet of snow within hours. Animals froze in place, and entire homesteads were buried beneath the onslaught. The sky itself seemed to warp, as if torn between dimensions, with flashes of unnatural lightning illuminating the storm. It became clear that the storm was not a mere force of nature, but a manifestation of the ley lines reacting violently to the unfinished ritual.
* **The [[Amish-Keeper]] and [[Ho-Chunk]] Intervention**:  
	* Both the **Amish** and the **Ho-Chunk** communities, with their deep understanding of the ley lines and supernatural forces, quickly realized that the blizzard was the result of the botched ritual. Though hesitant to cooperate due to cultural and religious differences, they understood that the survival of the land—and possibly the world—depended on stopping the storm.
	* **The Ho-Chunk**: Led by spiritual elders, the Ho-Chunk used their ancient rituals to calm the ley lines. They identified sacred locations near the ritual site and channeled the land’s energy to create barriers that would prevent the cult's power from further spreading. Ho-Chunk warriors, braving the supernatural storm, ventured close to the cult’s gathering, disrupting their ritual by destroying key artifacts and symbols that were amplifying the storm's intensity.
	* **The Amish**: The Amish, guided by their secret knowledge passed down through generations, performed a series of protective rituals centered on grounding the ley lines. Using ancient symbols and herbal remedies, they worked to absorb and nullify the dark energies being unleashed. Their actions were crucial in preventing the corruption from spreading to the surrounding farmland. A select group of Amish elders ventured to the heart of the storm, using their knowledge of herbal magic to counteract the ritual’s effects on nature, effectively calming the storm’s destructive force.
	* Together, the Amish and Ho-Chunk managed to weaken the blizzard and break the ley line's connection to the cult’s ritual site. By dawn, the worst of the storm had passed, though it left the region covered in snow and ice, with many homes and farms destroyed.
* **Aftermath for the Cult**:  
	* The **Church of the Delayed Blossom** suffered a major defeat. Several high-ranking members were killed in the blizzard, unable to control the forces they had unleashed. The remaining cultists were forced to flee, retreating deeper underground to rebuild their strength. Their failure weakened their influence over the land, leaving them fractured and desperate. Some members blamed the botched ritual on interference from [[Brotherhood of the Gate Unveiled]], further deepening the divide between the two groups.
	* This monumental failure of the ritual, combined with the blizzard’s devastating effects, attracted the attention of the local Lutheran population. Seeing the region as in need of moral and spiritual guidance, Lutheran leaders moved to establish themselves in the area. By **1890**, the region had been renamed **[[Watashuka]]**, and the **Caroline Religious Teaching College** was founded. The Lutherans, unaware of the deeper supernatural forces at play, believed their arrival signaled divine intervention, unaware that the true cause of the storm had been an eldritch power narrowly averted by the joint efforts of the Amish and Ho-Chunk.
* **Legacy of the Blizzard**:  
	* Locals still speak of the Blizzard of 1888 with reverence and fear. Though few know the truth, whispers of unnatural forces tied to the storm persist, passed down through generations. The event marked a turning point in the town’s hidden history, with the cults driven deeper underground, the Lutherans unknowingly filling the power vacuum, and the Amish and Ho-Chunk remaining ever-vigilant to prevent such a catastrophe from repeating.

# Blizzard of 1888
The **Blizzard of 1888** is remembered as one of the most devastating natural disasters in [[Watashuka|Watashuka's]] history. In **January 1888**, a sudden and violent snowstorm swept across the region, burying homes, freezing livestock, and leaving the town struggling for survival. The storm was so intense that temperatures dropped to dangerous levels within hours, and snowdrifts reached several feet, isolating entire communities. The storm lasted for days, leaving a landscape of snow and ice that destroyed much of the area’s infrastructure.
**Impact on the Town**: Entire families were trapped in their homes, and the storm claimed the lives of many who couldn’t escape its reach. Farmers lost livestock, crops were ruined, and the town’s growing population faced severe food shortages in the weeks that followed. For many, the blizzard was seen as a sign of the region’s unforgiving nature, with settlers wondering whether the land could truly be tamed.
**Relief Efforts and the [[Great Influx]]**: The disaster triggered a humanitarian response from [[Lutheran Church|Lutheran]] settlers, particularly from German immigrant communities who traveled to the region to provide aid. These settlers brought food, supplies, and the knowledge needed to survive such harsh conditions. Known as the **Great Influx**, this movement of Lutheran immigrants not only helped the region recover but also led many to stay and settle in Watashuka, laying the foundation for the town’s strong Lutheran presence.
By **1890**, many of these settlers had established churches and schools, and their contributions helped Watashuka rebuild after the storm. The **[[Caroline College|Caroline Religious Teaching College]]** was founded as a direct result of their efforts to educate future generations and provide spiritual guidance to the region. This period marked the beginning of a new era for the town, with the Lutheran Church playing a key role in shaping its cultural and religious identity.
**Legacy**: The Blizzard of 1888 is still spoken of with awe and respect by the people of Watashuka. It is remembered as a turning point in the town’s history, not only for the lives lost but for the resilience and community spirit it inspired. The storm solidified the town’s Lutheran roots and marked the arrival of a new chapter in its development, as settlers turned tragedy into opportunity. The blizzard is commemorated in local history as a testament to the strength and faith of those who survived.

title: The Great Influx

**January 12, 1897**  
_Watashuka, Wisconsin, United States_
**Dear Brother Heinrich,**
I trust this letter finds you in good health, and I pray the Lord’s blessings continue to rest upon your ministry in Germany. It has been nearly nine years since I arrived in this distant land, and I feel it is finally time to recount for you the story of our **Great Influx** into what we now call [[Watashuka]] - a story of both hardship and divine providence.
As you may recall, in January of **1888**, a [[Blizzard of 1888|terrible blizzard]] struck this region. The storm was like none we had ever seen, a merciless torrent of snow and ice that swallowed entire homes and froze men, women, and livestock in their place. It was a catastrophe that left the land paralyzed, and many of the early settlers here wondered if God had forsaken this place.
But it was in the midst of this devastation that the Lord called us, His faithful servants, to action. Word of the suffering reached our Lutheran congregations scattered across neighboring states, and we knew we could not stand idle. The people of Watashuka were in dire need—not only of food and shelter but of hope. I, along with many other brothers and sisters in the faith, packed our wagons with what provisions we could muster and set out for this desolate land.
What we found upon our arrival was a sight of utter ruin. Fields that had once been fertile lay buried under the snow, and the faces of those we came to help were gaunt with despair. Yet, through their trials, we saw a flicker of light—the potential for a new community to rise from these ashes. With the Lord’s guidance, we brought what aid we could, but more importantly, we brought with us the message of His love and salvation.
By the grace of God, many of us chose to stay. What began as a mission of relief soon turned into something far greater—a new beginning. We built churches, schools, and homes, binding ourselves to this land and to one another. In the years since, we have seen Watashuka grow. The **Caroline Religious Teaching College** was established just two years ago in **1895**, and it has already become a beacon of learning and faith for the region. Here, young men and women are being trained not only in the ways of the world but in the Word of God, ensuring that this land will continue to be a place of faith and righteousness.
The trials we faced during that dreadful winter were not in vain. We now see that the Lord used the blizzard not as a punishment but as a test, a crucible through which this community could be forged. Those of us who arrived in the wake of the storm have come to be known as the **Great Influx**, and though we did not seek such recognition, it is clear that God had a plan for us. We were His hands and feet in a time of great need, and now we are the foundation of a growing and devout Lutheran community. This morning alone we have lain the cornerstone for our new church. 
I write all this to you, dear Heinrich, not to boast of our works but to testify to the Lord’s faithfulness. He has turned a great disaster into an opportunity for His glory to shine, and it is with a grateful heart that I share this story with you.
May God continue to bless you in your ministry, as He has so richly blessed us here in Watashuka. I look forward to hearing news of your work in Germany, and I pray that one day you might visit this place to see with your own eyes what the Lord has accomplished through us.
In His Service,  
_Pastor Wilhelm Kraus_

# The Baptism of '39
(_The Event that Triggered Government Involvement and the Founding of Project Caroline_)
## **Event Description**:  
The supernatural disaster that locals now call **The Baptism of '39** was the result of a failed time-manipulation ritual by [[Brotherhood of the Gate Unveiled]]. What began as a sinister attempt to manipulate the ley lines and access alternate timelines spiraled out of control when misled members of the **Lutheran Church**, believing they were conducting a mass baptism, became unwitting participants in the ritual.
## **The Cover Story**:  
According to the official—and widely believed—version of events, the **Lutheran pastor**, **Reverend Frederick "Fred" Olsen**, led a congregation down to **Lake Mary** for a large-scale baptism ceremony on **October 13, 1939**. The pastor, a well-respected man in his 50s with a warm and charismatic presence, had recently gathered a group of new converts who were eager to be baptized together. The ceremony took place at dusk, with over a dozen parishioners, young and old, standing along the shore of the lake, singing hymns and preparing to enter the water.
As they began the ritual, something went terribly wrong. Inexplicable phenomena occurred—strange lights flickered above the water, and a sudden, bone-chilling fog rolled in from nowhere. The water in the lake rose, unnaturally high, forming bizarre swirling patterns. Congregants were pulled into the water by unseen forces, while others stood frozen in place, unable to move or speak. The skies above seemed to shimmer, and witnesses described seeing distorted reflections in the lake—visions of past and future events, alternate versions of themselves, and eerie figures that never existed.
The church members were trapped in what seemed like a **time anomaly**, as the rising waters of Lake Mary acted as a temporal gateway. Some were thrown forward in time, while others vanished entirely. A few survivors were found later, dazed and confused, with no memory of the event beyond stepping into the water. Local authorities chalked it up to a freak accident, but those closest to the church whispered about **demonic interference**.
## **The True Cause**:  
Unbeknownst to **Reverend Olsen** or his congregation, the baptism was actually the culmination of a ritual being conducted by [[Brotherhood of the Gate Unveiled]]. Cultists embedded within the congregation had altered the baptism’s timing and location to coincide with an arcane ritual designed to manipulate time. Their goal was to create a rift in time using the ley lines converging at **Lake Mary**, allowing them to gain knowledge from alternate dimensions and use that power to summon the "original god."
However, the interference of the Lutheran congregation—believing they were engaged in a holy ritual—disrupted the cult’s carefully laid plans. The energy they had hoped to harness from the ley lines surged out of control, and instead of manipulating time in a controlled way, they unleashed an unstable rift. The rising waters of Lake Mary became a temporal whirlpool, pulling people into alternate timelines and distorting reality.
## **Aftermath**:
- **For the Cults**:  
	- [[Brotherhood of the Gate Unveiled]] suffered a major setback. The ritual had backfired spectacularly, resulting in the deaths or disappearances of several high-ranking cult members who were caught in the time anomaly. Some cultists were flung into the future or past, while others were twisted into bizarre, unrecognizable forms by their exposure to alternate dimensions. The Brotherhood’s leadership was left fractured, and they were forced to retreat deeper into secrecy to rebuild their power and recover from the failed ritual.
	- [[Church of the Delayed Blossom]] saw this as fertile ground for their own ends. [[Shub-Niggurath]], often associated with fertility, transformation, and unchecked growth, thrived on manipulating primal human desires, including sexuality and indulgence. See below    
- **For the Lutheran Church**:  
    Reverend Fred Olsen was devastated by the event. He had no knowledge of the cult’s involvement, and in his eyes, the tragedy was a catastrophic accident—a test of faith. Reverend Olsen became more reclusive in the years following the event, haunted by the loss of his parishioners. The survivors, confused and traumatized, were never the same, and many left the church. The Baptism of '39 remains a stain on the church’s history, and the Lutheran congregation worked hard to distance themselves from the event, reinforcing the cover story that it had been a freak natural disaster.   
- **For the Town**:  
    Most locals accepted the church’s explanation of the event. While rumors of supernatural occurrences circulated, particularly among older residents, the official story held. The **Baptism of '39** became a cautionary tale about the dangers of Lake Mary, with many avoiding the lake after dark for fear of "bad luck" or worse. The lake developed a reputation for being haunted, and strange phenomena continued to be reported in the years following the event—echoes of voices from the past, distorted reflections in the water, and the occasional unexplained disappearance.   
## **Government Involvement and the Birth of Project Caroline**:  
While the locals might have accepted the cover story, the government took notice of the strange anomalies surrounding the Baptism of '39. Reports of missing persons, time distortions, and bizarre weather patterns at Lake Mary reached the desk of **Agent Howard Fitzsimmons**, a sharp and inquisitive investigator with the **Office of Scientific Research and Development (OSRD)**—a government agency tasked with exploring unusual phenomena, especially during the early years of WWII.
Fitzsimmons, in his early 40s and known for his no-nonsense approach, was sent to investigate. He quickly determined that something far more unusual than a baptism had taken place. Interviews with survivors and local authorities, as well as his own experience with classified government experiments, led Fitzsimmons to conclude that the ley lines around Lake Mary had been disturbed by some kind of occult activity. He suspected that the event was tied to **time manipulation**, though he lacked concrete evidence.
Fitzsimmons’ report to the OSRD recommended further investigation into the supernatural properties of the Watashuka region. His superiors, impressed by his findings and the potential implications for time manipulation in wartime technology, authorized the creation of [[Project Caroline]] in 1940. Fitzsimmons was appointed as the project’s first director, tasked with uncovering the secrets of the ley lines and understanding how the energies around Watashuka could be harnessed.
## **Legacy of the Baptism of '39**:  
The Baptism of '39 became the founding event for **Project Caroline**, the top-secret government initiative that would study the supernatural forces at work in Watashuka for decades to come. Fitzsimmons’ work laid the foundation for the project’s ongoing investigation into time anomalies, ley lines, and the influence of the cults operating in the shadows of the town.
Though Reverend Olsen and the Lutheran Church continued to distance themselves from the tragedy, the event marked the beginning of a new chapter in Watashuka’s secret history—one where government agents, cults, and local residents became unwitting players in a much larger cosmic game.
## The Wet Spot: The Aftermath of a Failed Ritual
(A Cult Capitalizing on Rival Failure and Hidden Desires)
The Baptism of '39 of 1939 not only left deep scars on Watashuka's lakes and time itself but also created lingering, unseen consequences in the land and people near Lake Mary. While the Brotherhood of the Gate Unveiled suffered a tremendous setback from their failed time manipulation ritual, their rivals— [[Church of the Delayed Blossom]] —saw an opportunity.
The botched ritual had temporarily destabilized the ley lines near Lake Mary, leaving the area around it highly susceptible to supernatural corruption and manipulation. The Delayed Blossom cult saw this as fertile ground for their own ends. [[Shub-Niggurath]], often associated with fertility, transformation, and unchecked growth, thrived on manipulating primal human desires, including sexuality and indulgence.
### The Founding of The Wet Spot:
In the early 1940s, shortly after the Baptism of '39, a quiet shift occurred in the area just beyond the town limits, near Lake Mary. What had once been a respectable lakeside resort fell into disrepair, as locals avoided the area due to the unnatural feelings of discomfort and fear. Without fully understanding why, residents felt uneasy near the water, especially at night. Many reported strange dreams or sudden impulses they couldn’t explain.
Sensing the opportunity, members of the Church of the Delayed Blossom began subtly influencing the land and those who still ventured near Lake Mary. Over time, their efforts coalesced into something more overt. In 1952, under the guidance of "Big" Tony D’Amato, an outsider with connections to the town’s seedier elements, The Wet Spot was established. Officially an adult establishment, The Wet Spot catered to the baser instincts of the town's population—sex, indulgence, and secrecy. Unofficially, it became a node of power for the Delayed Blossom, feeding off the suppressed desires of its patrons and slowly corrupting the land further.
### The Church of the Delayed Blossom’s Influence:
The Church of the Delayed Blossom thrives on exploiting the primal, chaotic aspects of humanity, particularly sexuality, fertility, and uncontrolled growth. The establishment of The Wet Spot near Lake Mary, on land already tainted by the failed ritual, allowed the cult to further anchor their influence in Watashuka.
- Sexuality as a Tool: For the Delayed Blossom cult, sexuality is not just a human urge—it is a form of power. By opening an establishment like The Wet Spot, the cult taps into the suppressed desires of the town, using the indulgence of lust and vice as a way to fuel their rituals. The sexual energy released at the club serves as a type of fertility magic, subtly warping the land and spreading Shub-Niggurath’s influence through the area.
- Twisting the Failure: While the Brotherhood of the Gate Unveiled failed in their time manipulation, the Delayed Blossom found a way to benefit from the weakened ley lines. The ritual’s disruption left Lake Mary’s surroundings spiritually vulnerable, making it easier for the Delayed Blossom to exert their influence over the region and its residents. The Wet Spot, positioned in an area avoided by most locals, became a hidden focal point for the cult’s activities.
### The Wet Spot’s Reputation:
To this day, The Wet Spot maintains its outward appearance as a sleazy but profitable adult establishment, frequented by college students and visitors passing through. While most of the town avoids the place, chalking it up to personal morals or discomfort, many don’t realize that the real reason they stay away stems from the lingering supernatural energy left over from the 1939 event.
- Strange Atmosphere: Those who do visit often report a strange atmosphere in the club. The air feels thick, like it’s charged with something unexplainable. Time seems to slow, and people lose track of the hours they spend inside. There are rumors that some patrons have gone missing, never seen again after a night out at the club, though this is written off as typical seedy rumors.
- Unnatural Growth: Unbeknownst to most, The Wet Spot serves as a breeding ground for darker, more unnatural forces. The cult uses the energy of indulgence and sexual desire to foster their connection to Shub-Niggurath. Some areas near the club are marked by strange growths—twisted plants, unusual fertility in the soil, and occasional sightings of hybrid creatures, believed to be the results of dark rituals.
- Dormant Power: The Delayed Blossom cult maintains a low profile, using The Wet Spot as a cover for their true activities. While not every patron is affected by the cult’s influence, those who frequent the establishment regularly often find themselves plagued by strange dreams and desires. Some even become unwitting pawns in the cult’s ongoing efforts to manipulate and corrupt the town’s ley lines.
### Legacy of the Baptism of '39:
The Baptism of '39’s aftermath left scars not only on the landscape but on the people as well. The Wet Spot, though seemingly just an adult entertainment venue, is a lingering reminder of how the disrupted ritual in 1939 forever altered the spiritual fabric of Watashuka. Where the Brotherhood of the Gate Unveiled failed in controlling time, the Church of the Delayed Blossom succeeded in harnessing the primal urges of humanity to further their influence in the town.
## **Key Figures**:
- **Reverend Frederick "Fred" Olsen**: Lutheran pastor who led the ill-fated baptism ceremony. A warm, charismatic man in his 50s, he was devastated by the events of 1939 and spent the rest of his life in quiet, guilt-ridden reflection.
- **Agent Howard Fitzsimmons**: Government investigator with the OSRD who was assigned to the case. His investigation into the Baptism of '39 led to the creation of **Project Caroline**, and he became its first director. Fitzsimmons was known for his sharp mind, skepticism, and unrelenting drive to uncover the truth.
- **"Big" Tony D’Amato**: Transplant from Indiana who established the Wet Spot under cult suggestion. Tony is not a cultist and tries to distance himself from their activities but at the end of the day, he is a businessman.

# **Tragedy at Lake Mary: Baptism Ceremony Ends in Disaster**
_October 14, 1939_  
By **[[Margaret Wilkins]]**, _The Prairie Press_
A serene autumn evening on the shores of **Lake Mary** turned tragic yesterday as a mass baptism led by **Reverend Frederick Olsen** ended in disaster. What should have been a joyous occasion for the Lutheran Church has left the Watashuka community reeling, with several parishioners still unaccounted for.
The ceremony, intended to baptize new members of the church, began around dusk. Reverend Olsen, a man beloved by many in the congregation, led a group of thirteen down to the water’s edge, accompanied by the hymns and prayers of fellow churchgoers. The atmosphere was one of peace and spiritual renewal.
That peace was shattered when a thick fog rolled in from the lake, obscuring the shore. Witnesses reported strange lights hovering above the water and a sudden, unnerving stillness. What had been a calm and sacred moment swiftly turned to chaos.
“Something wasn’t right,” said **Helen Thomas**, one of the witnesses standing on the shore. “The fog wasn’t natural. It felt... alive. And those lights, they weren’t lanterns or reflections. It was like they were floating just above the lake, and the air felt wrong.”
Several of the parishioners, including Reverend Olsen, had entered the lake when the waters began to swell unnaturally, rising higher than anyone had seen before. According to witnesses, the water seemed to pull at those in the lake, dragging them in despite their efforts to return to shore.
“I heard them calling out for help, but we couldn’t reach them,” said **Peter McKenzie**, another witness. “It was like the water was alive, pulling them in.”
As the fog thickened, those still on the shore were frozen in place, unable to move or speak. Some reported seeing strange shapes in the mist, distorted reflections that did not match the figures standing at the lake.
“I saw myself,” said **Judith Harper**, one of the survivors, trembling. “But it wasn’t me. It was like a shadow of what I could have been—older, sadder. It didn’t make any sense.”
By the time the fog cleared, several of the participants had vanished into the lake, including longtime church member **Thomas Pierce** and new convert **Ellen Linton**. Reverend Olsen himself was pulled from the water by nearby parishioners, but several others were not so fortunate. Rescue efforts continued late into the night, but as of this morning, five parishioners remain missing.
The exact cause of the incident remains unclear. Sheriff **Albert Reynolds** described it as a “freak natural occurrence,” though he admitted that the suddenness and intensity of the fog were unusual for this time of year.
“It was a terrible accident,” said Reverend Olsen in a brief statement this morning. “We were there to celebrate God’s grace, and something went terribly wrong. I ask the community to join me in prayer for the missing and their families.”
The Lutheran Church is urging the public to avoid speculation, though whispers of supernatural interference have already begun to circulate. Some locals recall past stories of strange happenings at Lake Mary, though they have long been dismissed as folklore.
As the search for the missing continues, Watashuka is left grappling with the mystery of what truly happened at the lake. What was meant to be a peaceful baptism has turned into a chilling reminder that not all is as it seems beneath the surface of our town.
Margaret Wilkins  
_The Prairie Press_

# Metal At Midnight: Black Lake
//
Oh, yeah, it's time to wake up sleepyheads. {WCTU is interrupted by static and electrical interference.}
{Dave laughing maniacally}
Ohhhh yeah! It’s time to wake up, sleepyheads! I don't care if you've got your Old Spice or not. This is your friendly neighborhood madman, DAVE, comin’ at ya live with another installment. _Metal at Midnight_ is live and have I got somethin’ that’s gonna melt your mind faster than a Sabbath riff at double speed!
{Cue heavy metal track – “Specter at Dawn” by Nightstalker, featuring eerie riffs and relentless drumming.}
So, while all the fresh meat have been worrying about their exams, and dodging campus security, I’ve been out here diggin’ deep into the stuff THEY don’t want you to know. And tonight, we’re taking a little trip off the beaten path. We're heading up country away from our cozy little Watashuka... Let’s talk about somethin’ I call… the Black Lake Incident.
{Static and ominous feedback}
What? You've never heard of it? Yeah, figures. That's because GI Joe don't want you in the know. THEY made sure to bury this shit deeper than your last biology grade. Picture this: out in the middle of nowhere, deep in the northern woods—there’s a lake. Dave! We're in Wisconsin. We know lakes Dave! But you see, this ain't just any lake. It’s dark, man. Too dark. Black Lake. Real original name, right? I know. But this place? It ain’t like your summer camp getaways. No, this ain't no Crystal Lake. This is a place even Mr. Voorhees wouldn't book a cabin at.
{Distant, echoing whispers}
Back in ‘79, a whole group of people—locals, hikers, campers, hippies, - went missing there. Like, vanished off the face of the earth. And it wasn't just the people. Their cars, their tents, their gear, ALL of it just… gone. The lake? It swallowed them whole my little stoners. And allow me to shock and surprise absolutely no one - there’s no record of an official investigation. Oh sure, they’ll tell you it’s just another ‘urban legend,’ but when was the last time an urban legend came with classified government files?!
Now here’s where it gets really freaky. Word on the wire is that Project Blacklight, some super-secret government operation, was sent in to clean it all up. But they didn’t just show up with your run-of-the-mill troops. Oh no no my friends. They sent in special forces -paranormal specialists. Yeah, that’s right. The kind of guys that make the things that go bump in the night wet their sheets.
{Ominous drumming in the background}
Locals claim they saw military trucks rollin’ in, all blacked out. No lights, no sound. And get this—ever since that night, anyone who tries to camp near Black Lake ends up with the same nightmare. They wake up, choking, gasping for air, like something’s pulling them down. Drowning them. They say you can still hear the whispers if you listen close enough. 
But hey, I’m just your friendly neighborhood conspiracy nut, right?
And here’s where it gets even weirder. Rumor has it there’s some kind of ancient artifact buried deep beneath that water. Something older than grandfather time himself. Maybe the lake was always cursed, maybe it’s something the g-men did, maybe its this or maybe its that. I don't know man. But one thing I do know is that whatever they found there in ‘79, the government has been doing everything it can to cover it up. Reports buried, witnesses silenced, the whole shebang.
{Music fades in, "Buried Secrets" by Void Cross, fast and aggressive.}
So, if you’re thinking of takin’ a little weekend trip to Black Lake, let me just say... pack light, my tattooed freaks. Real light. And maybe bring some iron, ‘cause you never know what’s lurking beneath those waters.
{Sound of flipping through papers}
///But, hey, what do I know? I’m just a guy with a mic. Stay curious, stay skeptical, and remember… they’re always watching.
Alright, my metal militia, it’s time to sign off, but not before I drive one more nail of pure auditory rebellion into your skull. Keep your head on a swivel, ‘cause the truth is out there, man, and they don’t want you to find it. But I’ll be here, keepin’ it real for all you truth-seekers. Now go on, fight back, and crank this next one loud enough for them to hear all the way out at Black Lake!"_
{Outro song begins – “Whispers of the Dead” by Shrine of Dusk, slow and haunting.}
And remember, my metalheads… they’re out there, but so are we. Dave out!
_Broadcast fades into static, cutting off WCTU's regular programming once again._

# Metal At Midnight: Sister Sarah's Stinks
{WCTU is interrupted by static and electrical interference}
{ [[Dave]] laughing demonically}
Let there be METAL!
{Heavy metal song about expecting mothers who are happy to be part of a dark, strange, future}
Dave Is Back Babies. ‘Metal at Midnight’ is live and we’ve got all the music and news you need to survive this messed up little town. And speaking of news, we’ve got some real juicy nuggets for all you little pink faced freshmen joining our church of METAL for the first time. And believe me, its news that THEY do NOT want you to know.
We’re going live tonight because I know some of you little metal headed sideshow freaks have got class in that torture chamber known as Sister Sarah’s. And believe me, they are trying super hard to keep this quiet. So Dave’s going all School House Rock tonight. Knowledge is power! And power is what they don’t want you to have.
Yeah, that hospital’s all clean and bleachy fresh outside but in the back rooms … Oh brother, it’s Mike Myers meets that freaky little alien chest baby.
Us vets know it. We've heard the screams. We've seen shadows moving all weird. We've seen dumpsters getting collected late at night. Ain't no trashman working after midnight! Yeah, Sarah’s stinks alright so watch your back there.
Worst yet, THEY know it’s there! And Dave’s got the cancelled checks to prove it; right where you’d expect. In that nasty, creepy museum all the norms pass every day on their way to class. Prairie Hall is just a 24/7, 365, all you can eat charnel house with a receptionist. But they do keep records there….
Hell, someone call Mr. King; I've got a pitch for his next book!

we’ll never surrender

# Metal At Midnight: Stratton Mill Fire
_WCTU signal cuts out with a burst of static and distant, distorted laughter._
Oh-ho-ho-ho, yeah! You know what time it is, you beautiful misfits! This is _Metal at Midnight_, and I’ve got some juice tonight that’s gonna twist your minds into knots. You think you know what’s goin’ on in this quiet little town? Hah! Buckle up, ‘cause tonight, we’re takin’ a ride down memory lane… but not the kind they print in those tourist brochures.
{Cue heavy metal track – “Buried Secrets” by Void Cross, fast and ominous with pounding drums.}
So, [[Watashuka]], our lovely little nowhere town—plenty of weird things have happened here, right? You’ve heard the whispers, the stories your parents won’t talk about. But there’s one incident that most of you’ve probably never even heard of, ‘cause it was scrubbed clean. Erased. Until now.
{Static crackles}
Ever heard of the Stratton Mill Fire? No? Yeah, they like it that way. It happened ten years ago, October 1973, and they’ve been keeping it under wraps ever since. That’s right, folks. Stratton Mill, one of the oldest buildings in town, went up in flames one chilly autumn night. But here’s the kicker… no one saw it burn. No one.
{Ominous guitar riff building in the background}
I know, I know, sounds like I’m making it up, right? A whole building burns down in the middle of town, and no one notices? But let me tell ya, there’s a reason for that. The fire wasn’t normal. It didn’t happen like you’re thinkin’. I dug deep, bro—old records, whispers from the few old-timers who still remember. And guess what? The fire was cold.
{Screeching feedback, then dead silence for a beat}
Yeah, you heard me. Cold fire. It burned, but the temperature dropped. People near the mill that night reported seeing blue flames and hearing this weird hum, like a vibration in the air. Some folks claim they saw shadowy figures walking into the fire like they were just taking a Sunday stroll. But here’s where it gets really freaky… there were no bodies. And when they found the building the next morning? Not even ash, man. Just… gone.
Now, here’s where it gets juicy. My sources tell me that the town’s finest, including our favorite boy in blue, [[Jan Ducochik|Sgt. Jan Ducochik]], have been diggin’ into this for years. What they’re not tellin’ you is that there were three people missing that night—three workers who were never found. But the mill owners? They just quietly shut the whole thing down, and any record of it? Poof! Erased like it never happened.
Now, why would they go to all that trouble, huh? What’s so special about a little old mill burning down? Well, here’s a theory for you. The Stratton Mill wasn’t just a place for grinding grain. It was a meeting place for some real shady characters—people who dabbled in things they shouldn’t have. Rituals, man. Dark ones. And those ‘figures’ walking into the cold fire? They weren’t running from it. They were walking into it to disappear.
{Cue another heavy track – “The Haunter” by Death Mask, with eerie vocals and fast, thrashing guitars.}
Now, the official story, if you dig deep enough, says that there was a 'minor structural collapse' at the mill and that it was abandoned afterward. No big deal, right? But you won’t find any real records from the town on it. No fire report, no insurance claims, nothing. Why? Because they’re scared, bro. Scared of what really happened that night. And scared of what might still be hiding underneath those ruins.
{Sound of papers shuffling and Dave laughing under his breath}
Here’s a little nugget for you truth-seekers out there… I got wind that our good sergeant has been poking around the mill site again. It’s all locked up now, fences and all, but something—or someone—has been stirring things up over there. And it ain’t just rats in the walls, bro. So if you’re feeling brave, why not take a little midnight stroll to the Stratton Mill ruins and see for yourself?
{Sound of Dave tapping on the microphone}
Just don’t be surprised if you feel a chill in the air that’s got nothin’ to do with the weather. And hey, if you start hearin’ that hum? Run, dude. Run fast. ‘Cause whatever’s still hiding at the Stratton Mill… it’s cold, and it’s hungry.
{Music picks up – “Veil of Shadows” by Spectral Abyss, heavy and atmospheric, filled with dread.}
Alright, metal militia, time for me to disappear into the night before THEY try to shut me down again. Keep your ears to the ground, your minds sharp, and your amps cranked. And remember… truth is colder than fiction.
{Outro guitar fades out into static}
Till next time, freaks. Stay metal, stay alive.
_Broadcast cuts out with a final screech of static as WCTU’s regular programming attempts to resume._

# Metal At Midnight: The Repairman Returns
_WCTU is interrupted by static and electrical interference._  
{Dave laughing with a mix of sarcasm and intensity}  
"Ohhhh yeah! You thought you were safe tonight, huh? Well, think again, ‘cause it’s _Metal at Midnight_, and you’ve tuned in just in time for a real mind-bender! This time, we're diving deep into a story that’s been bouncing around Caroline College for years—long before any of you freshmen got here. And it just got a whole lot stranger.
But first, let’s talk about this new writer on the scene—he’s just a sophomore, but the stuff he’s coming up with, man? I’m telling ya, it’s like he’s tapped into something none of us are seeing. Let’s just call him _The Kid_ for now. You’ve never heard of him, but I guarantee you’re gonna hear a lot more about him real soon. He’s been adding his own twists to one of Caroline’s… longest-running stories."
{Cue heavy metal track: “Outsider” by Black Crucible, low and slow with ominous riffs.}  
"Now, this ain’t just your regular creative writing assignment, bro. Nah, it’s something much darker. You see, since ‘69, students have been passing down pieces of this story—building on it like a twisted game of telephone. No one’s ever heard the whole thing, and no one ever will ‘cause it changes every time someone adds a piece. But what’s freakin’ me out is _The Kid_… his latest entry? It’s like he knows more than he should.
Before I get into his part, you need to hear about where it all started. And wouldn’t you know it, it came from a former _WCTU_ host. A real talent. A native of Illinois, not Wisconsin, mind you. _Melissa Young_—yep, you might remember her. She vanished a little over a year ago, but before that? She was one of the best on the mic. But way before that, when she was a freshman, Melissa wrote this story about a TV repairman from her hometown. But it wasn’t just some ‘random inspiration,’ no sir. Word is, the story was based on something _real_—something that happened out in her neck of the woods."
{Sound of static crackling, then fading.}  
"So here’s how it went: This repairman, just your average Joe, used his job to rob people blind. Got caught, thrown in the slammer. End of story, right? Not exactly. _Melissa’s_ tale ended with him behind bars, but you could tell she was building to something bigger.
And then… last year. _The Kid_ wrote the next part, totally unaware of what Melissa had written. But get this—he picked up the story like he’d heard it before. Only… he hadn’t. His version? Well, it takes place years after the first part. The repairman’s out, but he’s not robbing houses anymore. No. Now he’s in the TVs, man! Not fixing them, not repairing them—he’s _inside them_. And whatever comes through that screen? It’s not cartoons, bro. It’s something twisted. Commercials that drive people mad. Shows that scare them to death. The repairman? He’s found a way to kill without even leaving the living room."
{Pause, eerie silence.}  
"Now, let me tell you, that _right there_ would be enough to keep me awake at night. But there’s more. _The Kid_, he’s been writing some other strange stuff, too. Stories about weird static showing up on people’s TV screens, and people claiming they saw someone moving behind the broadcast signal—someone who shouldn’t be there. And he’s written about that old, run-down place we all know as _The Hut_. Yeah, that’s right, the electronics shop over on Main. Apparently, some of those old TV sets? They ain’t exactly ‘gently used,’ if you catch my drift.
Buzz Horton—oh, he’s a character, man—he’s been selling more than a few of those old sets with some strange… side effects. Customers returning them, saying the TVs flicker when they’re off, or that they hear voices in the static. But hey, I’m just here to keep the airwaves creepy, right? What do I know? Just remember, there’s more to this than an old repairman and some busted electronics. Sometimes… things find a way to crawl through the static."
{Another crackle of static and feedback.}  
"But before I sign off for tonight, let me leave you with this little nugget of truth. You see, _Melissa_ was doing her thing on _Mystery Hour_ the night she disappeared. And guess what her last story was about? Yeah, you got it—the _repairman_. But it wasn’t just a story, no. She saw something that night. Right here, in the station. And her last words weren’t part of the script. She said, ‘He’s here… inside.’ Then, poof! Gone. No trace. So, you tell me, metal militia, was it all just a story, or was she trying to warn us about something coming through the airwaves?"
{Cue ominous metal track: “Into the Abyss” by Death’s Pulse, slow and heavy.}  
"So keep your eyes open, especially if you’re watching late-night TV. And maybe, just maybe, don’t leave that old set on when you’re not in the room. Because you never know who—or what—might be watching back. Dave out!"
_Broadcast cuts out with static, leaving the airwaves dead silent before regular programming resumes._

**Band**: _Death’s Pulse_  
**Genre**: Doom Metal / Heavy Metal  
**Vibe**: Slow, heavy, and ominous, with haunting guitar riffs and growling vocals. The song evokes a sense of dread, as if descending into a dark, endless void. Its atmosphere is thick with tension, building up to crushing, distorted breakdowns.
---
### **Lyrics**:
_(Verse 1)_  
Shadows flicker on the screen,  
Through static cracks, a ghost unseen,  
Whispers crawl across the light,  
Twisting truth into the night.

Into the abyss, we fall,  
No return, no voice to call.  
Eyes of fire, black as sin,  
Pull us deeper, pull us in.
_(Verse 2)_  
From the wires, the demon feeds,  
On your fears, on twisted needs.  
Lost within a broken line,  
Trapped between the space and time.
_(Chorus)_  
Into the abyss, we fall,  
No escape, no light at all.  
Eyes of terror, cold as death,  
Steal the air, steal your breath.
_(Bridge)_  
Sinking, sinking—can't break free,  
Bound by chains you cannot see.  
The signal fades, the pulse grows thin,  
The void awaits—it's pulling in.
_(Final Chorus)_  
Into the abyss, we descend,  
No beginning, and no end.  
Eyes of darkness, void of sound,  
Nowhere left, we’re lost and drowned.
---
**Description**:  
_“Into the Abyss”_ is a doom-laden track that blends slow, thunderous guitar riffs with eerie, distorted melodies. The vocals alternate between a guttural growl and haunting whispers, evoking an overwhelming sense of being trapped in an endless void. The song's lyrics speak of being pulled into a nightmare realm, where reality twists and there's no escape. The chorus is heavy and relentless, echoing the sense of falling deeper into something inescapable. Ideal for fans of dark, atmospheric metal.
