---
title: Cold Flames at Stratton Mill
draft: true
publish: false
tags:
  - TTRPG
  - Horror
  - adventure
---
# Adventure: Cold Flames at Stratton Mill
## **Setting**:
[[Watashuka]], Wisconsin, Early October 1983
## **Synopsis**:
The investigators are drawn into an investigation of the **Stratton Mill Fire**, a cold case from 1973 involving a mysterious blaze that left no trace of bodies or normal fire damage. As they dig deeper into the abandoned mill’s history, they discover that the fire was the result of a dark ritual performed by [[Brotherhood of the Gate Unveiled]] . The ritual was meant to open a portal to another dimension, but something went wrong, leaving behind "cold fire" that still burns beneath the mill ruins, alongside spectral remnants of the failed ritual. The investigators must navigate the mill’s haunted grounds and uncover the truth before the Brotherhood attempts to complete what was left unfinished.
---
## **Keeper Information**:
The **Brotherhood of the Gate Unveiled** used the Stratton Mill as a site for their rituals, aiming to tear the veil between dimensions and bring forth eldritch knowledge and power. On the night of the fire, three cultists led a ritual to open the gate, but the energy they summoned spiraled out of control, consuming the mill in a fire that burned cold—something not of this world. The fire was not natural, and its source still lingers beneath the ruins, along with the restless spirits of the three cultists who perished. The Brotherhood has sent new members to try and finish what was started, using the "cold flame" as a gateway.
---
## **Adventure Hooks**:
- **A Cry for Help**:  
     [[Jan Ducochik|Sgt. Jan Ducochik]] has been investigating the fire in secret, and after uncovering a clue that points to a possible Brotherhood connection, he reaches out to the investigators for help. He’s too close to the case and fears that any more direct involvement will draw unwanted attention. The investigators must pick up where Ducochik left off.
- **Strange Activity at the Ruins**:  
    Locals report strange lights and eerie humming noises coming from the abandoned Stratton Mill. Some even claim to have seen shadowy figures moving around the site at night. The investigators are hired (by a town council member, a local journalist, or a business owner) to investigate whether trespassers or something more sinister is at play.
- **Unsettling Dreams**:  
    One or more of the investigators begin to have disturbing dreams of walking through blue flames, hearing whispers, and seeing shadowy figures beckoning them toward the ruins of the mill. The dreams are accompanied by a growing sense of dread that compels the investigators to visit the site.
---
## **Locations**:
- **Stratton Mill Ruins**:  
    The abandoned mill is a dilapidated structure, overgrown with weeds and vines, surrounded by a rusted chain-link fence. The area is eerily quiet, and the temperature around the ruins is unnaturally cold, even during the day. At night, strange blue flames can occasionally be seen flickering beneath the surface, and an otherworldly hum fills the air.
    - **Key Features**:
        - **The Mill Basement**: Beneath the ruins, the remnants of the ritual chamber still exist. Charred symbols line the floor, and the faint blue flames emanate from cracks in the foundation. The portal the cult attempted to open is unstable, leaking energy into the material world.
        - **The Cold Fire**: The "cold fire" is supernatural in origin and does not behave like a normal flame. It emits no heat and instead seems to drain warmth from the area. It can cause **Sanity Loss** for those who stare into it for too long.
        - **The Spectral Cultists**: The ghosts of the three cultists who perished in the failed ritual haunt the mill. They are trapped, reliving the moments before their deaths, unable to move on until the gate is either opened or closed forever.
- **[[Watashuka]] Town Records Office**:  
    Buried deep within the town’s old records are documents about the mill, including inspection reports, property deeds, and an old police report from the night of the fire. However, some of the documents are missing or have been tampered with, hinting at a cover-up.
    - **Key Clues**:
        - A copy of a report from a local police officer who responded to the fire. The report mentions seeing "strange figures" near the mill just before the fire, but the officer’s statement was dismissed as nonsense.
        - An old photo of the mill taken the day after the fire, showing the absence of ash or debris where the fire supposedly occurred.
- **The Brotherhood’s Safehouse**:  
    Unbeknownst to the investigators, the Brotherhood has a safehouse near the mill where they’ve been planning to finish the ritual. The building is an inconspicuous, run-down shack on the outskirts of town, but inside, the walls are covered in occult symbols and diagrams related to the portal. One of the Brotherhood members may be watching the investigators, keeping an eye on their progress.
---
## **Important NPCs**:
- **Sergeant Jan Ducochik**
    - **Role**: The investigator’s contact in town. Ducochik has been investigating the mill fire for years but has kept it quiet to avoid drawing attention. He has suspicions about the Brotherhood’s involvement but doesn’t have enough proof to act. He enlists the investigators’ help to uncover the truth and stop whatever is happening at the mill.
    - **Personality**: Serious, methodical, with a deep sense of duty to protect the town. While he doesn't fully believe in the supernatural, he’s seen enough strange things to know something is wrong.
- **The Spectral Cultists**
    - **Role**: Ghostly remnants of the Brotherhood members who died during the ritual. They are bound to the mill and attempt to lure the investigators into completing the ritual or destroying the gate for good.
    - **Appearance**: They appear as shadowy, indistinct figures, their faces contorted in terror, moving as if they’re still trying to complete the ritual. Their presence can cause **Sanity Loss**.
- **Brotherhood Operatives**
    - **Role**: The new members of the Brotherhood, sent to finish what was started. They are aware of the investigators’ interest in the mill and may try to stop them or manipulate them into completing the ritual on their behalf.
    - **Personality**: Cold, calculating, and ruthless. They are fanatically devoted to the Brotherhood’s goals, believing that opening the gate will bring them immense power.
---
## **Encounters**:
- **The Cold Fire**:  
    Investigators will have to deal with the cold fire that still burns beneath the mill. If they attempt to approach or interact with it, they will experience strange phenomena, such as the air around them freezing, voices whispering in their ears, and flashes of the night of the fire. The fire can only be extinguished by severing its connection to the portal, which will require an occult ritual of their own.
    - **Sanity Loss**: Looking directly into the cold fire for more than a few moments causes 1d4 **Sanity Loss**. Being touched by the fire causes 1d6 **Sanity Loss** and 1d4 physical damage, though the fire leaves no visible wounds.
- **Spectral Manifestations**:  
    The ghosts of the three cultists will attempt to manipulate the investigators into completing the ritual by guiding them deeper into the mill. The investigators may see the cultists’ final moments play out before them, or hear them chanting in the shadows. At times, the ghosts may turn hostile if they feel the investigators are trying to stop the ritual.
    - **Combat Option**: While the ghosts cannot be fought physically, they can be banished by breaking the ritual’s connection to the cold fire.
- **The Brotherhood’s Interference**:  
    Once the investigators are close to uncovering the truth, the new members of the Brotherhood will take action. They may attempt to sabotage the investigators' efforts, lure them into a trap, or even trick them into completing the ritual by pretending to be allies. If the investigators discover the Brotherhood’s safehouse, they can find critical clues about how to close the gate.
---
## **Climax**:
The final showdown takes place in the **Mill Basement**, where the cold fire burns the brightest, and the portal to another dimension flickers just out of view. The investigators must decide whether to close the portal once and for all, banishing the cold fire and the cultists’ spirits, or allow the Brotherhood to complete the ritual, risking the unleashing of eldritch horrors.
- **Closing the Portal**: The investigators will need to use **Occult Knowledge** and gather materials from the Brotherhood’s safehouse to sever the connection between the cold fire and the portal. This requires a successful **Occult** roll and possibly the destruction of the mill ruins to prevent the Brotherhood from ever attempting the ritual again.
- **Failing to Stop the Ritual**: If the Brotherhood succeeds in completing the ritual, the portal will open fully, allowing a powerful, otherworldly entity to cross into this dimension. The investigators will need to flee as the entity begins warping reality around them, or face it in a desperate struggle for survival.
---
## **Aftermath**:
- **Success**: If the investigators close the portal and extinguish the cold fire, the spirits of the cultists will be freed, and the mill will be at peace. Sergeant Ducochik will be grateful for their help, though the town may never know the full truth. However, the Brotherhood may still be watching, waiting for another opportunity.
- **Failure**: If the investigators fail to stop the ritual, the portal will remain open, and strange phenomena will begin to plague Watashuka. The Brotherhood will have gained power, and the town’s supernatural troubles will escalate.
---
## **Rewards**:
- **Sanity Gain**: Closing the portal and laying the cultists to rest grants 1d6 **Sanity**.
- **Experience**: Investigators will gain experience for uncovering the truth about the mill fire, outsmarting the Brotherhood, and banishing the cold fire.

---

---
title: Inside The Screen
draft: true
publish: false
tags:
  - TTRPG
  - Horror
  - adventure
---
# Adventure: Inside The Screen
**Setting**: [[Watashuka]], Fall 1983  
**Trigger Event**: During a late-night _Metal at Midnight_ show, hosted by the mysterious [[Dave]], the characters hear a cryptic reading of passages from a sophomore's story. The story is eerie, detailing a TV repairman who haunts his former customers by becoming part of their television broadcasts. [[[[Dave]] suggests the author, whom he refers to only as "The Kid," knows more than he’s letting on, hinting at a deeper truth behind the fictional tale.
---
### **The Hook**
The characters tune into _Metal at Midnight_, a popular local radio show known for its bizarre mix of metal music and dark, cryptic commentary. During the broadcast, Dave reads from an anonymous writer’s work, a sophomore at Caroline College. The chilling story about a TV repairman who infiltrates people’s screens resonates with the players. Dave finishes the segment with an ominous message:
_"The Kid, he's no ordinary writer, folks. He's seen things... things he can’t explain, things I’ve tried to ignore. Maybe some of you know him, but I’m not naming names. Just know that his stories, they come from somewhere real. And if you’re unlucky, maybe you’ll see for yourself."_
The players can’t shake the feeling that the story is connected to something happening in Watashuka.
See [[The Repairman Returns]]
---
### **Investigation Begins**
The players begin their investigation by following the clues from Dave’s broadcast. They can pursue the following leads:
1. **Dave’s Show**: If the players contact WCTU to ask about Dave, they’re stonewalled—no one at the station seems to know who Dave is. His show _Metal at Midnight_ is listed, but it’s treated as a joke among the station staff. However, they mention Melissa Young, a former host of _Mystery Hour_, who disappeared after reading a story that sounds eerily similar to Dave’s broadcast.
2. **Alan Sanders**: Through investigation, the players can connect "The Kid" to Alan Sanders, a shy and creative sophomore at Caroline College. When approached, Alan is evasive, claiming that his story was just a dream. However, he becomes visibly anxious when asked how he came up with the TV repairman character, deflecting further questions.
3. **The Hut (Electronics and Appliance Store)**: If the players dig into the theme of the TV repairman, they’ll discover that Watashuka’s local electronics store, _The Hut_, owned by Jerry “Buzz” Horton, has recently been selling strange, outdated television sets. These TVs have been returned by customers complaining of strange interference and distorted broadcasts. Buzz is a friendly but chaotic man who brushes off the complaints, calling them "technical glitches."
---
### **The Truth Behind the Story**
Alan Sanders has been unknowingly tapping into a dark, occult force linked to _The Hut_. Buzz Horton has been collecting old television sets from strange sources, many of which are imbued with a malevolent presence. One particular set was once owned by a former Caroline College student from the late 1960s, and it was used in a ritual by a local cult seeking to manipulate broadcasts. The ritual failed, but it left the TV cursed—able to channel eldritch energies and connect to the _Outer God Nyarlathotep_ through broadcast signals.
Alan’s story wasn’t just a creative work—it was a reflection of the entity lurking inside these old TV sets. When he wrote his "fictional" story, he was unconsciously drawing from the real, lurking presence in Watashuka's electrical systems. Melissa Young’s disappearance was tied to this, as she encountered the entity during her final broadcast. Now, the entity has started to stir again, using television broadcasts to influence and manipulate people through fear.
---
### **Key Locations and Encounters**
1. **The Hut**:
    - Players can visit _The Hut_ and question Buzz Horton. They notice a variety of old, retro TV sets gathering dust in the back. Buzz is reluctant to talk about the returns but eventually admits that some customers have returned sets, claiming they see strange figures or hear whispers when the TVs are on, even when unplugged.
    - Upon inspecting one of the returned TVs, the players experience static interference and brief, disturbing images of a shadowy figure twisting in and out of various TV programs, much like the repairman from Alan’s story.
2. **Alan’s Dorm Room**:
    - If the players confront Alan again, he admits that ever since writing the story, he’s been having nightmares and seeing static-filled TV screens in his dreams. He doesn’t know how his story connected to Melissa’s, but something about the radio station feels wrong. He mentions hearing strange noises the last time he visited WCTU to drop off a new script.
3. **WCTU Station**:
    - When the players investigate WCTU, they can find old tapes from Melissa’s broadcasts. Replaying her final show, they’ll hear her voice growing frantic toward the end before her chilling final words: _"He’s here... inside..."_
    - While at the station, the players may experience unexplained static on the monitors, flickering lights, and brief, unnerving glimpses of a shadowy figure on an old TV set in the corner of the room.
---
### **Climactic Encounter**
The final confrontation occurs at _The Hut_ after hours. The players learn that one of the returned TVs is still "active" and must be destroyed before the entity fully manifests. Buzz mentions that this particular TV came from a customer near Lakeview Shores who disappeared under strange circumstances. When they attempt to destroy the TV, it begins broadcasting disturbing images of themselves—warped and twisted versions of their own lives.
As they try to stop the TV, the entity that Melissa saw and Alan wrote about finally manifests through the screen. The shadowy figure—an echo of the TV repairman—attempts to pull the players into a nightmare world inside the television broadcast. The players must use their wits and knowledge of the occult to sever the connection between the cursed TVs and the eldritch presence before they too become part of the programming.
---
### **Aftermath and Potential Hooks**
- **Alan Sanders’ Fate**: If the players succeed, Alan is freed from the nightmare influence of his story. He may remain in Watashuka, grateful but haunted by what he inadvertently unleashed. If they fail, Alan could fall deeper into the occult mystery, either as an ally or a pawn for future adventures.
- **The Hut**: Buzz Horton may continue to unknowingly stock cursed electronics, or he may become a key source of occult information for the players, as the cursed TVs are revealed to be part of a larger, more sinister conspiracy tied to the town’s electronics infrastructure.
- **WCTU’s Dark Secrets**: The players may choose to investigate more about WCTU, especially as rumors of Melissa’s disappearance and the cursed broadcasts grow. Could the station itself be a focal point for occult manipulation, or is something even darker lurking in the static between shows?
## Details
### Melissa's Story: "The TV Repairman"
**Summary**:  
Melissa's original story, written during her freshman year, was about a seemingly ordinary TV repairman who used his job to scope out homes for theft. After robbing one of his customers, he was eventually caught and sent to prison. The story ended with his arrest and the reassurance that justice had been served, with no supernatural or eerie elements. It was a straightforward crime tale, with the focus on the repairman’s moral downfall and his comeuppance.
---
### The New Story: "Inside the Screen"
**Summary**:  
The new story, written by a sophomore named **Alan Sanders**, picks up years after the events of Melissa’s original work. The TV repairman, now out of prison, seeks revenge on his former customers. However, the repairman doesn’t physically return to their homes—instead, he becomes part of the TV programming. His presence warps the content, turning commercials and shows into horrific parodies. One by one, his victims experience disturbing, nightmarish visions on their screens. At first, they believe it's part of the broadcast, but the terror escalates until the repairman finally learns how to scare them to death, feeding off their fear.
---
### Author of the New Story: Alan Sanders
Alan Sanders, a quiet and creative sophomore at Caroline College, has a talent for writing eerie and unsettling stories. He frequently contributes to "Mystery Hour" and had no knowledge of Melissa's earlier work. Despite this, his story was an uncanny continuation of her original TV repairman tale. Alan claimed the idea came to him in a dream, but the perfect alignment with Melissa's work was too strange to be a coincidence. His writing style blends dark humor with psychological horror, making him a favorite among listeners of the program.
---
### Melissa's Last Words on Air
After reading Alan’s story during her final broadcast, Melissa closed with these unsettling words:
_"You think the repairman’s gone, but he never really left, did he? He’s still out there, crawling into places he shouldn’t be. It’s not always a TV—it could be anything, really. The walls... the wires... even right here, inside the station. He’s watching... waiting..."_
At first, the audience believed Melissa was merely adding her own spooky twist to the story. But her tone shifted, the fear in her voice palpable as she whispered her final words:
_"Oh God, he's... he's here. He’s inside..."_
Then the transmission cut off, leaving dead air. The listeners assumed it was a technical glitch, but Melissa was never seen again.
---
### What Did Melissa See?
In her final moments, Melissa noticed something strange with the station’s equipment. The static on the monitors, the flickering of lights, and an eerie distortion in the soundboard made her realize that something—or someone—was manipulating the broadcast from within the station. As she pieced it together, she glanced at one of the old, unused TV sets in the station’s storage room. There, distorted on the flickering screen, was the faint, shadowy figure of a man—the TV repairman, watching her through the glass.
That’s when she knew she wasn’t alone.

---
title: The Dissection Ritual
draft: true
publish: false
tags:
  - TTRPG
  - Horror

---
# Adventure: The Dissection Ritual
## Overview
The players are introduced to a mysterious ritual disguised as a mundane lab exercise. [[Church of the Delayed Blossom]] is trying to complete a summoning ritual under the guise of a biology class at Caroline College. The disappearance of [[Amy Mann]], an undercover government agent posing as a valley girl student, serves as a red herring, distracting the players from the true threat: the cult's ongoing ritual. The adventure spans a week, with moments of investigation, spooky phenomena, and a final confrontation.
---
## Scene 1: The First Night - The Interrupted Ritual
- **When**: August 29<sup>th</sup>, 1983
- **Location**: [[Caroline College]], Biology Lab (Night)
- **Important Characters**:
  - **Substitute (cultist of [[Shub-Niggurath]])**: Leading the ritual disguised as a mundane lab exercise.
  - **Students (including [[Amy Mann]])**: Distracted and unaware of what’s happening.
- **Purpose**: Introduce the ritual and hint at something supernatural, but interrupt it before it fully manifests.
- **Threat/Puzzle**: Players unknowingly arrange lab tools in a sigil. Eerie events follow: flickering lights, whispers, and a sudden, chilling wind. Everyone panics and flees the lab.
- **Spooky Interruption**: A minor supernatural manifestation—spectral figure, cold gusts, and doors slamming—forces the evacuation of the lab.
- **Clue**: A torn piece of paper with sigil symbols is left behind.
---
## Scene 2: Day 2 - The Disappearance of Amy Mann
- **Location**: Campus (Lab, Dorms, Library, etc.)
- **Important Characters**:
  - **Amy Mann**: Disappears the morning after the lab.
  - **Fellow Students**: Worried about Amy’s disappearance.
  - **Campus Police and Government Agents (undercover)**: Involved in the investigation, with agents pretending to be ordinary police.
- **Purpose**: Shift focus to Amy’s disappearance, introducing a red herring and giving the players reason to investigate.
- **Threat/Puzzle**: Amy doesn’t show up for class. Players may join the search for her, encountering undercover agents trying to keep them away from the truth.
- **Clue**: A **journal in Amy’s dorm room** reveals cryptic notes, surveillance logs, and advanced science research.
---
## Scene 3: Day 3 - The Search Intensifies
- **Location**: Across Watashuka (Library, Amy’s Dorm, local park)
- **Important Characters**:
  - **Amy’s Friends/Acquaintances**: Offering misleading or vague information.
  - **Government Agents**: Disguised as helpful police, subtly steering players away from sensitive areas.
- **Purpose**: Deepen the mystery with red herrings and mislead the players into thinking Amy’s disappearance had an Earthly cause.
- **Threat/Puzzle**: Players may find **shoe prints leading to a wooded area** or **Amy’s notebook in the library**. Red herrings include sightings of suspicious men or Amy’s scarf at the lake.
- **Subtle Clue**: A missing **student ID** and a forged one hint at Amy’s true identity.
---
## Scene 4: Day 4-5 - Unsettling Discoveries
- **Location**: Biology Lab, Amy’s Dorm, Campus Library
- **Important Characters**:
  - **Substitute (cultist)**: More agitated, as they must complete the ritual before the week ends.
  - **Students/Investigators**: Still searching for Amy.
- **Purpose**: Build tension as players investigate, noticing that the ritual may still be ongoing.
- **Threat/Puzzle**: The lab shows **residual effects of the ritual**—symbols burned into tables, strange shadows, and odd sensations. Subtle red herrings lead players away from the ritual.
- **Subtle Clue**: The substitute wears **occult symbols** as jewelry, hinting at their involvement.
---
## Scene 5: Day 6-7 - The Ritual Resumes
- **Location**: Biology Lab (Night)
- **Important Characters**:
  - **Substitute (cultist)**: Desperately trying to complete the ritual.
  - **Other Students**: Still distracted by Amy’s disappearance.
- **Purpose**: Final confrontation where the players can stop or fail to stop the ritual.
- **Threat/Puzzle**: The substitute resumes the ritual, with phenomena such as **levitating objects, flickering lights, and unnatural cold**. Players must decide to confront the substitute or disrupt the sigil.
- **Subtle Clue**: Amy’s **journal** hints at the cult’s activities, adding more layers to the mystery of her disappearance.
- **Climax**: Players confront the substitute and try to stop the ritual before the entity fully manifests.
---
## Possible Outcomes
### 1. The Cult Succeeds in Completing the Ritual
- **Effect**: A **lesser entity of Shub-Niggurath** manifests briefly, warping reality and causing mental or physical damage to the players.
- **Consequences**:
  - **Physical Damage**: Players may suffer scars or mysterious injuries.
  - **Mental Trauma**: Permanent Sanity loss and mental disorders (phobias, paranoia, hallucinations).
  - **New Motivation**: The players are driven to stop the cult from summoning something worse.
- **Hook for Future Adventures**: Lingering effects—odd phenomena, people acting strangely, warped objects—hint that the entity’s influence remains.
### 2. The Players Stop the Ritual
- **Effect**: The ritual is disrupted before it fully manifests, but reality warps temporarily, causing hallucinations and Sanity loss.
- **Consequences**:
  - **Physical Evidence**: Ritual scars and residual energy in the environment.
  - **Mental Consequences**: Players suffer from flashbacks or irrational fears related to the event.
  - **New Motivation**: The players realize they’ve only delayed the cult, motivating them to investigate further.
- **Hook for Future Adventures**: Clues about the cult’s broader network and future plans emerge.
---
# Follow-Up Adventures
### 1. The Vanishing Farm
- **Premise**: A local Amish farm is mysteriously abandoned, with all inhabitants missing and livestock mutilated.
- **Connection**: The symbols found on the farm match the sigils from the biology lab ritual.
- **New Motivation**: The players investigate the Amish’s secret role in protecting the town from supernatural forces.
---
### 2. The Haunting of Caroline College
- **Premise**: After the biology lab incident, students report hauntings and eerie phenomena on campus.
- **Connection**: Residual energy from the failed or successful ritual causes hauntings, leading to ghostly manifestations of past cultists.
- **New Motivation**: Players must banish lingering spirits and uncover the cult’s ties to the college.
---
### 3. The Forgotten Burial Grounds
- **Premise**: Sacred Ho-Chunk burial grounds are disturbed, angering spirits and causing animals to act violently.
- **Connection**: The cult is using the burial grounds for another ritual. The players discover ancient ties between the cult and the Ho-Chunk tribe.
- **New Motivation**: Players work with the Ho-Chunk tribe to stop the cult from raising something from the burial grounds.
---
### 4. The Disappearing Agents
- **Premise**: Law enforcement and government officials investigating Project Caroline disappear one by one.
- **Connection**: The players realize that Project Caroline’s own agents are being targeted by either the cult or internal factions.
- **New Motivation**: The players investigate the agents’ disappearances and uncover hidden files about Project Caroline’s secret projects.
---
### 5. The Returning Entity
- **Premise**: Strange weather patterns and eerie phenomena suggest that something summoned by the ritual is trying to return.
- **Connection**: The entity from the biology lab ritual is slowly breaking through into reality, causing odd occurrences and sightings of a mysterious figure.
- **New Motivation**: The players must find a way to seal the breach between dimensions and prevent the entity from fully manifesting.
---
# Conclusion
This adventure sets the stage for a broader investigation into the cult of Shub-Niggurath and the hidden activities of Project Caroline. The players’ choices in this first adventure will shape the direction of the campaign, whether they are driven by their encounter with the supernatural or the mystery of Amy Mann’s disappearance. The follow-up adventures provide a variety of ways to expand the world, introducing new dangers and deeper connections to the mythos of Watashuka.
# Amy Mann "Valley Girl" Dialogue Suggestions
## 1. Loudly Bragging About Non-Existent Parties
- “Oh my God, you guys, like, last weekend? I was *so* wasted, I, like, didn’t even know where I was! It was, like, totally insane. We, like, drank sooo much Bartles & Jaymes. Have you ever had Bartles & Jaymes? It’s, like, so fancy.”
- “Yeah, so, I met this guy—he’s *so* cute—and, like, we went to this totally secret rave. He said he’s, like, in *pre-law*? Ugh, *so* hot. But I totally don’t even, like, remember his name.”
## 2. Talking About Academic Topics in a Weird, Inappropriate Way (Slipping Up)
- “Like, have you guys ever wondered, like, if you could, like, totally stop time? I mean, think about it, like, if you accelerated, like, particles to near-light speed, you’d totally experience time dilation. Like, *so* crazy, right?”
- “OMG, *bodies* are, like, *so* fascinating, you know? Like, all those little mitochondria doing their thing, generating ATP, like, it’s just so cute. It’s like they’re partying in your cells! *Totally radical!*”
- “You ever think, like, the universe could be, like, a simulation? ‘Cause, like, quantum fluctuations? Totally feels like it, right? *Whatever.*”
## 3. Overcompensating to Fit In
- “So, like, when are we gonna get to the part of the class where we get to cut stuff open? Like, *ew*, but also, like, *sooo* cool, you know?”
- “I’m totally not into, like, math or science or whatever, but, like, my dad said I had to take this class. He’s, like, a *really* smart guy, though, so I guess he’s right. *Whatevs*, I’ll figure it out.”
- “Ugh, dissecting things is, like, sooo grody, but also kinda hot, you know? Like, I’m totally not into it, but, like, I could get used to it.”
## 4. Loud and Inappropriate Comments
- “Like, I *totally* blacked out the other night. We were playing, like, *beer pong*, and I think I, like, invented a new math formula or something? *Hah*, that’d be, like, *so* funny, right?”
- “Oh my God, is this where we, like, cut open frogs or whatever? I heard my friend in *bio* say they squirt when you poke ‘em. *Gag me*, right?”
- “This guy, like, came up to me and was all, like, *serious*? He was, like, ‘You should *study* more,’ and I’m like, *whatever*, dude, like, I don’t have time for that, you know? I’m here to, like, have fun!”
## 5. Accidentally Too Smart
- “So, like, when the mitochondria produce ATP during oxidative phosphorylation, it’s, like, sooo efficient, right? I mean, it’s kinda boring, but also, like, fascinating in a molecular biology sense, you know?”
- “Yeah, well, when I was, like, totally wasted the other night, I started thinking about how **Heisenberg's uncertainty principle** basically implies we can never know the true state of a particle’s velocity *and* position at the same time. Ugh, like, what a *buzzkill*, right?”
- "Wait, don’t you guys know that the Pythagorean theorem only works in Euclidean geometry? Like, duh! But, whatever, right?”

[[Ho-Chunk]] name for [[Yog-Sothoth]], [[Shub-Niggurath]] and other eldritch entities

---
title: Nyarlathotep
draft: true
publish: false
tags:
  - TTRPG
  - Horror
---
**Role in the Setting:**  
Nyarlathotep, the "Crawling Chaos," is a malevolent cosmic entity known for taking many forms and directly interacting with mortals. Unlike [[Shub-Niggurath]] and [[Yog-Sothoth]], who rarely interact directly, Nyarlathotep delights in manipulating humans, sowing discord and chaos. He has been pulling the strings in Watashuka since its founding, subtly influencing both the original occultists who established **Prairieville Academy** and the ongoing activities of the cults.
Nyarlathotep is the true force behind much of the supernatural activity in the region. He enjoys playing the cults against each other, allowing them to believe they are following separate paths to summon the "original god," when in reality, they are all serving his greater agenda. His ultimate goal is chaos, destruction, and the collapse of human society through their own hubris.
**Manipulating the Cults:**  
Nyarlathotep has been guiding both the **[[Brotherhood of the Gate Unveiled]]** and the **[[Church of the Delayed Blossom]]**, ensuring that their rituals continue while keeping them in conflict. He takes on various forms to influence key figures in [[Watashuka]], sometimes posing as government agents or college officials to steer events in his favor.
- **Divide and Conquer:** Nyarlathotep fosters conflict between the cults, ensuring they remain distracted by their rivalry rather than focusing on the true nature of their "god."
- **Direct Manipulation:** Nyarlathotep occasionally appears to cult leaders in visions or dreams, providing them with just enough knowledge to keep their rituals progressing while hiding the full consequences of their actions.
**Ultimate Goal:**  
Nyarlathotep’s endgame is to unleash Cthulhu and other Great Old Ones by ensuring that the cults’ final ritual in 1987 succeeds—though not in the way they expect. He knows that summoning these beings will lead to mass destruction, and he relishes the chaos that will ensue. Unlike the other entities, Nyarlathotep has no desire for a structured outcome—he simply wants to watch the world burn.

---

---
title: Shub-Niggurath
draft: true
publish: false
tags:
  - TTRPG
  - Horror
---
**Role in the Setting:**  
Shub-Niggurath, known as the "Black Goat of the Woods with a Thousand Young," is a cosmic entity associated with fertility, nature, and monstrous offspring. In [[Watashuka]], Shub-Niggurath's influence is primarily felt through the **[[Church of the Delayed Blossom]]**, which arose from the failed occult attempts at **Prairieville Academy** in the mid-19th century. The cult believes that by manipulating the ley lines' natural energy and performing rituals involving human fertility, they can summon Shub-Niggurath to bless the world with her "young"—mutant creatures that will reshape reality.
The cult’s rituals often involve pregnant women, tapping into the natural forces of growth and transformation. They believe that human fertility, when augmented by ley line power, can give birth to something greater—monstrous offspring capable of bending nature and reality to the cult's will. These rituals have intensified since the 1980s, with the cult using the local teaching hospital as a cover for their experiments, often targeting vulnerable women or those in desperate need of care.
**Goals and Influence:**  
Shub-Niggurath’s primary goal is to spread her influence across the world through her offspring, creating grotesque new forms of life that defy the natural order. The **Church of the Delayed Blossom** believes they are nurturing these creatures to prepare for a time when Shub-Niggurath will emerge fully, reshaping Watashuka and, eventually, the world.
- **Corrupting Nature:** Through Shub-Niggurath's influence, nature itself begins to turn hostile. Infected animals, monstrous flora, and increasingly unpredictable weather patterns all signal her growing presence.
- **Pregnant Women as Vessels:** The cult uses rituals that involve pregnant women to create hybrid creatures. Their goal is to birth powerful beings that will carry out Shub-Niggurath’s will.
**Key Locations:**
- **Luttermoser Science Hall**: Some of the cult’s experiments are conducted here, masked as medical research.
- Sister Sarah's Teaching Hospital:
- Gale Veterinarian School:
**Connection to Other Entities:**  
Shub-Niggurath’s influence over nature contrasts with the temporal and dimensional control sought by **[[Yog-Sothoth]]**. While the cults of the two entities sometimes clash, they also occasionally collaborate when their goals align, particularly when it comes to opening gateways that benefit both their agendas. The **Brotherhood of the Gate Unveiled** occasionally aids the Church of the Delayed Blossom in finding ley line nodes, but both believe their paths are the true route to summoning the "original god."

---

---
title: Yog-Sothoth
draft: true
publish: false
tags:
  - TTRPG
  - Horror
---
**Role in the Setting:**  
Yog-Sothoth is the "Lurker at the Threshold," a being of unfathomable knowledge who exists outside of time and space. Yog-Sothoth’s influence in [[Watashuka]] is channeled through the **[[Brotherhood of the Gate Unveiled]]**, which emerged after the destruction of **Prairieville Academy**. The Brotherhood believes that by controlling time and opening dimensional gates, they can commune directly with Yog-Sothoth and ultimately summon him into the material world. They view him as a key to unlocking the mysteries of existence and gaining ultimate power.
The cult, especially active during the 1980s, conducts experiments with ley lines, seeking to manipulate time and open dimensional rifts. These experiments have resulted in dangerous phenomena, such as time loops and pockets of altered reality around Caroline College. **[[Project Caroline]]**, rebooted in secret by the government, unknowingly collaborates with Yog-Sothoth’s cult by conducting similar experiments on time manipulation.
**Goals and Influence:**  
Yog-Sothoth's followers seek to break the barriers between dimensions, allowing their god to enter the material world. They believe that control over time will grant them the ability to transcend mortality and reshape the world to their vision.
- **Time Loops and Dimensional Gates:** The Brotherhood’s rituals are focused on bending time and opening gateways to other realities. They hope to control these gates to bring Yog-Sothoth into this dimension.
- **The Time Loop:** A side effect of their rituals is the accidental creation of a **time loop** from 1983 to 1987, trapping many individuals, including **Dr. Amy Mann**, within a repeating cycle of events. The cult views this loop as a necessary phase of their greater plan, believing that mastery over the loop will give them control over time itself.
**Key Locations:**
- **Qubit Tower at Caroline College:** The supercomputers in this building play a key role in the cult’s manipulation of time, serving as a hub for their experiments.
- **Castelaz Building (Physical Sciences):** The Brotherhood conducts its dimensional experiments here under the guise of scientific research.
**Connection to Other Entities:**  
Yog-Sothoth is often in opposition to **[[Shub-Niggurath]]**, as the nature-focused rituals of the **[[Church of the Delayed Blossom]]** interfere with the temporal and dimensional work of the **Brotherhood of the Gate Unveiled**. However, both cults occasionally collaborate, particularly when it comes to rituals involving ley lines, though they believe they are summoning different aspects of the "original god."

---
